								<div id="contentSub"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">  (Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt_am_Main&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankfurt am Main">Frankfurt am Main</a>)</span></div>

For the town in Brandenburg, see <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_(Oder)" title="Frankfurt (Oder)">Frankfurt (Oder)</a>. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Frankfurt (disambiguation)">Frankfurt (disambiguation)</a>.</div>

<p><b>Frankfurt</b>, officially <b>Frankfurt am Main</b> (Literally "Frankfurt on the Main", <small>German pronunciation:</small> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Standard_German" title="Help:IPA/Standard German">[ˈfʁaŋkfʊɐ̯t am ˈmaɪ̯n]</a></span><small class="nowrap metadata">&#160;(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:De-Frankfurt_am_Main-pronunciation.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/25/De-Frankfurt_am_Main.ogg" class="internal" title="De-Frankfurt am Main.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small>), is a <a href="/wiki/Metropolis" title="Metropolis">metropolis</a> and the largest city in the <a href="/wiki/States_of_Germany" title="States of Germany">German state</a> of <a href="/wiki/Hesse" title="Hesse">Hesse</a> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Germany_by_population" title="List of cities in Germany by population">fifth-largest city</a> in Germany, with a 2015 population of 732,688 within its administrative boundaries,<sup id="cite_ref-Statistik-Hessen.de_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Statistik-Hessen.de-4">[4]</a></sup> and 2.3&#160;million in its <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Rhein-Main_Regional_Authority" title="Frankfurt Rhein-Main Regional Authority">urban area</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-region-frankfurt.de_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-region-frankfurt.de-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-staedtestatistik.de_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-staedtestatistik.de-5">[5]</a></sup> The city is at the centre of the larger <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Rhine-Main" title="Frankfurt Rhine-Main">Frankfurt Rhine-Main Metropolitan Region</a>, which has a population of 5.5&#160;million<sup id="cite_ref-metro_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-metro-1">[1]</a></sup> and is <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_regions_in_Germany" title="Metropolitan regions in Germany">Germany's second-largest metropolitan region</a> after <a href="/wiki/Rhine-Ruhr" title="Rhine-Ruhr">Rhine-Ruhr</a>. Since the <a href="/wiki/Enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="Enlargement of the European Union">enlargement of the European Union in 2013</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Geographical_midpoint_of_Europe#Geographic_centre_of_the_European_Union" title="Geographical midpoint of Europe">geographic centre of the EU</a> is about 40&#160;km (25&#160;mi) to the east of Frankfurt's CBD, the <a href="/wiki/Bankenviertel" title="Bankenviertel">Bankenviertel</a>. Frankfurt is culturally and ethnically diverse, with around half of the population, and a majority of young people, having a <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Germany" title="Immigration to Germany">migration background</a>. A quarter of the population are foreign nationals, including many <a href="/wiki/Expatriate" title="Expatriate">expatriates</a>.</p>
<p>Frankfurt is an <a href="/wiki/Global_city#GaWC_study" title="Global city">alpha world city</a> and a global hub for commerce, culture, education, tourism and transportation. It's the site of many global and European corporate headquarters. <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Airport" title="Frankfurt Airport">Frankfurt Airport</a> is among the world's busiest. Frankfurt is the major <a href="/wiki/Financial_centre" title="Financial centre">financial centre</a> of the European continent, with the HQs of the <a href="/wiki/European_Central_Bank" title="European Central Bank">European Central Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bundesbank" title="Deutsche Bundesbank">German Federal Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Stock_Exchange" title="Frankfurt Stock Exchange">Frankfurt Stock Exchange</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bank" title="Deutsche Bank">Deutsche Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/Commerzbank" title="Commerzbank">Commerzbank</a>, <a href="/wiki/DZ_Bank" title="DZ Bank">DZ Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/KfW" title="KfW">KfW</a>, several <a href="/wiki/Cloud_computing" title="Cloud computing">cloud</a> and <a href="/wiki/Financial_technology" title="Financial technology">fintech</a> <a href="/wiki/Startup_company" title="Startup company">startups</a><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> and other institutes. Automotive, technology and research, services, consulting, media and <a href="/wiki/Creative_industries" title="Creative industries">creative industries</a> complement the economic base. Frankfurt's <a href="/wiki/Deutscher_Commercial_Internet_Exchange" title="Deutscher Commercial Internet Exchange">DE-CIX</a> is the world's largest <a href="/wiki/Internet_exchange_point" title="Internet exchange point">internet exchange point</a>. <a href="/wiki/Messe_Frankfurt" title="Messe Frankfurt">Messe Frankfurt</a> is one of the world's largest <a href="/wiki/Trade_fair" title="Trade fair">trade fairs</a>. Major fairs include the <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Motor_Show" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankfurt Motor Show">Frankfurt Motor Show</a>, the world's largest motor show, the <a href="/wiki/Musikmesse_Frankfurt" title="Musikmesse Frankfurt">Music Fair</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Book_Fair" title="Frankfurt Book Fair">Frankfurt Book Fair</a>, the world's largest book fair.</p>
<p>Frankfurt is home to influential <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Germany" title="Education in Germany">educational</a> institutions, including the <a href="/wiki/Goethe_University_Frankfurt" title="Goethe University Frankfurt">Goethe University</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_University_of_Applied_Sciences" title="Frankfurt University of Applied Sciences">UAS</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_University_of_Music_and_Performing_Arts" title="Frankfurt University of Music and Performing Arts">FUMPA</a>, and graduate schools like the <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_School_of_Finance_%26_Management" title="Frankfurt School of Finance &amp; Management">Frankfurt School of Finance &amp; Management</a>. Its renowned <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Germany" title="Culture of Germany">cultural</a> venues include the concert hall <a href="/wiki/Alte_Oper" title="Alte Oper">Alte Oper</a>, Europe's largest <a href="/wiki/The_English_Theatre_Frankfurt" title="The English Theatre Frankfurt">English Theatre</a> and many museums (e.g. the <a href="/wiki/Museumsufer" title="Museumsufer">Museumsufer</a> ensemble with <a href="/wiki/St%C3%A4del" class="mw-redirect" title="Städel">Städel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Liebieghaus" title="Liebieghaus">Liebieghaus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Naturmuseum_Senckenberg" title="Naturmuseum Senckenberg">Senckenberg Natural Museum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Goethe_House" title="Goethe House">Goethe House</a>), the <a href="/wiki/Schirn_Kunsthalle_Frankfurt" title="Schirn Kunsthalle Frankfurt">Schirn</a> art venue at the <a href="/wiki/Altstadt_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Altstadt (Frankfurt am Main)">old town</a>. <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_Frankfurt" title="List of tallest buildings in Frankfurt">Frankfurt's skyline</a> is shaped by some of Europe's tallest skyscrapers. The city is also characterised by various green areas and parks, including the central <a href="/wiki/Wallanlagen" title="Wallanlagen">Wallanlagen</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_City_Forest" title="Frankfurt City Forest">City Forest</a> and two major <a href="/wiki/Botanical_garden" title="Botanical garden">botanical gardens</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Palmengarten" title="Palmengarten">Palmengarten</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Botanischer_Garten_der_Johann_Wolfgang_Goethe-Universit%C3%A4t_Frankfurt_am_Main" class="mw-redirect" title="Botanischer Garten der Johann Wolfgang Goethe-Universität Frankfurt am Main">University's Botanical Garden</a>. In <a href="/wiki/Electronic_music" title="Electronic music">electronic music</a>, Frankfurt has been a pioneering city since the 1980s, with renowned DJs including <a href="/wiki/Sven_V%C3%A4th" title="Sven Väth">Sven Väth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marc_Trauner" title="Marc Trauner">Marc Trauner</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scot_Project" title="Scot Project">Scot Project</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kai_Tracid" title="Kai Tracid">Kai Tracid</a>, and the clubs <a href="/wiki/Dorian_Gray_(club)" title="Dorian Gray (club)">Dorian Gray</a>, U60311, Omen and <a href="/wiki/Cocoon_(club)" title="Cocoon (club)">Cocoon</a>. In sports, the city is known as the home of the top tier football club <a href="/wiki/Eintracht_Frankfurt" title="Eintracht Frankfurt">Eintracht Frankfurt</a>, the basketball club <a href="/wiki/Skyliners_Frankfurt" title="Skyliners Frankfurt">Frankfurt Skyliners</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Marathon" title="Frankfurt Marathon">Frankfurt Marathon</a> and the venue of <a href="/wiki/Ironman_Germany" title="Ironman Germany">Ironman Germany</a>. It's the seat of German sport unions for <a href="/wiki/Deutscher_Olympischer_Sportbund" title="Deutscher Olympischer Sportbund">Olympics</a>, <a href="/wiki/German_Football_Association" title="German Football Association">football</a> and <a href="/wiki/Deutscher_Motor_Sport_Bund" title="Deutscher Motor Sport Bund">motor sports</a>.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Distinctions">Distinctions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Distinctions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rotlichviertel_Frankfurt_Main.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Rotlichviertel_Frankfurt_Main.JPG/220px-Rotlichviertel_Frankfurt_Main.JPG" width="220" height="156" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Rotlichviertel_Frankfurt_Main.JPG/330px-Rotlichviertel_Frankfurt_Main.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Rotlichviertel_Frankfurt_Main.JPG/440px-Rotlichviertel_Frankfurt_Main.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2454" data-file-height="1742" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rotlichviertel_Frankfurt_Main.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Often narrowly stereotyped as a financial city, Frankfurt is multifaceted, including the <a href="/wiki/Entertainment_district" title="Entertainment district">entertainment district</a> at <a href="/wiki/Bahnhofsviertel" title="Bahnhofsviertel">Bahnhofsviertel</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Frankfurt is the largest <a href="/wiki/Financial_centre" title="Financial centre">financial centre</a> in <a href="/wiki/Continental_Europe" title="Continental Europe">continental Europe</a>. It is home to the <a href="/wiki/European_Central_Bank" title="European Central Bank">European Central Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bundesbank" title="Deutsche Bundesbank">Deutsche Bundesbank</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Stock_Exchange" title="Frankfurt Stock Exchange">Frankfurt Stock Exchange</a> and several large commercial banks.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Stock_Exchange" title="Frankfurt Stock Exchange">Frankfurt Stock Exchange</a> is one of the world's largest <a href="/wiki/Stock_exchange" title="Stock exchange">stock exchanges</a> by <a href="/wiki/Market_capitalization" title="Market capitalization">market capitalization</a> and accounts for more than 90 percent of the turnover in the German market.</p>
<p>In 2010, 63 national and 152 international banks had their registered offices in Frankfurt, including Germany's major banks, notably <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bank" title="Deutsche Bank">Deutsche Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/Commerzbank" title="Commerzbank">Commerzbank</a>, <a href="/wiki/DZ_Bank" title="DZ Bank">DZ Bank</a> and <a href="/wiki/KfW" title="KfW">KfW</a>, as well as 41 representative offices of international banks.<sup id="cite_ref-Bundesbank:_Bankenplatz_Frankfurt_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bundesbank:_Bankenplatz_Frankfurt-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>Frankfurt is considered a <a href="/wiki/Global_city" title="Global city">global city</a> (alpha world city) as listed by the <a href="/wiki/Globalization_and_World_Cities_Research_Network" title="Globalization and World Cities Research Network">GaWC</a> group's 2012 inventory.<sup id="cite_ref-GaWC_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GaWC-8">[8]</a></sup> Among global cities it was ranked 10th by the <a href="/wiki/Global_city#Global_Power_City_Index" title="Global city">Global Power City Index 2011</a> and 11th by the <a href="/wiki/Global_city#Global_City_Competitiveness_Index" title="Global city">Global City Competitiveness Index 2012</a>. Among financial centres it was ranked 8th by the <a href="/wiki/Financial_centre#International_Financial_Centres_Development_Index" title="Financial centre">International Financial Centers Development Index 2013</a> and 9th by the <a href="/wiki/Global_Financial_Centres_Index" title="Global Financial Centres Index">Global Financial Centres Index 2013</a>.</p>
<p>Its central location within Germany and Europe makes Frankfurt a major air, rail and road <a href="/wiki/Transport_hub" title="Transport hub">transport hub</a>. <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Airport" title="Frankfurt Airport">Frankfurt Airport</a> is one of the <a href="/wiki/World%27s_busiest_airports_by_passenger_traffic" class="mw-redirect" title="World's busiest airports by passenger traffic">world's busiest international airports by passenger traffic</a> and the main hub for Germany's <a href="/wiki/Flag_carrier" title="Flag carrier">flag carrier</a> <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa" title="Lufthansa">Lufthansa</a>. <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_(Main)_Hauptbahnhof" title="Frankfurt (Main) Hauptbahnhof">Frankfurt Central Station</a> is one of the largest <a href="/wiki/Terminal_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Terminal station">rail stations</a> in Europe and the busiest junction operated by <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bahn" title="Deutsche Bahn">Deutsche Bahn</a>, the German national railway company, with 342 trains a day to domestic and European destinations.<sup id="cite_ref-Bahnhof.de_Frankfurt_Hbf_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bahnhof.de_Frankfurt_Hbf-9">[9]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Frankfurter_Kreuz" title="Frankfurter Kreuz">Frankfurter Kreuz</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Autobahn" title="Autobahn">Autobahn</a> <a href="/wiki/Interchange_(road)" title="Interchange (road)">interchange</a> close to the airport, is the most heavily used interchange in the EU, used by 320,000 cars daily.<sup id="cite_ref-Infos_at_strassenwaerter.de_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Infos_at_strassenwaerter.de-10">[10]</a></sup> In 2011 human-resource-consulting firm <a href="/wiki/Mercer_(consulting_firm)" title="Mercer (consulting firm)">Mercer</a> ranked Frankfurt as seventh in its annual 'Quality of Living' survey of cities around the world.<sup id="cite_ref-Mercer.27s_Survey_2011_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mercer.27s_Survey_2011-11">[11]</a></sup> According to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">The Economist</a></i> cost-of-living survey, Frankfurt is Germany's most expensive city and the world's 10th most expensive.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Economist_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Economist-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>Frankfurt has many <a href="/wiki/Tower_block" title="Tower block">high-rise buildings</a> in the city centre, forming the <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_Frankfurt" title="List of tallest buildings in Frankfurt">Frankfurt skyline</a>. It is one of the few cities in the European Union to have such a skyline and because of it Germans sometimes refer to Frankfurt as <a href="/wiki/Mainhattan" title="Mainhattan">Mainhattan</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Portmanteau" title="Portmanteau">portmanteau</a> of the local <a href="/wiki/Main_(river)" title="Main (river)">Main River</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">Manhattan</a>. The other well known and obvious nickname is <a href="/wiki/Bankfurt" class="mw-redirect" title="Bankfurt">Bankfurt</a>. Before <a href="/wiki/Bombing_of_Frankfurt_am_Main_in_World_War_II" title="Bombing of Frankfurt am Main in World War II">World War II</a> the city was globally noted for its unique <a href="/wiki/Altstadt_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Altstadt (Frankfurt am Main)">old town</a> with timber-framed buildings, the largest timber-framed old town in Europe. The <a href="/wiki/R%C3%B6mer" title="Römer">Römer</a> area was later rebuilt and is popular with visitors and for events such as <a href="/wiki/Christmas_market" title="Christmas market">Christmas markets</a>. Other parts of the old town are to be reconstructed as part of the <a href="/wiki/Dom-R%C3%B6mer_Project" title="Dom-Römer Project">Dom-Römer Project</a> by 2016.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Die_Frankenfurt.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Die_Frankenfurt.jpg/300px-Die_Frankenfurt.jpg" width="300" height="211" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Die_Frankenfurt.jpg/450px-Die_Frankenfurt.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Die_Frankenfurt.jpg/600px-Die_Frankenfurt.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1408" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Die_Frankenfurt.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The legend of the <i>Frankenfurt</i> (ford of the Franks)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><i>Frankonovurd</i> (in <a href="/wiki/Old_High_German" title="Old High German">Old High German</a>) or <i>Vadum Francorum</i> (in <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a>) were the first names mentioned in written records from 794. It transformed to <i>Frankenfort</i> during the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a> and then to <i>Franckfort</i> and <i>Franckfurth</i> in the <a href="/wiki/Modern_history" title="Modern history">modern era</a>. According to Czech historian <a href="/wiki/David_Gans" title="David Gans">Dovid Solomon Ganz</a>, the city was named <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr> 146 AD by its builder, a Frankish king named Zuna, who ruled over the province then known as <a href="/wiki/Sicambri" title="Sicambri">Sicambri</a>. He hoped thereby to perpetuate the name of his lineage.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> The name is derived from the <i>Franconofurd</i> of the <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">Germanic tribe</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Franks" title="Franks">Franks</a>; <i>Furt</i> (<a href="/wiki/Cf." title="Cf.">cf.</a> English '<a href="/wiki/Ford_(river)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford (river)">ford</a>) where the river was shallow enough to be crossed on foot.</p>
<p>By the 19th century, the name <i>Frankfurt</i> had been established as the official spelling. The older English spelling of <i><a href="/wiki/Frankfort_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="Frankfort (disambiguation)">Frankfort</a></i> is now rarely seen in reference to Frankfurt am Main, although more than a dozen other towns and cities, mainly in the United States, use this spelling (e.g., <a href="/wiki/Frankfort,_Kentucky" title="Frankfort, Kentucky">Frankfort, Kentucky</a>; <a href="/wiki/Frankfort_(town),_New_York" title="Frankfort (town), New York">Frankfort, New York</a>; <a href="/wiki/Frankfort,_Illinois" title="Frankfort, Illinois">Frankfort, Illinois</a>).</p>
<p>The suffix 'am Main' has been used regularly since the 14th century. In English, the city's full name of Frankfurt am Main means 'Frankfurt on the Main' (pronounced like English 'mine' or German <i>mein</i>). Frankfurt is located on an ancient ford (German: <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Furt</span></i>) on the <a href="/wiki/Main_(river)" title="Main (river)">Main River</a>. As a part of early <a href="/wiki/Franconia" title="Franconia">Franconia</a>, the inhabitants were the early <a href="/wiki/Franks" title="Franks">Franks</a>, thus the city's name reveals its legacy as "the ford of the Franks on the Main".<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>Among English speakers, the city is commonly known simply as Frankfurt, but Germans occasionally call it by its full name to distinguish it from the other (significantly smaller) German city of <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_(Oder)" title="Frankfurt (Oder)">Frankfurt an der Oder</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Federated_state" title="Federated state">federated state</a> of <a href="/wiki/Brandenburg" title="Brandenburg">Brandenburg</a> on the Polish border.</p>
<p>The city district <a href="/wiki/Bonames" title="Bonames">Bonames</a> has a name probably dating back to Roman times, thought to be derived from <i>bona me(n)sa</i> (good table).</p>
<p>The common abbreviations for the city, primarily used in railway services and on road signs, are <i>Frankfurt (Main)</i>, <i>Frankfurt (M)</i>, <i>Frankfurt a.M.</i>, <i>Frankfurt/Main</i> or <i>Frankfurt/M</i>. The common <a href="/wiki/Abbreviation" title="Abbreviation">abbreviation</a> for the name of the city is "FFM". Also in use is "FRA", the <a href="/wiki/International_Air_Transport_Association_airport_code" class="mw-redirect" title="International Air Transport Association airport code">IATA code</a> for Frankfurt Airport.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Frankfurt_am_Main" title="History of Frankfurt am Main">History of Frankfurt am Main</a> and <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Frankfurt" title="Timeline of Frankfurt">Timeline of Frankfurt</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Germania" title="Germania">Roman settlements</a> were established in the area of the <i>Römer</i>, probably in the first century. <i>Nida</i> (<a href="/wiki/Heddernheim" title="Heddernheim">Heddernheim</a>) was also a Roman civitas capital.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Alemanni" title="Alemanni">Alemanni</a> and Franks <a href="/wiki/Francia" title="Francia">lived there</a>, and by 794, <a href="/wiki/Charlemagne" title="Charlemagne">Charlemagne</a> presided over an <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Frankfurt" title="Council of Frankfurt">imperial assembly</a> and church synod, at which <i>Franconofurd</i> (alternative spellings end with -furt and -vurd) was first mentioned.</p>
<p>Frankfurt was one of the most important cities in the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a>. From 855, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_German_Kings_and_Emperors" class="mw-redirect" title="List of German Kings and Emperors">German kings and emperors</a> were elected and crowned in <a href="/wiki/Aachen" title="Aachen">Aachen</a>. From 1562, the kings and emperors were crowned in Frankfurt, initiated for <a href="/wiki/Maximilian_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Maximilian II, Holy Roman Emperor">Maximilian II</a>. This tradition ended in 1792, when <a href="/wiki/Francis_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Francis II, Holy Roman Emperor">Franz II</a> was elected. His coronation was deliberately held on <a href="/wiki/Bastille_Day" title="Bastille Day">Bastille Day</a>, 14 July, the anniversary of the <a href="/wiki/Storming_of_the_Bastille" title="Storming of the Bastille">storming of the Bastille</a>. The elections and coronations took place in <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Cathedral" title="Frankfurt Cathedral">St. Bartholomäus Cathedral</a>, known as the <i>Kaiserdom</i> (Emperor's Cathedral), or its predecessors.</p>
<p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Messe_Frankfurt" title="Messe Frankfurt">Frankfurter Messe</a></i> (Frankfurt Trade Fair) was first mentioned in 1150. In 1240, <a href="/wiki/Frederick_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Frederick II, Holy Roman Emperor">Emperor Friedrich II</a> granted an imperial privilege to its visitors, meaning they would be protected by the empire. The fair became particularly important when similar fairs in French Beaucaire lost attraction around 1380. Book trade fairs began in 1478.</p>
<p>In 1372, Frankfurt became a <i>Reichsstadt</i> (<a href="/wiki/Imperial_Free_City" class="mw-redirect" title="Imperial Free City">Imperial Free City</a>), i.e., directly subordinate to the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Holy Roman Emperor">Holy Roman Emperor</a> and not to a regional ruler or a local nobleman.</p>
<p>In 1585, Frankfurt traders established a system of <a href="/wiki/Exchange_rate" title="Exchange rate">exchange rates</a> for the various currencies that were circulating to prevent cheating and extortion. Therein lay the early roots for the Frankfurt Stock Exchange.</p>
<p>Frankfurt managed to remain neutral during the <a href="/wiki/Thirty_Years%27_War" title="Thirty Years' War">Thirty Years' War</a>, but suffered from the <a href="/wiki/Bubonic_plague" title="Bubonic plague">bubonic plague</a> that refugees brought to the city. After the war, Frankfurt regained its wealth.</p>
<div class="thumb tmulti tnone center">

</div>
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a>, Frankfurt was occupied or bombarded several times by French troops. It remained a <a href="/wiki/Free_imperial_city" title="Free imperial city">free city</a> until the collapse of the Holy Roman Empire in 1805/6. In 1806, it became part of the <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Aschaffenburg" title="Principality of Aschaffenburg">principality of Aschaffenburg</a> under the <i>Fürstprimas</i> (<a href="/wiki/Prince-Primate" class="mw-redirect" title="Prince-Primate">Prince-Primate</a>), <a href="/wiki/Karl_Theodor_Anton_Maria_von_Dalberg" title="Karl Theodor Anton Maria von Dalberg">Karl Theodor Anton Maria von Dalberg</a>. This meant that Frankfurt was incorporated into the <a href="/wiki/Confederation_of_the_Rhine" title="Confederation of the Rhine">confederation of the Rhine</a>. In 1810, Dalberg adopted the title of a <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Frankfurt" title="Grand Duchy of Frankfurt">Grand Duke of Frankfurt</a>. <a href="/wiki/Napoleon_I_of_France" class="mw-redirect" title="Napoleon I of France">Napoleon</a> intended to make his adopted son <a href="/wiki/Eug%C3%A8ne_de_Beauharnais" title="Eugène de Beauharnais">Eugène de Beauharnais</a>, already <i>Prince de Venise</i> ("<a href="/wiki/Prince_of_Venice" class="mw-redirect" title="Prince of Venice">prince of Venice</a>", a newly established primogeniture in Italy), Grand Duke of Frankfurt after Dalberg's death (since the latter as a Catholic bishop had no legitimate heirs). The Grand Duchy remained a short episode lasting from 1810 to 1813, when the military tide turned in favour of the Anglo-Prussian lead allies that overturned the Napoleonic order. Dalberg abdicated in favour of Eugène de Beauharnais, which of course was only a symbolic action, as the latter effectively never ruled after the ruin of the French armies and Frankfurt's takeover by the allies.</p>
<p>After Napoleon's final defeat and abdication, the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Vienna" title="Congress of Vienna">Congress of Vienna</a> (1814–1815) dissolved the grand-duchy, and Frankfurt entered the newly founded <a href="/wiki/German_Confederation" title="German Confederation">German Confederation</a> (till 1866) as a free city, becoming the seat of its <i>Bundestag</i>, the confederal parliament where the nominally presiding <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_Monarchy" title="Habsburg Monarchy">Habsburg Emperor of Austria</a> was represented by an Austrian "presidential envoy".</p>
<p>After the ill-fated <a href="/wiki/The_Revolutions_of_1848_in_the_German_states" class="mw-redirect" title="The Revolutions of 1848 in the German states">revolution of 1848</a>, Frankfurt was the seat of the first democratically elected German parliament, the <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Parliament" title="Frankfurt Parliament">Frankfurt Parliament</a>, which met in the <a href="/wiki/Frankfurter_Paulskirche" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankfurter Paulskirche">Frankfurter Paulskirche</a> (St. Paul's Church) and was opened on 18 May 1848. The institution failed in 1849 when the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Prussia" title="Kingdom of Prussia">Prussian</a> king declared that he would not accept "a crown from the gutter". In the year of its existence, the assembly developed a common constitution for a unified Germany, with the Prussian king as its monarch.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Courbet_Frankfurt.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Courbet_Frankfurt.jpg/220px-Courbet_Frankfurt.jpg" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Courbet_Frankfurt.jpg/330px-Courbet_Frankfurt.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Courbet_Frankfurt.jpg/440px-Courbet_Frankfurt.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="542" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Courbet_Frankfurt.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>View of Frankfurt am Main</i>, including the <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alte_Br%C3%BCcke_(Frankfurt_am_Main)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Alte Brücke (Frankfurt am Main) (page does not exist)">Alte Brücke</a></i> (Old Bridge), by <a href="/wiki/Gustave_Courbet" title="Gustave Courbet">Gustave Courbet</a> (1858)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Frankfurt lost its independence after the <a href="/wiki/Austro-Prussian_War" title="Austro-Prussian War">Austro-Prussian War</a> in 1866 when Prussia annexed several smaller states, among them the <a href="/wiki/Free_City_of_Frankfurt" title="Free City of Frankfurt">Free City of Frankfurt</a>. Frankfurt had stayed neutral in the war, but its free press bothered the Prussians and they used the opportunity to occupy the city by force: Bismarck had been an ambassador to the German Confederation there and constantly quarrelled with the local press. The Prussian administration incorporated Frankfurt into its province of <a href="/wiki/Hesse-Nassau" title="Hesse-Nassau">Hesse-Nassau</a>. The formerly independent towns of <a href="/wiki/Bornheim_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Bornheim (Frankfurt am Main)">Bornheim</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bockenheim_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Bockenheim (Frankfurt am Main)">Bockenheim</a> were incorporated in 1890.</p>
<p>In 1914, the citizens founded the University of Frankfurt, later named <a href="/wiki/Goethe_University_Frankfurt" title="Goethe University Frankfurt">Goethe University Frankfurt</a>. This marked the only civic foundation of a university in Germany; today it is one of Germany's largest.</p>
<p>From 6 April to 17 May 1920, following military intervention to put down the <a href="/wiki/Ruhr_uprising" title="Ruhr uprising">Ruhr uprising</a>, Frankfurt was occupied by French troops.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> The French claimed that Articles 42 to 44 of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles_(1919)" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty of Versailles (1919)">peace treaty of Versailles</a> concerning the demilitarisation of the <a href="/wiki/Rhine_Province" title="Rhine Province">Rhineland</a> had been broken.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> In 1924, <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_Landmann" title="Ludwig Landmann">Ludwig Landmann</a> became the first <a href="/wiki/Jewish" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish">Jewish</a> mayor of the city, and led a significant expansion during the following years. During the <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi era</a>, the synagogues of the city were destroyed.</p>
<p>Frankfurt was severely <a href="/wiki/Bombing_of_Frankfurt_am_Main_in_World_War_II" title="Bombing of Frankfurt am Main in World War II">bombed in World War II</a> (1939–1945). About 5,500 residents were killed during the raids, and the once-famous <a href="/wiki/Altstadt_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Altstadt (Frankfurt am Main)">medieval city centre</a>, by that time the largest in Germany, was almost completely destroyed. It became a ground battlefield on 26 March 1945, when the Allied advance into Germany was forced to take the city in contested urban combat that included a river assault. The <a href="/wiki/5th_Infantry_Division_(United_States)" title="5th Infantry Division (United States)">5th Infantry Division</a> and the <a href="/wiki/6th_Armored_Division_(United_States)" title="6th Armored Division (United States)">6th Armored Division</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army" title="United States Army">United States Army</a> captured Frankfurt after several days of intense fighting, and it was declared largely secure on 29 March 1945.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the end of the war, Frankfurt became a part of the newly founded state of Hesse, consisting of the old <a href="/wiki/People%27s_State_of_Hesse" title="People's State of Hesse">Hesse-(Darmstadt)</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Kurhessen" title="Province of Kurhessen">Prussian Hesse</a> provinces. The city was part of the <a href="/wiki/Allied_Occupation_Zones_in_Germany#American_Zone_of_Occupation" class="mw-redirect" title="Allied Occupation Zones in Germany">American Zone of Occupation</a> of Germany. The Military Governor for the United States Zone (1945–1949) and the United States High Commissioner for Germany (HICOG) (1949–1952) had their headquarters in the <a href="/wiki/IG_Farben_Building" title="IG Farben Building">IG Farben Building</a>, intentionally left undamaged by the Allies' wartime bombardment.</p>
<p>Frankfurt was the original choice for the provisional capital city of the newly founded state of <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">West Germany</a> in 1949. The city constructed a parliament building that was never used for its intended purpose (it housed the radio studios of <a href="/wiki/Hessischer_Rundfunk" title="Hessischer Rundfunk">Hessischer Rundfunk</a>). In the end, <a href="/wiki/Konrad_Adenauer" title="Konrad Adenauer">Konrad Adenauer</a>, the first postwar <a href="/wiki/Chancellor_of_Germany_(Federal_Republic)" class="mw-redirect" title="Chancellor of Germany (Federal Republic)">Chancellor</a>, preferred the town of <a href="/wiki/Bonn" title="Bonn">Bonn</a>, for the most part because it was close to his hometown, but also because many other prominent politicians opposed the choice of Frankfurt out of concern that Frankfurt would be accepted as the permanent capital, thereby weakening the West German population's support for a <a href="/wiki/German_reunification" title="German reunification">reunification</a> with <a href="/wiki/East_Germany" title="East Germany">East Germany</a> and the eventual return of the capital to <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a>.</p>
<p>Postwar reconstruction took place in a sometimes simple modern style, thus changing Frankfurt's architectural face. A few landmark buildings were reconstructed historically, albeit in a simplified manner (e.g., <a href="/wiki/R%C3%B6mer" title="Römer">Römer</a>, <a href="/wiki/St._Paul%27s_Church,_Frankfurt_am_Main" title="St. Paul's Church, Frankfurt am Main">St. Paul's Church</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Goethe_House" title="Goethe House">Goethe House</a>). The collection of historically significant <a href="/wiki/Cairo_Genizah" class="mw-redirect" title="Cairo Genizah">Cairo Genizah</a> documents of the Municipal Library was destroyed by the bombing. According to <a href="/wiki/Arabist" title="Arabist">Arabist</a> and Genizah scholar <a href="/wiki/S.D._Goitein" class="mw-redirect" title="S.D. Goitein">S.D. Goitein</a>, "not even handlists indicating its contents have survived."<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tmulti tnone center">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:1022px;max-width:1022px">

</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:367px;max-width:367px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Frankfurt_Am_Main-Samstagsberg-20070607.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Frankfurt_Am_Main-Samstagsberg-20070607.jpg/365px-Frankfurt_Am_Main-Samstagsberg-20070607.jpg" width="365" height="243" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Frankfurt_Am_Main-Samstagsberg-20070607.jpg/548px-Frankfurt_Am_Main-Samstagsberg-20070607.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Frankfurt_Am_Main-Samstagsberg-20070607.jpg/730px-Frankfurt_Am_Main-Samstagsberg-20070607.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2000" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
<center>Reconstruction (1981–1984) of six houses at the east side of the Römerberg which were destroyed in World War II</center>
</div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The end of the war marked Frankfurt's comeback as Germany's leading financial centre, mainly because Berlin, now a city divided into <a href="/wiki/History_of_Berlin#The_divided_city" title="History of Berlin">four sectors</a>, could no longer rival it. In 1948, the allies founded the <a href="/wiki/Bank_deutscher_L%C3%A4nder" title="Bank deutscher Länder">Bank deutscher Länder</a>, the forerunner of <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bundesbank" title="Deutsche Bundesbank">Deutsche Bundesbank</a>. Following this decision, more financial institutions were re-established, e.g. <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bank" title="Deutsche Bank">Deutsche Bank</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dresdner_Bank" title="Dresdner Bank">Dresdner Bank</a>. In the 1950s, Frankfurt Stock Exchange regained its position as the country's leading stock exchange.</p>
<p>Frankfurt also re-emerged as Germany's transportation centre and <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Airport" title="Frankfurt Airport">Frankfurt Airport</a> became Europe's second-busiest airport behind <a href="/wiki/London_Heathrow_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="London Heathrow Airport">London Heathrow Airport</a> in 1961.</p>
<p>During the 1970s, the city created one of Europe's most efficient underground transportation systems.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="most efficient is an opinion without data to back it up (October 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> That system includes a suburban rail system (<a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_S-Bahn" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankfurt S-Bahn">S-Bahn</a>) linking outlying communities with the city centre, and a deep underground light rail system with smaller coaches (<a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_U-Bahn" title="Frankfurt U-Bahn">U-Bahn</a>) also capable of travelling above ground on rails.</p>
<p>In 1998, the <a href="/wiki/European_Central_Bank" title="European Central Bank">European Central Bank</a> was founded in Frankfurt, followed by the <a href="/wiki/European_Insurance_and_Occupational_Pensions_Authority" title="European Insurance and Occupational Pensions Authority">European Insurance and Occupational Pensions Authority</a> and <a href="/wiki/European_Systemic_Risk_Board" title="European Systemic Risk Board">European Systemic Risk Board</a> in 2011.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>It is the largest city in the <a href="/wiki/Federated_state" title="Federated state">federated state</a> of Hesse in the south-western part of Germany.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Site">Site</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Site">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Frankfurt_Skyline_with_Cranes.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Frankfurt_Skyline_with_Cranes.JPG/300px-Frankfurt_Skyline_with_Cranes.JPG" width="300" height="199" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Frankfurt_Skyline_with_Cranes.JPG/450px-Frankfurt_Skyline_with_Cranes.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Frankfurt_Skyline_with_Cranes.JPG/600px-Frankfurt_Skyline_with_Cranes.JPG 2x" data-file-width="6016" data-file-height="4000" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Frankfurt_Skyline_with_Cranes.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Frankfurt's skyline from across the Main, showing construction cranes</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Frankfurt is located on both sides of the <a href="/wiki/Main_(river)" title="Main (river)">Main River</a>, south-east of the <a href="/wiki/Taunus" title="Taunus">Taunus</a> mountain range. The southern part of the city contains the <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_City_Forest" title="Frankfurt City Forest">Frankfurt City Forest</a>, Germany's largest city forest. The city area is 248.31&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (95.87&#160;sq&#160;mi) and extends over 23.4&#160;km (14.54&#160;mi) east to west and 23.3&#160;km (14.48&#160;mi) north to south. The city centre is north of the River Main in <a href="/wiki/Altstadt_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Altstadt (Frankfurt am Main)">Altstadt</a> district (the historical centre) and the surrounding <a href="/wiki/Innenstadt_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Innenstadt (Frankfurt am Main)">Innenstadt</a> district. The geographical centre is in <a href="/wiki/Bockenheim_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Bockenheim (Frankfurt am Main)">Bockenheim</a> district near <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_West_station" title="Frankfurt West station">Frankfurt West station</a>.</p>
<p>Frankfurt is the centre of the densely populated <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Rhine-Main" title="Frankfurt Rhine-Main">Frankfurt Rhine-Main Metropolitan Region</a> with a population of 5.5&#160;million. Other important cities in the region are <a href="/wiki/Wiesbaden" title="Wiesbaden">Wiesbaden</a> (capital of <a href="/wiki/Hessen" class="mw-redirect" title="Hessen">Hessen</a>), <a href="/wiki/Mainz" title="Mainz">Mainz</a> (capital of <a href="/wiki/Rhineland-Palatinate" title="Rhineland-Palatinate">Rhineland-Palatinate</a>), <a href="/wiki/Darmstadt" title="Darmstadt">Darmstadt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Offenbach_am_Main" title="Offenbach am Main">Offenbach am Main</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hanau" title="Hanau">Hanau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aschaffenburg" title="Aschaffenburg">Aschaffenburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bad_Homburg_vor_der_H%C3%B6he" title="Bad Homburg vor der Höhe">Bad Homburg vor der Höhe</a>, <a href="/wiki/R%C3%BCsselsheim" class="mw-redirect" title="Rüsselsheim">Rüsselsheim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wetzlar" title="Wetzlar">Wetzlar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marburg" title="Marburg">Marburg</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Districts">Districts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Districts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Frankfurt_Subdivisions_boroughs.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Frankfurt_Subdivisions_boroughs.svg/220px-Frankfurt_Subdivisions_boroughs.svg.png" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Frankfurt_Subdivisions_boroughs.svg/330px-Frankfurt_Subdivisions_boroughs.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Frankfurt_Subdivisions_boroughs.svg/440px-Frankfurt_Subdivisions_boroughs.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="921" data-file-height="921" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Frankfurt_Subdivisions_boroughs.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The 46 <i>Stadtteile</i> (city districts) of central Frankfurt</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The city is divided into 46 city districts (<i>Stadtteile</i>), which are in turn divided into 121 city boroughs (<i>Stadtbezirke</i>) and 448 electoral districts (<i>Wahlbezirke</i>). The 46 city districts combine into 16 area districts (<i><a href="/wiki/Ortsbezirk_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ortsbezirk (Frankfurt am Main)">Ortsbezirke</a></i>), which each have a district committee and chairperson.</p>
<p>The largest city district by population and area is <a href="/wiki/Sachsenhausen_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Sachsenhausen (Frankfurt am Main)">Sachsenhausen</a>, while the smallest is <a href="/wiki/Altstadt_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Altstadt (Frankfurt am Main)">Altstadt</a>, Frankfurt's historical center. Three larger city districts (Sachsenhausen, <a href="/wiki/Westend_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Westend (Frankfurt am Main)">Westend</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nordend_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Nordend (Frankfurt am Main)">Nordend</a>) are divided for administrative purposes into a northern (<i>-Nord</i>) and a southern (<i>-Süd</i>) part, respectively a western (<i>-West</i>) and an eastern (<i>-Ost</i>) part, but are generally considered as one city district (which is why often only 43 city districts are mentioned, even on the City's official website).<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>Some larger housing areas are often falsely called city districts, even by locals, like Nordweststadt (part of <a href="/wiki/Niederursel_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" class="mw-redirect" title="Niederursel (Frankfurt am Main)">Niederursel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heddernheim_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" class="mw-redirect" title="Heddernheim (Frankfurt am Main)">Heddernheim</a> and <a href="/wiki/Praunheim_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" class="mw-redirect" title="Praunheim (Frankfurt am Main)">Praunheim</a>), Goldstein (part of <a href="/wiki/Schwanheim_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Schwanheim (Frankfurt am Main)">Schwanheim</a>), Riedberg (part of <a href="/wiki/Kalbach-Riedberg_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kalbach-Riedberg (Frankfurt am Main)">Kalbach-Riedberg</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Europaviertel_(Frankfurt)" class="mw-redirect" title="Europaviertel (Frankfurt)">Europaviertel</a> (part of <a href="/wiki/Gallus_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Gallus (Frankfurt am Main)">Gallus</a>). The <a href="/wiki/Bankenviertel" title="Bankenviertel">Bankenviertel</a> (<i>banking district</i>), Frankfurt's financial district, is also not an administrative city district (it covers parts of the western <a href="/wiki/Innenstadt_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Innenstadt (Frankfurt am Main)">Innenstadt</a> district, the southern <a href="/wiki/Westend_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Westend (Frankfurt am Main)">Westend</a> district and the eastern <a href="/wiki/Bahnhofsviertel_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bahnhofsviertel (Frankfurt am Main)">Bahnhofsviertel</a> district).</p>
<p>Many city districts are incorporated suburbs (<i><a href="/wiki/Vororte" class="mw-redirect" title="Vororte">Vororte</a></i>), or were previously independent cities, such as <a href="/wiki/H%C3%B6chst_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Höchst (Frankfurt am Main)">Höchst</a>. Some like <a href="/wiki/Nordend_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Nordend (Frankfurt am Main)">Nordend</a> and <a href="/wiki/Westend_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Westend (Frankfurt am Main)">Westend</a> arose during the rapid growth of the city in the <a href="/wiki/Gr%C3%BCnderzeit" title="Gründerzeit">Gründerzeit</a> following the <a href="/wiki/Unification_of_Germany" title="Unification of Germany">Unification of Germany</a>, while others were formed from territory which previously belonged to other city district(s), such as <a href="/wiki/Dornbusch_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Dornbusch (Frankfurt am Main)">Dornbusch</a> and <a href="/wiki/Riederwald_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" class="mw-redirect" title="Riederwald (Frankfurt am Main)">Riederwald</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="History_of_incorporations">History of incorporations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: History of incorporations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Until the year 1877 the city's territory consisted of the present-day inner-city districts of <a href="/wiki/Altstadt_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Altstadt (Frankfurt am Main)">Altstadt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Innenstadt_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Innenstadt (Frankfurt am Main)">Innenstadt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bahnhofsviertel_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bahnhofsviertel (Frankfurt am Main)">Bahnhofsviertel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gutleutviertel_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" class="mw-redirect" title="Gutleutviertel (Frankfurt am Main)">Gutleutviertel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gallus_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Gallus (Frankfurt am Main)">Gallus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Westend_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Westend (Frankfurt am Main)">Westend</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nordend_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Nordend (Frankfurt am Main)">Nordend</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ostend_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Ostend (Frankfurt am Main)">Ostend</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sachsenhausen_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Sachsenhausen (Frankfurt am Main)">Sachsenhausen</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Bornheim_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Bornheim (Frankfurt am Main)">Bornheim</a> was part of an administrative district called <i>Landkreis Frankfurt</i>, before becoming part of the city on 1 January 1877, followed by <a href="/wiki/Bockenheim_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Bockenheim (Frankfurt am Main)">Bockenheim</a> on 1 April 1895. <a href="/wiki/Seckbach_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Seckbach (Frankfurt am Main)">Seckbach</a>, <a href="/wiki/Niederrad_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" class="mw-redirect" title="Niederrad (Frankfurt am Main)">Niederrad</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oberrad_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" class="mw-redirect" title="Oberrad (Frankfurt am Main)">Oberrad</a> followed on 1 July 1900. The <i>Landkreis Frankfurt</i> was finally dispersed on 1 April 1910, and therefore <a href="/wiki/Berkersheim_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" class="mw-redirect" title="Berkersheim (Frankfurt am Main)">Berkersheim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bonames_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bonames (Frankfurt am Main)">Bonames</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eckenheim_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" class="mw-redirect" title="Eckenheim (Frankfurt am Main)">Eckenheim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eschersheim_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" class="mw-redirect" title="Eschersheim (Frankfurt am Main)">Eschersheim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ginnheim_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ginnheim (Frankfurt am Main)">Ginnheim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hausen_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Hausen (Frankfurt am Main)">Hausen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heddernheim_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" class="mw-redirect" title="Heddernheim (Frankfurt am Main)">Heddernheim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Niederursel_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" class="mw-redirect" title="Niederursel (Frankfurt am Main)">Niederursel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Praunheim_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" class="mw-redirect" title="Praunheim (Frankfurt am Main)">Praunheim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Preungesheim_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" class="mw-redirect" title="Preungesheim (Frankfurt am Main)">Preungesheim</a> and <a href="/wiki/R%C3%B6delheim_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" class="mw-redirect" title="Rödelheim (Frankfurt am Main)">Rödelheim</a> joined the City. In the same year a new city district, <a href="/wiki/Riederwald_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" class="mw-redirect" title="Riederwald (Frankfurt am Main)">Riederwald</a>, was created on territory that had formerly belonged to Seckbach and Ostend.</p>
<p>On 1 April 1928 the City of <a href="/wiki/H%C3%B6chst_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Höchst (Frankfurt am Main)">Höchst</a> became part of Frankfurt, as well as its city districts <a href="/wiki/Sindlingen_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sindlingen (Frankfurt am Main)">Sindlingen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Unterliederbach_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" class="mw-redirect" title="Unterliederbach (Frankfurt am Main)">Unterliederbach</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zeilsheim_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" class="mw-redirect" title="Zeilsheim (Frankfurt am Main)">Zeilsheim</a>. Simultaneously the <i>Landkreis Höchst</i> was dispersed with its member cities either joining Frankfurt (<a href="/wiki/Fechenheim_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" class="mw-redirect" title="Fechenheim (Frankfurt am Main)">Fechenheim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Griesheim_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Griesheim (Frankfurt am Main)">Griesheim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nied_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Nied (Frankfurt am Main)">Nied</a>, <a href="/wiki/Schwanheim_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Schwanheim (Frankfurt am Main)">Schwanheim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sossenheim_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sossenheim (Frankfurt am Main)">Sossenheim</a>) or joining the newly established <i>Landkreis</i> of <a href="/wiki/Main-Taunus-Kreis" title="Main-Taunus-Kreis">Main-Taunus-Kreis</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Dornbusch_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Dornbusch (Frankfurt am Main)">Dornbusch</a> became a city district in 1946. It was created on territory that had formerly belonged to Eckenheim and Ginnheim.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Enkheimer_Ried.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Enkheimer_Ried.jpg/220px-Enkheimer_Ried.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Enkheimer_Ried.jpg/330px-Enkheimer_Ried.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Enkheimer_Ried.jpg/440px-Enkheimer_Ried.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2576" data-file-height="1932" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Enkheimer_Ried.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Bergen-Enkheim_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bergen-Enkheim (Frankfurt am Main)">Enkheimer</a> Ried</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 1 August 1972 Hesse's smaller suburbs of <a href="/wiki/Harheim_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" class="mw-redirect" title="Harheim (Frankfurt am Main)">Harheim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kalbach_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kalbach (Frankfurt am Main)">Kalbach</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nieder-Erlenbach_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" class="mw-redirect" title="Nieder-Erlenbach (Frankfurt am Main)">Nieder-Erlenbach</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nieder-Eschbach_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" class="mw-redirect" title="Nieder-Eschbach (Frankfurt am Main)">Nieder-Eschbach</a> became districts while other neighbouring suburbs chose to join the Main-Taunus-Kreis, the <a href="/wiki/Landkreis_Offenbach" class="mw-redirect" title="Landkreis Offenbach">Landkreis Offenbach</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Kreis_Gro%C3%9F-Gerau" class="mw-redirect" title="Kreis Groß-Gerau">Kreis Groß-Gerau</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Hochtaunuskreis" title="Hochtaunuskreis">Hochtaunuskreis</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Main-Kinzig-Kreis" title="Main-Kinzig-Kreis">Main-Kinzig-Kreis</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Wetteraukreis" title="Wetteraukreis">Wetteraukreis</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Bergen-Enkheim_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bergen-Enkheim (Frankfurt am Main)">Bergen-Enkheim</a> was the last suburb to become part of Frankfurt on 1 January 1977.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Flughafen_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" class="mw-redirect" title="Flughafen (Frankfurt am Main)">Flughafen</a> became an official city district in 1979. It covers the area of Frankfurt Airport that had belonged to Sachsenhausen and the neighbouring city of <a href="/wiki/M%C3%B6rfelden-Walldorf" title="Mörfelden-Walldorf">Mörfelden-Walldorf</a>.</p>
<p>Frankfurt's youngest city district is <a href="/wiki/Frankfurter_Berg" title="Frankfurter Berg">Frankfurter Berg</a>. It was part of Bonames until 1996.</p>
<p>Kalbach was officially renamed <a href="/wiki/Kalbach-Riedberg" title="Kalbach-Riedberg">Kalbach-Riedberg</a> in 2006 because of the large residential housing development in the area known as Riedberg.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Neighbouring_districts_and_cities">Neighbouring districts and cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Neighbouring districts and cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Locator_map_of_Planungsverband_Ballungsraum_Frankfurt_Rhein-Main_in_Hesse.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Locator_map_of_Planungsverband_Ballungsraum_Frankfurt_Rhein-Main_in_Hesse.svg/180px-Locator_map_of_Planungsverband_Ballungsraum_Frankfurt_Rhein-Main_in_Hesse.svg.png" width="180" height="214" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Locator_map_of_Planungsverband_Ballungsraum_Frankfurt_Rhein-Main_in_Hesse.svg/270px-Locator_map_of_Planungsverband_Ballungsraum_Frankfurt_Rhein-Main_in_Hesse.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Locator_map_of_Planungsverband_Ballungsraum_Frankfurt_Rhein-Main_in_Hesse.svg/360px-Locator_map_of_Planungsverband_Ballungsraum_Frankfurt_Rhein-Main_in_Hesse.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="3365" data-file-height="4007" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Locator_map_of_Planungsverband_Ballungsraum_Frankfurt_Rhein-Main_in_Hesse.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Frankfurt urban area within <a href="/wiki/Hesse" title="Hesse">Hesse</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>To the west Frankfurt borders the <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Germany" title="Districts of Germany">administrative district</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/List_of_rural_districts_of_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="List of rural districts of Germany">Landkreis</a></i>) of <a href="/wiki/Main-Taunus-Kreis" title="Main-Taunus-Kreis">Main-Taunus-Kreis</a> with towns such as <a href="/wiki/Hattersheim_am_Main" title="Hattersheim am Main">Hattersheim am Main</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kriftel" title="Kriftel">Kriftel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hofheim_am_Taunus" class="mw-redirect" title="Hofheim am Taunus">Hofheim am Taunus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kelkheim_(Taunus)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kelkheim (Taunus)">Kelkheim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liederbach_am_Taunus" title="Liederbach am Taunus">Liederbach am Taunus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sulzbach_(Taunus)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sulzbach (Taunus)">Sulzbach</a>, <a href="/wiki/Schwalbach_am_Taunus" title="Schwalbach am Taunus">Schwalbach am Taunus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eschborn" title="Eschborn">Eschborn</a>; to the northwest the <a href="/wiki/Hochtaunuskreis" title="Hochtaunuskreis">Hochtaunuskreis</a> with <a href="/wiki/Steinbach_(Taunus)" title="Steinbach (Taunus)">Steinbach</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oberursel_(Taunus)" title="Oberursel (Taunus)">Oberursel (Taunus)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bad_Homburg_vor_der_H%C3%B6he" title="Bad Homburg vor der Höhe">Bad Homburg vor der Höhe</a>; to the north the <a href="/wiki/Wetteraukreis" title="Wetteraukreis">Wetteraukreis</a> with <a href="/wiki/Karben" title="Karben">Karben</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bad_Vilbel" title="Bad Vilbel">Bad Vilbel</a>; to the northeast the <a href="/wiki/Main-Kinzig-Kreis" title="Main-Kinzig-Kreis">Main-Kinzig-Kreis</a> with <a href="/wiki/Niederdorfelden" title="Niederdorfelden">Niederdorfelden</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maintal" title="Maintal">Maintal</a>; to the southeast the city of <a href="/wiki/Offenbach_am_Main" title="Offenbach am Main">Offenbach am Main</a>; to the south the <a href="/wiki/Offenbach_(district)" title="Offenbach (district)">Kreis Offenbach</a> with <a href="/wiki/Neu-Isenburg" title="Neu-Isenburg">Neu-Isenburg</a> and to the southwest the <a href="/wiki/Gro%C3%9F-Gerau_(district)" title="Groß-Gerau (district)">Kreis Groß-Gerau</a> with <a href="/wiki/M%C3%B6rfelden-Walldorf" title="Mörfelden-Walldorf">Mörfelden-Walldorf</a>, <a href="/wiki/R%C3%BCsselsheim" class="mw-redirect" title="Rüsselsheim">Rüsselsheim</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kelsterbach" title="Kelsterbach">Kelsterbach</a>.</p>
<p>Together with these towns (and some larger nearby towns, e.g., <a href="/wiki/Hanau" title="Hanau">Hanau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rodgau" title="Rodgau">Rodgau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dreieich" title="Dreieich">Dreieich</a>, <a href="/wiki/Langen,_Hesse" title="Langen, Hesse">Langen</a>) Frankfurt forms a contiguous built-up urban area called <i>Stadtregion Frankfurt</i> which is not an official administrative district. The urban area had an estimated population of 2.3&#160;million in 2010 and is therefore the <a href="/wiki/Largest_urban_areas_in_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Largest urban areas in the European Union">13th largest urban area in the European Union</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Frankfurt has a <a href="/wiki/Temperateness" class="mw-redirect" title="Temperateness">temperate</a>-<a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">oceanic climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen</a>: Cfb). Its average annual temperature is 10.6&#160;°C (51.1&#160;°F), with monthly mean temperatures ranging from 1.6&#160;°C (34.9&#160;°F) in January to 20.0&#160;°C (68.0&#160;°F) in July.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Population">Population</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Population">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Main_Luftbild_Offenbach_%26_Frankfurt.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Main_Luftbild_Offenbach_%26_Frankfurt.jpg/200px-Main_Luftbild_Offenbach_%26_Frankfurt.jpg" width="200" height="133" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Main_Luftbild_Offenbach_%26_Frankfurt.jpg/300px-Main_Luftbild_Offenbach_%26_Frankfurt.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Main_Luftbild_Offenbach_%26_Frankfurt.jpg/400px-Main_Luftbild_Offenbach_%26_Frankfurt.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000" /></a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Frankfurt_Skyline_at_Night.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Frankfurt_Skyline_at_Night.jpg/200px-Frankfurt_Skyline_at_Night.jpg" width="200" height="133" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Frankfurt_Skyline_at_Night.jpg/300px-Frankfurt_Skyline_at_Night.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Frankfurt_Skyline_at_Night.jpg/400px-Frankfurt_Skyline_at_Night.jpg 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" /></a></div>
</div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent">Aerial photographs</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>With a population of 732.688 (2015) within its administrative boundaries<sup id="cite_ref-Statistik-Hessen.de_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Statistik-Hessen.de-4">[4]</a></sup> and of 2,300,000 in the actual <a href="/wiki/Largest_urban_areas_of_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Largest urban areas of the European Union">urban area</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-staedtestatistik.de_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-staedtestatistik.de-5">[5]</a></sup> Frankfurt is <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Germany_by_population" title="List of cities in Germany by population">the fifth largest city in Germany</a> after <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a>, Hamburg, <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a>. Central Frankfurt has been a <i>Großstadt</i> (a city with at least 100,000 residents by definition) since 1875. With 414,576 residents in 1910, it was the ninth largest city in Germany and the number of inhabitants grew to 553,464 before <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>. After the war, at the end of the year 1945, the number had dropped to 358,000. In the following years the population grew again and reached an all-time-high of 691,257 in 1963. It dropped again to 592,411 in 1986 but has increased since then. According to the demographic forecasts for central Frankfurt, the city will have a population up to 825,000 within its administrative boundaries in 2020 and more than 2.5&#160;million inhabitants in its urban area.</p>
<p>During the 1970s the state government of <a href="/wiki/Hesse" title="Hesse">Hesse</a> wanted to include the entire urban area into its administrative boundaries. This would have made Frankfurt officially the second largest city in Germany after Berlin with up to 3 million inhabitants.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> However, because local authorities did not agree the administrative territory is still much smaller than its actual urban area.</p>

<p>According to data from the city <a href="/wiki/Resident_registration#Germany" title="Resident registration">register of residents</a>, 51,2 percent of the population had an immigrant background as of 2015. For the first time a majority of the city residents had a non-German background.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> Moreover, three of four children in the city under the age of six had immigrant backgrounds.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> Moreover, about 27,7 percent of residents had a foreign citizenship.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>The city is considered a multicultural city because it is home to people of 180 nationalities. The city contains sizable immigrant populations from <a href="/wiki/Turks_in_Germany" title="Turks in Germany">Turkey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Croatians_in_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Croatians in Germany">Croatia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italians_in_Germany" title="Italians in Germany">Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poles_in_Germany" title="Poles in Germany">Poland</a>, Romania, <a href="/wiki/Serbs_in_Germany" title="Serbs in Germany">Serbia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bulgarians_in_Germany" title="Bulgarians in Germany">Bulgaria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greeks_in_Germany" title="Greeks in Germany">Greece</a>, <a href="/wiki/Macedonians_in_Germany" title="Macedonians in Germany">Macedonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russians_in_Germany" title="Russians in Germany">Russia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_people_in_Germany" title="Lebanese people in Germany">Lebanon</a>, Afghanistan, Bosnia and Herzegovina, <a href="/wiki/Spaniards_in_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Spaniards in Germany">Spain</a>, Portugal, France, <a href="/wiki/Chinese_people_in_Germany" title="Chinese people in Germany">China</a>, Japan, the United States, Austria, the United Kingdom, Pakistan, Morocco and India.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The Frankfurt urban area is also home to the second-largest <a href="/wiki/Koreans_in_Germany" title="Koreans in Germany">Korean</a> community in Europe, and to Germany's largest <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lankan_Tamil" class="mw-redirect" title="Sri Lankan Tamil">Sri Lankan Tamil</a> community.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Frankfurt was historically a <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a>-dominated city. However, during the 19th century an increasing number of <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism in Germany">Catholics</a> moved there. The Jewish community has a history dating back to Medieval times and has always ranked among the largest in Germany. Two synagogues operate there. Due to the growing immigration of people from Muslim countries beginning in the 1960s, Frankfurt has a large Muslim community. The <a href="/wiki/Ahmadiyya" title="Ahmadiyya">Ahmadiyya</a> <a href="/wiki/Noor_Mosque" title="Noor Mosque">Noor Mosque</a>, constructed in 1959, is the city's largest mosque and the third largest in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of 2013<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> the largest Christian denominations were Roman Catholicism (22.7% of the population) and Protestantism (19.4%).<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> Estimations put the share of Muslim inhabitants at approximately 12% (2006).<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> According to calculations based on census data for 21 countries of origin the number of Muslim migrants in Frankfurt amounted to about 84,000 in 2011, making up 12.6 percent of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> A large part of them was from Turkey and Morocco. Over 7,000 inhabitants were affiliated with the Jewish community, amounting to approximately 1% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">

<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. <p>Frankfurt is one of five <a href="/wiki/Independent_city" title="Independent city">independent district-free cities</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Urban_districts_of_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Urban districts of Germany">kreisfreie Städte</a></i>) in <a href="/wiki/Hesse" title="Hesse">Hesse</a>, which means that it does not form part of another general-purpose local government entity, in this case it is not part of a <i><a href="/wiki/List_of_rural_districts_of_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="List of rural districts of Germany">Landkreis</a></i>. The other four cities are the second to fifth largest cities in Hesse: <a href="/wiki/Wiesbaden" title="Wiesbaden">Wiesbaden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kassel" title="Kassel">Kassel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Darmstadt" title="Darmstadt">Darmstadt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Offenbach_am_Main" title="Offenbach am Main">Offenbach am Main</a>. A <i>kreisfreie Stadt</i> has territorial <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">sovereignty</a> within its defined city limits.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Petra_Roth" title="Petra Roth">In 1995 Petra Roth</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Christian_Democratic_Union_(Germany)" class="mw-redirect" title="Christian Democratic Union (Germany)">Christian Democratic Union</a> (CDU) became <a href="/wiki/Lord_Mayor" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord Mayor">Lord Mayor</a> (<i>Oberbürgermeisterin</i>), Frankfurt's municipal leader. In 2012, <a href="/wiki/Peter_Feldmann" title="Peter Feldmann">Peter Feldmann</a> (SPD) succeeded Roth as Lord Mayor. The CDU and the <a href="/wiki/Alliance_%2790/The_Greens" class="mw-redirect" title="Alliance '90/The Greens">Alliance '90/The Greens</a> (<i>Bündnis '90/Die Grünen</i>) formed the government.</p>
