<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Partnerships">Partnerships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Partnerships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Partnerships and city friendships are a weaker form of cooperation than the sister city relationship, acting more like a fixed-term cooperation or limited to certain projects. Frankfurt has partnerships with the following cities:</p>
<ul>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt"><img alt="Egypt" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Flag_of_Egypt.svg/23px-Flag_of_Egypt.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Flag_of_Egypt.svg/35px-Flag_of_Egypt.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Flag_of_Egypt.svg/45px-Flag_of_Egypt.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Cairo" title="Cairo">Cairo</a>, Egypt (1979)</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel"><img alt="Israel" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Flag_of_Israel.svg/21px-Flag_of_Israel.svg.png" width="21" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Flag_of_Israel.svg/32px-Flag_of_Israel.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Flag_of_Israel.svg/41px-Flag_of_Israel.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="660" data-file-height="480" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv" title="Tel Aviv">Tel Aviv</a>, Israel (1980)</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada"><img alt="Canada" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cf/Flag_of_Canada.svg/23px-Flag_of_Canada.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cf/Flag_of_Canada.svg/35px-Flag_of_Canada.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cf/Flag_of_Canada.svg/46px-Flag_of_Canada.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="500" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a>, Ontario, Canada, (1989)<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/France" title="France"><img alt="France" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/23px-Flag_of_France.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/35px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/45px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Deuil-la-Barre" title="Deuil-la-Barre">Deuil-la-Barre</a>, Val-d'Oise, <a href="/wiki/%C3%8Ele-de-France" title="Île-de-France">Île-de-France</a>, France, partnered with <a href="/wiki/Nieder-Eschbach_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" class="mw-redirect" title="Nieder-Eschbach (Frankfurt am Main)">Nieder-Eschbach</a>, (1967; incorporated into Frankfurt in 1972)</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland"><img alt="Poland" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/12/Flag_of_Poland.svg/23px-Flag_of_Poland.svg.png" width="23" height="14" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/12/Flag_of_Poland.svg/35px-Flag_of_Poland.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/12/Flag_of_Poland.svg/46px-Flag_of_Poland.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="800" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w" title="Kraków">Kraków</a>, Poland, (1991)<sup id="cite_ref-Krak.C3.B3w_partnerships_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Krak.C3.B3w_partnerships-37">[37]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany"><img alt="Germany" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/23px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png" width="23" height="14" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/35px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/46px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Leipzig" title="Leipzig">Leipzig</a>, Saxony, Germany (1990)</li>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Landmarks">Landmarks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Landmarks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Frankfurter_R%C3%B6mer.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Frankfurter_R%C3%B6mer.jpg/300px-Frankfurter_R%C3%B6mer.jpg" width="300" height="221" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Frankfurter_R%C3%B6mer.jpg/450px-Frankfurter_R%C3%B6mer.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Frankfurter_R%C3%B6mer.jpg/600px-Frankfurter_R%C3%B6mer.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1474" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Frankfurter_R%C3%B6mer.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/R%C3%B6mer" title="Römer">Römer</a>, the city hall</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/R%C3%B6mer" title="Römer">Römer</a></b></li>
</ul>
<p>"Römer" is the German word for "<a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Roman</a>" and the name of a complex of nine houses that form Frankfurt <a href="/wiki/City_hall" class="mw-redirect" title="City hall">city hall</a> (<i>Rathaus</i>). The houses were acquired by the city council in 1405 from a wealthy merchant family. The middle house became the city hall and was later connected with its neighbours. The <i>Kaisersaal</i> ("Emperor's Hall") is located on the upper floor and is where the newly crowned emperors held their banquets. The Römer was partially destroyed in World War II and later rebuilt. The surrounding square, the Römerberg, is named after the city hall.</p>
<p>The former <a href="/wiki/Altstadt_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Altstadt (Frankfurt am Main)">Altstadt</a> (old town) quarter between the Römer and the Frankfurt Cathedral was to be redeveloped as the <a href="/wiki/Dom-R%C3%B6mer_Project" title="Dom-Römer Project">Dom-Römer Quarter</a> through 2016, including <a href="/wiki/Reconstruction_(architecture)" title="Reconstruction (architecture)">reconstructions</a> of historical buildings that were destroyed during World War II.</p>
<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Cathedral" title="Frankfurt Cathedral">Frankfurt Cathedral</a> (Dom)</b></li>
</ul>
<p>Saint Bartholomew's Cathedral (<i>Dom Sankt Bartholomäus</i>), (named after <a href="/wiki/Bartholomew_the_Apostle" title="Bartholomew the Apostle">Bartholomew the Apostle</a>), is a <a href="/wiki/Gothic_architecture" title="Gothic architecture">Gothic</a> building constructed in the 14th and 15th centuries on the foundation of an earlier church from the <a href="/wiki/Merovingian" class="mw-redirect" title="Merovingian">Merovingian</a> time. From 1356 onwards, kings of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a> were elected in this church, and from 1562 to 1792, <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Roman-German</a> emperors were crowned there. It is the city's main church.</p>
<p>Since the 18th century, St. Bartholomew's has been called "the cathedral" by the people, although it was never a bishop's seat. In 1867 it was destroyed by fire and rebuilt in its present style. It was again partially destroyed in <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> and rebuilt in the 1950s. Its height is 95 meters. The cathedral tower has a viewing platform open to the public at a height of 66 meters, accessed through a narrow spiral staircase with 386 steps.</p>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:812px;max-width:812px">

</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Frankfurt_Paulskirche_au%C3%9Fen_2011a.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Frankfurt_Paulskirche_au%C3%9Fen_2011a.jpg/200px-Frankfurt_Paulskirche_au%C3%9Fen_2011a.jpg" width="200" height="214" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Frankfurt_Paulskirche_au%C3%9Fen_2011a.jpg/300px-Frankfurt_Paulskirche_au%C3%9Fen_2011a.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Frankfurt_Paulskirche_au%C3%9Fen_2011a.jpg/400px-Frankfurt_Paulskirche_au%C3%9Fen_2011a.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2590" data-file-height="2776" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
<center><a href="/wiki/St._Paul%27s_Church,_Frankfurt" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Paul's Church, Frankfurt">Saint Paul's Church</a></center>
</div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/St._Paul%27s_Church,_Frankfurt" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Paul's Church, Frankfurt">Saint Paul's Church</a></b></li>
</ul>
<p>Saint Paul's Church (<i>Paulskirche</i>) is a national historic monument in Germany because it was the seat of the first democratically elected Parliament in 1848. It was established in 1789 as a <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> church, but was not completed until 1833. Its importance has its roots in the <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Parliament" title="Frankfurt Parliament">Frankfurt Parliament</a>, which met in the church during the revolutionary years of 1848/49 in order to write a constitution for a united Germany. The attempt failed because the monarchs of <a href="/wiki/Prussia" title="Prussia">Prussia</a> and Austria did not want to lose power. In 1849 Prussian troops ended the democratic experiment by force and the parliament dissolved. Afterwards, the building was used for church services again.</p>
<p>St. Paul's was partially destroyed in World War II, particularly its interior, which now has a modern appearance. It was quickly and symbolically rebuilt after the war; today it is used mainly for exhibitions and events.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Frankfurt_Hauptwache_View.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Frankfurt_Hauptwache_View.jpg/220px-Frankfurt_Hauptwache_View.jpg" width="220" height="331" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Frankfurt_Hauptwache_View.jpg/330px-Frankfurt_Hauptwache_View.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Frankfurt_Hauptwache_View.jpg/440px-Frankfurt_Hauptwache_View.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="6016" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Frankfurt_Hauptwache_View.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The view towards downtown Frankfurt from <a href="/wiki/Zeil" title="Zeil">Zeil</a> shopping street</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><b>Archäologischer Garten Frankfurt</b></li>
</ul>
<p>The Archaeological Garden contains small parts of the oldest recovered buildings: an ancient Roman settlement and the Frankfurt Royal Palace (<i>Kaiserpfalz Frankfurt</i>) from the 6th century. The garden is located between the Römerberg and St. Bartholomew's. It was discovered after World War II when the area was heavily bombed and later partly rebuilt. The remains were preserved and are now open to the public. There are plans underway to construct a building on top of the garden but anyhow it is decided that the garden will stay open to the public.</p>
<ul>
<li><b>Haus Wertheim</b></li>
</ul>
<p>Wertheim House is the only <a href="/wiki/Timber_framing" title="Timber framing">timbered house</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Altstadt_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Altstadt (Frankfurt am Main)">Altstadt</a> district that survived the heavy bombings of World War II undamaged. It is located on the Römerberg next to the Historical Museum.</p>
<ul>
<li><b>Saalhof</b></li>
</ul>
<p>The Saalhof is the oldest conserved building in the <a href="/wiki/Altstadt_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Altstadt (Frankfurt am Main)">Altstadt</a> district and dates to the 12th century. It was used as an exhibition hall by Dutch <a href="/wiki/Cloth_merchant" title="Cloth merchant">clothiers</a> when trade fairs were held during the 14th and 15th century. The Saalhof was partly destroyed in World War II and later rebuilt. Today it serves as a part of the <a href="/wiki/Historical_museum,_Frankfurt" class="mw-redirect" title="Historical museum, Frankfurt">Historical Museum</a>.</p>
<ul>
<li><b>Eiserner Steg</b></li>
</ul>
<p>The Eiserner Steg (Iron Bridge) is a pedestrian-only bridge over the Main river that connects Römerberg and Sachsenhausen. It was built in 1868 and was the second bridge to cross the river. After World War II, when it was blown up by the <a href="/wiki/Wehrmacht" title="Wehrmacht">Wehrmacht</a>, it was quickly rebuilt in 1946. Today some 10,000 people cross the bridge on a daily basis.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Alte_Oper_Frankfurt_Winter_2008.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Alte_Oper_Frankfurt_Winter_2008.jpg/300px-Alte_Oper_Frankfurt_Winter_2008.jpg" width="300" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Alte_Oper_Frankfurt_Winter_2008.jpg/450px-Alte_Oper_Frankfurt_Winter_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Alte_Oper_Frankfurt_Winter_2008.jpg/600px-Alte_Oper_Frankfurt_Winter_2008.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2000" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Alte_Oper_Frankfurt_Winter_2008.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Alte_Oper" title="Alte Oper">Alte Oper</a>, now a concert hall, at Opernplatz</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Alte_Oper" title="Alte Oper">Alte Oper</a></b></li>
</ul>
<p>The Alte Oper is a former <a href="/wiki/Opera_house" title="Opera house">opera house</a>, hence the name "Old Opera". It was built in 1880 by architect Richard Lucae. It was one of the major opera houses in Germany until it was heavily damaged in World War II. Until the late 1970s, it was a ruin, nicknamed "Germany's Most Beautiful Ruin". Former Frankfurt <a href="/wiki/Lord_Mayor" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord Mayor">Lord Mayor</a> Rudi Arndt called for blowing it up in the 1960s, which earned him the nickname "Dynamite-Rudi". (Later on, Arndt said he never had meant his suggestion seriously.)</p>
<p>Public pressure led to its refurbishment and reopening in 1981. Today, it functions as a famous concert hall, while operas are performed at the "new" Frankfurt Opera. The inscription on the <a href="/wiki/Frieze" title="Frieze">frieze</a> of the Alte Oper says: "<i>Dem Wahren, Schönen, Guten</i>" ("To the true, the beautiful, the good").</p>
<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Eschenheimer_Turm" title="Eschenheimer Turm">Eschenheimer Turm</a></b></li>
</ul>
<p>The Eschenheim Tower (<i>Eschenheimer Turm</i>) was erected at the beginning of the 15th century and served as a city gate as part of late-medieval fortifications. It is the oldest and most unaltered building in the <a href="/wiki/Innenstadt_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Innenstadt (Frankfurt am Main)">Innenstadt</a> district.</p>
<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/St._Catherine%27s_Church,_Frankfurt" title="St. Catherine's Church, Frankfurt">Saint Catherine's Church</a></b></li>
</ul>
<p>St. Catherine's Church (<i>Katharinenkirche</i>) is the largest <a href="/wiki/Evangelical_Church_in_Germany" title="Evangelical Church in Germany">evangelical</a> church, dedicated to the <a href="/wiki/Martyr" title="Martyr">martyred</a> early Christian <a href="/wiki/Saint" title="Saint">saint</a>, <a href="/wiki/Catherine_of_Alexandria" title="Catherine of Alexandria">Catherine of Alexandria</a>. It is located in the city centre at the entrance to the Zeil, the central shopping street.</p>
<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Hauptwache_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Hauptwache (Frankfurt am Main)">Hauptwache</a></b></li>
</ul>
<p>Although today "Hauptwache" is mostly associated with the inner-city underground train station <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_(Main)_Hauptwache_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankfurt (Main) Hauptwache station">of the same name</a>, the name originates from a <a href="/wiki/Baroque_architecture" title="Baroque architecture">baroque</a> building on the square above the station. The Hauptwache building was constructed in 1730 and was used as a prison, therefore the name that translates as "main guard-house". Today the square surrounding the building is also called "Hauptwache" (formal: <i>An der Hauptwache</i>). It is situated in the city centre opposite to St. Catherine's Church and houses a famous café.</p>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:742px;max-width:742px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:302px;max-width:302px">

</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:132px;max-width:132px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Frankfurt_Nextower.20130514.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Frankfurt_Nextower.20130514.jpg/130px-Frankfurt_Nextower.20130514.jpg" width="130" height="193" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Frankfurt_Nextower.20130514.jpg/195px-Frankfurt_Nextower.20130514.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Frankfurt_Nextower.20130514.jpg/260px-Frankfurt_Nextower.20130514.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2693" data-file-height="4000" /></a></div>

<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:302px;max-width:302px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Frankfurt_Main_Hauptbahnhof_6229.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Frankfurt_Main_Hauptbahnhof_6229.jpg/300px-Frankfurt_Main_Hauptbahnhof_6229.jpg" width="300" height="138" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Frankfurt_Main_Hauptbahnhof_6229.jpg/450px-Frankfurt_Main_Hauptbahnhof_6229.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Frankfurt_Main_Hauptbahnhof_6229.jpg/600px-Frankfurt_Main_Hauptbahnhof_6229.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="1413" /></a></div>

</div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Central_Station" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankfurt Central Station">Frankfurt Central Station</a></b></li>
</ul>
<p>Frankfurt Central Station (<i>Frankfurt Hauptbahnhof</i>), which opened in 1888, was built as the central train station for Frankfurt to replace three smaller train stations in the city centre and to boost the needed capacity for travellers. It was constructed as a <a href="/wiki/Terminal_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Terminal station">terminus station</a> and was the largest train station in Europe by floor area until 1915 when <a href="/wiki/Leipzig_Hauptbahnhof" title="Leipzig Hauptbahnhof">Leipzig Central Station</a> was opened. Its three main halls were constructed in a <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_Revival_architecture" title="Renaissance Revival architecture">neorenaissance</a>-style, while the later enlargement with two outer halls in 1924 was constructed in <a href="/wiki/Neoclassicism" title="Neoclassicism">neoclassic</a>-style.</p>
<ul>
<li><b>Frankfurter Hof</b></li>
</ul>
<p>The Frankfurter Hof is a landmarked hotel in the city centre at Kaiserplatz, built from 1872 to 1876. It is part of <a href="/wiki/Steigenberger_Hotels" class="mw-redirect" title="Steigenberger Hotels">Steigenberger Hotels</a> group and is considered the city's most prestigious.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th-century_architecture">20th-century architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: 20th-century architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Frauenfriedenskirche" title="Frauenfriedenskirche">Frauenfriedenskirche</a></b> and <b><a href="/wiki/Holy_Cross_Church,_Frankfurt-Bornheim" title="Holy Cross Church, Frankfurt-Bornheim">Holy Cross Church</a></b> (with the <a href="/wiki/Centre_for_Christian_Meditation_and_Spirituality_of_the_Diocese_of_Limburg" title="Centre for Christian Meditation and Spirituality of the Diocese of Limburg">Centre for Christian Meditation and Spirituality of the Diocese of Limburg</a>), both consecrated 1929, are examples of early modernist church buildings during the time of the <a href="/wiki/New_Frankfurt" title="New Frankfurt">New Frankfurt</a>.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Gro%C3%9Fmarkthalle" title="Großmarkthalle">Grossmarkthalle</a></b>, built 1926–1928 as a part of the <a href="/wiki/New_Frankfurt" title="New Frankfurt">New Frankfurt</a>-project, the former wholesale market hall, was (following reconstruction) to become part of the future <a href="/wiki/Seat_of_the_European_Central_Bank" title="Seat of the European Central Bank">seat of the European Central Bank</a>.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Goethe_House" title="Goethe House">Goethe House</a></b>, rebuilt 1947. The birthplace of <a href="/wiki/Johann_Wolfgang_von_Goethe" title="Johann Wolfgang von Goethe">Johann Wolfgang von Goethe</a> from 1749 was destroyed in World War II and then rebuilt true to the original.</li>
<li><b>Junior-Haus</b>, built 1951, an example of early post-World War II architecture located at Kaiserplatz.</li>
<li><b>Bayer-Haus</b>, built 1952, another example of early post-World War II architecture.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Museum_f%C3%BCr_angewandte_Kunst_Frankfurt" class="mw-redirect" title="Museum für angewandte Kunst Frankfurt">Museum für angewandte Kunst</a></b>, built 1985, designed by <a href="/wiki/Richard_Meier" title="Richard Meier">Richard Meier</a>.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/IG_Farben_Building" title="IG Farben Building">IG Farben Building</a></b> – Also known as <b>Poelzig Building</b> (<i>Poelzig-Bau</i>) after its architect <a href="/wiki/Hans_Poelzig" title="Hans Poelzig">Hans Poelzig</a>, it was built from 1928 to 1930 as the corporate headquarters of <a href="/wiki/IG_Farben" title="IG Farben">I.G. Farbenindustrie AG</a>. It is located in the <a href="/wiki/Westend_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Westend (Frankfurt am Main)">Westend</a> district and borders <a href="/wiki/Gr%C3%BCneburgpark" title="Grüneburgpark">Grüneburgpark</a> in the west. Upon its completion, the complex was the <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_buildings_in_the_world" class="mw-redirect" title="List of largest buildings in the world">largest office building</a> in Europe and remained so until the 1950s. The building served as headquarters for research projects relating to the development of <a href="/wiki/Synthetic_oil" title="Synthetic oil">synthetic oil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Synthetic_rubber" title="Synthetic rubber">rubber</a> and the manufacturing of <a href="/wiki/Magnesium" title="Magnesium">magnesium</a>, lubricating oil, explosives, <a href="/wiki/Methanol" title="Methanol">methanol</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Zyklon_B" title="Zyklon B">Zyklon B</a>, the lethal gas used in <a href="/wiki/Nazi_concentration_camps" title="Nazi concentration camps">concentration camps</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-zyclon_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-zyclon-38">[38]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-tourist_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tourist-39">[39]</a></sup> After World War II, it served as the headquarters for the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Allied_Commander" title="Supreme Allied Commander">Supreme Allied Command</a> and from 1949 to 1952 the High Commissioner for Germany (HICOG). It became the principal location for implementing the <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Plan" title="Marshall Plan">Marshall Plan</a>, which largely financed the post-war reconstruction of Europe. The state apparatus of the <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">Federal German Government</a> was devised there. It served as the headquarters for the <a href="/wiki/U.S._V_Corps" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. V Corps">US Army's V Corps</a> and the Northern Area Command (NACOM) until 1995 when the US Army returned control of the IG Farben Building to the German government. It was purchased on behalf of the <a href="/wiki/Goethe_University_Frankfurt" title="Goethe University Frankfurt">Goethe University Frankfurt</a> by the state of <a href="/wiki/Hesse" title="Hesse">Hesse</a>. In October 2001 it became part of the Westend Campus of Goethe University.
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width:auto; max-width:1018px;"></div>
</li>
</ul>
<div class="thumbinner" style="">
<div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:IG_Farben_Gebaeude_Uni_Frankfurt.jpg" class="image" title="IG Farben Building, now the central lecture building of the Westend Campus of the Goethe University"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/IG_Farben_Gebaeude_Uni_Frankfurt.jpg/1010px-IG_Farben_Gebaeude_Uni_Frankfurt.jpg" width="1010" height="195" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/IG_Farben_Gebaeude_Uni_Frankfurt.jpg/1515px-IG_Farben_Gebaeude_Uni_Frankfurt.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/IG_Farben_Gebaeude_Uni_Frankfurt.jpg/2020px-IG_Farben_Gebaeude_Uni_Frankfurt.jpg 2x" data-file-width="10176" data-file-height="1967" /></a></div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="21st-century_architecture">21st-century architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: 21st-century architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Squaire,_Frankfurt_am_Main-1060.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/The_Squaire%2C_Frankfurt_am_Main-1060.jpg/220px-The_Squaire%2C_Frankfurt_am_Main-1060.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/The_Squaire%2C_Frankfurt_am_Main-1060.jpg/330px-The_Squaire%2C_Frankfurt_am_Main-1060.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/The_Squaire%2C_Frankfurt_am_Main-1060.jpg/440px-The_Squaire%2C_Frankfurt_am_Main-1060.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4849" data-file-height="2728" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Squaire,_Frankfurt_am_Main-1060.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Squaire in 2017</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><b>Die Welle</b> (<i>The Wave</i>), built 1998–2003, a complex of three wavelike-formed office buildings next to the Opernplatz.</li>
<li><b>Alte Stadtbibliothek</b>, rebuilt 2003–2005, reconstruction of the old public library house originally built 1820–1825.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Palais_Thurn_und_Taxis" title="Palais Thurn und Taxis">Palais Thurn und Taxis</a></b>, rebuilt 2004–2009, reconstruction of a palace originally built 1731–1739.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/MyZeil" title="MyZeil">MyZeil</a></b>, built 2004–2009, shopping mall at the Zeil with an imposing vaulted glass-structure.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/The_Squaire" title="The Squaire">The Squaire</a></b> (<a href="/wiki/Portmanteau" title="Portmanteau">portmanteau</a> of <i>square</i> and <i>air</i>), also known as <b>Airrail Center Frankfurt</b>, is a 660&#160;m (2,165.35&#160;ft) long and 45&#160;m (147.64&#160;ft) tall office building located at <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Airport" title="Frankfurt Airport">Frankfurt Airport</a>. It was built from 2006 to 2011 on top of an existing railway station (<a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Airport_long-distance_station" title="Frankfurt Airport long-distance station">Frankfurt Airport long distance Station</a>) and has a connecting bridge to Terminal 1 for pedestrians. Its total of 140,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup> (1,506,947&#160;sq&#160;ft) rentable floor space makes it Germany's largest office building.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Skyscrapers">Skyscrapers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Skyscrapers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_Frankfurt" title="List of tallest buildings in Frankfurt">List of tallest buildings in Frankfurt</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Maintower-spitze-005.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Maintower-spitze-005.jpg/220px-Maintower-spitze-005.jpg" width="220" height="298" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Maintower-spitze-005.jpg/330px-Maintower-spitze-005.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Maintower-spitze-005.jpg/440px-Maintower-spitze-005.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2884" data-file-height="3902" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Maintower-spitze-005.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Upper section of the <a href="/wiki/Main_Tower" title="Main Tower">Main Tower</a> with a public observation deck at 200 metres</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Frankfurt is one of the few European cities with a significant number of skyscrapers, (buildings at least 150&#160;m (492.13&#160;ft) tall). It hosts 14 out of Germany's 15 <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_Germany" title="List of tallest buildings in Germany">skyscrapers</a>. Most skyscrapers and high-rise office buildings are located in the financial district (<a href="/wiki/Bankenviertel" title="Bankenviertel">Bankenviertel</a>) near the city centre, around the trade fair premises (<a href="/wiki/Europaviertel_(Frankfurt)" class="mw-redirect" title="Europaviertel (Frankfurt)">Europaviertel</a>) and at <a href="/wiki/Mainzer_Landstra%C3%9Fe" title="Mainzer Landstraße">Mainzer Landstraße</a> between Opernplatz and Platz der Republik, which connects the two areas.</p>
<p>The 14 skyscrapers are:</p>
<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Commerzbank_Tower" title="Commerzbank Tower">Commerzbank Tower</a></b>, 259.0&#160;m (849.74&#160;ft) – The European Union's second tallest building, Headquarters of <a href="/wiki/Commerzbank" title="Commerzbank">Commerzbank</a>.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Messeturm" title="Messeturm">Messeturm</a></b>, 256.5&#160;m (841.54&#160;ft) – The European Union's tallest building (1990–1997), Main tenant is <a href="/wiki/Goldman_Sachs" title="Goldman Sachs">Goldman Sachs</a> (Germany).</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Westend_Tower" class="mw-redirect" title="Westend Tower">Westend Tower</a></b>, 208.0&#160;m (682.41&#160;ft) – <a href="/wiki/DZ_Bank" title="DZ Bank">DZ Bank</a> headquarters</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Main_Tower" title="Main Tower">Main Tower</a></b>, 200.0&#160;m (656.17&#160;ft) – <a href="/wiki/Helaba" title="Helaba">Landesbank Hessen-Thüringen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Standard_%26_Poor%27s" title="Standard &amp; Poor's">Standard &amp; Poor's</a> (Germany) headquarters</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Tower_185" title="Tower 185">Tower 185</a></b>, 200.0&#160;m (656.17&#160;ft) – <a href="/wiki/PWC" class="mw-redirect" title="PWC">PricewaterhouseCoopers</a> (Germany) headquarters</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Trianon_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Trianon (Frankfurt am Main)">Trianon</a></b>, 186.0&#160;m (610.24&#160;ft) – <a href="/wiki/DekaBank" class="mw-redirect" title="DekaBank">DekaBank</a> headquarters</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Seat_of_the_European_Central_Bank" title="Seat of the European Central Bank">Seat of the European Central Bank</a></b>, 185.0&#160;m (606.96&#160;ft) – <a href="/wiki/European_Central_Bank" title="European Central Bank">European Central Bank headquarters</a></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Opernturm" title="Opernturm">Opernturm</a></b>, 170.0&#160;m (557.74&#160;ft) – <a href="/wiki/UBS" title="UBS">UBS</a> (Germany) headquarters</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Taunusturm" title="Taunusturm">Taunusturm</a></b>, 170.0&#160;m (557.74&#160;ft)</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Silberturm" title="Silberturm">Silberturm</a></b>, 166.3&#160;m (545.60&#160;ft) – Germany's tallest building (1978–1990), Main tenant is <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bahn" title="Deutsche Bahn">Deutsche Bahn</a>.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Westend_Gate" title="Westend Gate">Westend Gate</a></b>, 159.3&#160;m (522.64&#160;ft) – Germany's tallest building (1976–1978), Main tenant is <a href="/wiki/Marriott_International" title="Marriott International">Marriott</a> Frankfurt Hotel.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bank_Twin_Towers" title="Deutsche Bank Twin Towers">Deutsche Bank I</a></b>, 155.0&#160;m (508.53&#160;ft) – <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bank" title="Deutsche Bank">Deutsche Bank</a> headquarters</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bank_Twin_Towers" title="Deutsche Bank Twin Towers">Deutsche Bank II</a></b>, 155.0&#160;m (508.53&#160;ft) – "</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Skyper" title="Skyper">Skyper</a></b>, 153.8&#160;m (504.59&#160;ft) – Main tenant is DekaBank.</li>
</ul>
<p>Other high-rise buildings include:</p>
<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Eurotower_(Frankfurt)" class="mw-redirect" title="Eurotower (Frankfurt)">Eurotower</a></b>, 148.0&#160;m (485.56&#160;ft) – <a href="/wiki/European_Central_Bank" title="European Central Bank">European Central Bank headquarters</a></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Frankfurter_B%C3%BCro_Center" title="Frankfurter Büro Center">Frankfurter Büro Center</a></b>, 142.4&#160;m (467.19&#160;ft) – Main tenant is <a href="/wiki/Clifford_Chance" title="Clifford Chance">Clifford Chance</a> (Germany).</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/City-Haus" title="City-Haus">City-Haus</a></b>, 142.1&#160;m (466.21&#160;ft) – Main tenant is DZ Bank.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Gallileo_(skyscraper)" title="Gallileo (skyscraper)">Gallileo</a></b>, 136.0&#160;m (446.19&#160;ft) – Main tenant is Commerzbank.</li>
</ul>
<div class="center">
<div class="thumb tnone">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:1052px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Frankfurt_Skyline_Pano.S%C3%BCdwest.20130618.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Frankfurt_Skyline_Pano.S%C3%BCdwest.20130618.jpg/1050px-Frankfurt_Skyline_Pano.S%C3%BCdwest.20130618.jpg" width="1050" height="348" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Frankfurt_Skyline_Pano.S%C3%BCdwest.20130618.jpg/1575px-Frankfurt_Skyline_Pano.S%C3%BCdwest.20130618.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Frankfurt_Skyline_Pano.S%C3%BCdwest.20130618.jpg/2100px-Frankfurt_Skyline_Pano.S%C3%BCdwest.20130618.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6476" data-file-height="2147" /></a>

Frankfurt skyline in June 2013, view from south-west</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="History_of_high-rise_buildings">History of high-rise buildings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: History of high-rise buildings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_Frankfurt" title="List of tallest buildings in Frankfurt">List of tallest buildings in Frankfurt</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Frankfurt_Skyline_(16259801511).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Frankfurt_Skyline_%2816259801511%29.jpg/300px-Frankfurt_Skyline_%2816259801511%29.jpg" width="300" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Frankfurt_Skyline_%2816259801511%29.jpg/450px-Frankfurt_Skyline_%2816259801511%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Frankfurt_Skyline_%2816259801511%29.jpg/600px-Frankfurt_Skyline_%2816259801511%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3955" data-file-height="2966" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Frankfurt_Skyline_(16259801511).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Skyline at dusk, seen from Deutschherrnbrücke (2014)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>For centuries, <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Cathedral" title="Frankfurt Cathedral">St. Bartholomeus's Cathedral</a> was the tallest structure. The first building to exceed the 95-metre-high cathedral was not an office building but a <a href="/wiki/Grain_silo" class="mw-redirect" title="Grain silo">grain silo</a>, the 120-metre high <a href="/wiki/Henninger_Turm" title="Henninger Turm">Henninger Turm</a>, built from 1959 to 1961.</p>
<p>The first high-rise building boom came in the 1970s when <a href="/wiki/Westend_Gate" title="Westend Gate">Westend Gate</a> (then called <i>Plaza Büro Center</i>) and <a href="/wiki/Silberturm" title="Silberturm">Silberturm</a> were constructed and became the tallest buildings in Germany with a height of 159.3 metres and 166.3 metres, respectively. Around the same time, <a href="/wiki/Frankfurter_B%C3%BCro_Center" title="Frankfurter Büro Center">Frankfurter Büro Center</a> and <a href="/wiki/City-Haus" title="City-Haus">City-Haus</a> (142.4 metres and 142.1 metres) were constructed at Mainzer Landstraße and <a href="/wiki/Eurotower_(Frankfurt)" class="mw-redirect" title="Eurotower (Frankfurt)">Eurotower</a> (148.0 metres) and <a href="/wiki/Garden_Tower" title="Garden Tower">Garden Tower</a> (127.0 metres; then called <i>Helaba-Hochhaus</i>) were constructed in the financial district.</p>
<p>None of the buildings constructed during the 1980s surpassed Silberturm. The most famous buildings from this decade are the <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bank_Twin_Towers" title="Deutsche Bank Twin Towers">Deutsche Bank Twin Towers</a> at Taunusanlage, both 155.0 metres tall.</p>
<p>The 1990s featured a second wave. <a href="/wiki/Messeturm" title="Messeturm">Messeturm</a>, built on the trade fair site, reached a height of 256.5 metres and became the tallest building in Europe by 1991. It was overtaken by the 259-metre high <a href="/wiki/Commerzbank_Tower" title="Commerzbank Tower">Commerzbank Tower</a> in 1997. Other tall buildings from this decade are <a href="/wiki/Westendstrasse_1" title="Westendstrasse 1">Westendstrasse 1</a> (208.0 metres), <a href="/wiki/Main_Tower" title="Main Tower">Main Tower</a> (200.0 metres) and <a href="/wiki/Trianon_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Trianon (Frankfurt am Main)">Trianon</a> (186.0 metres).</p>
<p>In 21st-century Frankfurt, more high-rise buildings and skyscrapers (e.g., <a href="/wiki/Skyper" title="Skyper">Skyper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Opernturm" title="Opernturm">Opernturm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tower_185" title="Tower 185">Tower 185</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seat_of_the_European_Central_Bank" title="Seat of the European Central Bank">Seat of the European Central Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taunusturm" title="Taunusturm">Taunusturm</a>) emerged, but none have surpassed Commerzbank Tower.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_tall_structures">Other tall structures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Other tall structures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Europaturm_Abend.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Europaturm_Abend.jpg/220px-Europaturm_Abend.jpg" width="220" height="298" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Europaturm_Abend.jpg/330px-Europaturm_Abend.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Europaturm_Abend.jpg/440px-Europaturm_Abend.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1142" data-file-height="1545" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Europaturm_Abend.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Top of the <a href="/wiki/Europaturm" title="Europaturm">Europaturm</a>, a 337&#160;m communications tower</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Europaturm" title="Europaturm">Europaturm</a> —</b> The Europe Tower is a <a href="/wiki/Radio_masts_and_towers" title="Radio masts and towers">telecommunications tower</a>, also known as the Frankfurt TV Tower, built from 1974 to 1979. With a height of 337.5 metres it is the tallest tower and the second tallest structure in Germany after the <a href="/wiki/Fernsehturm_Berlin" title="Fernsehturm Berlin">Fernsehturm Berlin</a>. It was open to the public until 1999, with an entertainment establishment in the revolving top. It is normally referred to by locals as the "Ginnheimer Spargel" (<i>Ginnheim Asparagus</i>), but stands a few metres within <a href="/wiki/Bockenheim_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Bockenheim (Frankfurt am Main)">Bockenheim</a> district.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Henninger_Turm" title="Henninger Turm">Henninger Turm</a> —</b> The Henninger Tower was a 120-metre-high <a href="/wiki/Grain_silo" class="mw-redirect" title="Grain silo">grain silo</a> built from 1959 to 1961 and owned by <a href="/wiki/Henninger_Brewery" title="Henninger Brewery">Henninger Brewery</a>. It was the highest structure until 1974. The Henninger Tower had two rotating restaurants at the height of 101 and 106 metres and an open-air observation deck at the height of 110 metres. The tower closed to the public in October 2002 and was demolished in 2013 to be replaced by a 140&#160;m (459&#160;ft) tall residential tower, which is externally inspired by the old Henninger Turm, and will contain 130 luxury apartments. The cornerstone for this project was laid in June 2014 and was expected to be completed sometime in 2016. From 1962 to 2008 a famous yearly <a href="/wiki/Road_bicycle_racing" title="Road bicycle racing">cycling race</a> was named after the tower, the "Radrennen Rund um den Henninger Turm" (<i>Cycling race around Henninger Tower</i>). The now-renamed race is still a yearly event.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Goethe_Tower" title="Goethe Tower">Goetheturm —</a></b> The Goethe Tower is a 43-metre high tower on the northern edge of the <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_City_Forest" title="Frankfurt City Forest">Frankfurt City Forest</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sachsenhausen_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Sachsenhausen (Frankfurt am Main)">Sachsenhausen</a>. It is the fifth tallest wood construction structure in Germany. It was built in 1931 and is still a popular place for day-trippers, especially families, who frequent a large playground and café at the foot of the tower. Climbing the Goethe Tower is free of charge and offers a spectacular view of the Frankfurt skyline.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Shopping_streets">Shopping streets</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Shopping streets">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Frankfurt_Am_Main-Zeil-Ansicht_vom_Maintower_am_fruehen_Abend-20110328.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Frankfurt_Am_Main-Zeil-Ansicht_vom_Maintower_am_fruehen_Abend-20110328.jpg/170px-Frankfurt_Am_Main-Zeil-Ansicht_vom_Maintower_am_fruehen_Abend-20110328.jpg" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Frankfurt_Am_Main-Zeil-Ansicht_vom_Maintower_am_fruehen_Abend-20110328.jpg/255px-Frankfurt_Am_Main-Zeil-Ansicht_vom_Maintower_am_fruehen_Abend-20110328.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Frankfurt_Am_Main-Zeil-Ansicht_vom_Maintower_am_fruehen_Abend-20110328.jpg/340px-Frankfurt_Am_Main-Zeil-Ansicht_vom_Maintower_am_fruehen_Abend-20110328.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="4500" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Frankfurt_Am_Main-Zeil-Ansicht_vom_Maintower_am_fruehen_Abend-20110328.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Zeil" title="Zeil">Zeil</a>, Frankfurt's central shopping street.</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Zeil" title="Zeil">Zeil</a></b> – Frankfurt's central shopping street. It is a pedestrian-only area and is bordered by two large public squares, <a href="/wiki/Hauptwache_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Hauptwache (Frankfurt am Main)">Hauptwache</a> in the west and <a href="/wiki/Konstablerwache" title="Konstablerwache">Konstablerwache</a> in the east. It is the second most expensive street for shops to rent in Germany after the Kaufingerstraße in <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a>. 85 percent of the shops are retail chains such as <a href="/wiki/H%26M" title="H&amp;M">H&amp;M</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saturn_(store)" title="Saturn (store)">Saturn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Esprit_Holdings" title="Esprit Holdings">Esprit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zara_(retailer)" title="Zara (retailer)">Zara</a> or <a href="/wiki/NewYorker" title="NewYorker">NewYorker</a>. In 2009 a new shopping mall named <a href="/wiki/MyZeil" title="MyZeil">MyZeil</a> opened there with nearly 100 stores and chains like <a href="/wiki/Hollister_Co." title="Hollister Co.">Hollister</a>. Three more shopping malls occupy the Zeil: <a href="/wiki/Zeilgalerie" title="Zeilgalerie">Zeilgalerie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Metro_AG" title="Metro AG">Galeria Kaufhof</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arcandor" title="Arcandor">Karstadt</a>, as well as large fashion retail clothing stores from <a href="/wiki/Peek_%26_Cloppenburg" title="Peek &amp; Cloppenburg">Peek &amp; Cloppenburg</a> and <a href="/wiki/C%26A" title="C&amp;A">C&amp;A</a>. During the month before Christmas, the extended pedestrian-only zone is host to <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Christmas_Market" title="Frankfurt Christmas Market">Frankfurt Christmas Market</a>, one of the largest and oldest Christmas markets in Germany.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Goethestra%C3%9Fe" title="Goethestraße">Goethestraße</a></b> – Frankfurt's most expensive shopping street with prestigious shops like <a href="/wiki/Louis_Vuitton" title="Louis Vuitton">Louis Vuitton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prada" title="Prada">Prada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gucci" title="Gucci">Gucci</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tiffany_%26_Co." title="Tiffany &amp; Co.">Tiffany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Giorgio_Armani" title="Giorgio Armani">Giorgio Armani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Versace" title="Versace">Versace</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cartier_SA" class="mw-redirect" title="Cartier SA">Cartier</a>, <a href="/wiki/Burberry" title="Burberry">Burberry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vertu" title="Vertu">Vertu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bulgari" title="Bulgari">Bulgari</a>. It is located between the financial district and the city centre and runs from Goetheplatz to Opernplatz.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fre%C3%9Fgass" title="Freßgass">Freßgass</a> – (officially <i>Kalbächer Gasse</i> and <i>Große Bockenheimer Straße</i>) is a pedestrian-only street section between Börsenstraße and Opernplatz in the city centre. The name translates as "feeding alley" because of its high concentration of gastronomy, but lately prestigious shops (e.g., <a href="/wiki/Apple_Store" title="Apple Store">Apple Store</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Boss" title="Hugo Boss">Hugo Boss</a>, <a href="/wiki/Porsche_Design_Group" title="Porsche Design Group">Porsche Design</a>) have moved here due to the lack of space in the neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Goethestra%C3%9Fe" title="Goethestraße">Goethestraße</a>, displacing old, established restaurants, butchers and delicatessens.</li>
<li><b>Berger Straße</b> – Frankfurt's longest shopping street. It starts in the city center, runs through <a href="/wiki/Nordend,_Frankfurt" class="mw-redirect" title="Nordend, Frankfurt">Nordend</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bornheim_(Frankfurt)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bornheim (Frankfurt)">Bornheim</a> and ends in <a href="/wiki/Seckbach_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Seckbach (Frankfurt am Main)">Seckbach</a>. The street is less crowded than the Zeil and offers a greater variety of smaller shops, restaurants and cafés.</li>
<li><b>Leipziger Straße</b> – Central shopping street in the Bockenheim district starting at Bockenheimer Warte going towards West. High density of shops for daily needs.</li>
<li><b>Braubachstraße</b> – in the <a href="/wiki/Altstadt_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Altstadt (Frankfurt am Main)">Altstadt</a> district, close to the historic sites of the city, offers a large variety of art galleries, second-hand bookshops and antique shops.</li>
<li><b>Münchener Straße</b> – In the <a href="/wiki/Bahnhofsviertel_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bahnhofsviertel (Frankfurt am Main)">Bahnhofsviertel</a> district, located between the central station and Willy-Brandt-Platz, is the most multicultural shopping street with lots of shops that sell imported products mainly from Turkey, the Middle East and Asia.</li>
<li><b>Kaiserstraße</b> – One of the best-known streets and considered one of the most beautiful because of its amount of <a href="/wiki/Gr%C3%BCnderzeit" title="Gründerzeit">Gründerzeit</a>-style buildings. It runs parallel to Münchener Straße from the central station to the financial district. Kaiserstraße is still a synonym for Frankfurt's <a href="/wiki/Red-light_district" title="Red-light district">Red-light district</a> although <a href="/wiki/Sex_industry" title="Sex industry">sex-oriented businesses</a> moved to neighbouring streets such as Taunusstraße in the 1990s. Today Kaiserstraße houses many smaller shops, restaurants and cafés.</li>
<li><b>Kleinmarkthalle</b> – (literally: <i>Small Market Hall</i>) is a market hall in the city centre close to Konstablerwache offering fresh food and flowers. In addition to regional delicacies like <a href="/wiki/Green_sauce" title="Green sauce">green sauce</a> imported goods are offered. The Kleinmarkthalle is the largest public market place in Frankfurt.</li>
</ul>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:1026px;max-width:1026px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:354px;max-width:354px">

</div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Green_city">Green city</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Green city">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Skyline-sued-ffm001.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Skyline-sued-ffm001.jpg/220px-Skyline-sued-ffm001.jpg" width="220" height="114" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Skyline-sued-ffm001.jpg/330px-Skyline-sued-ffm001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Skyline-sued-ffm001.jpg/440px-Skyline-sued-ffm001.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2845" data-file-height="1480" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Skyline-sued-ffm001.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_City_Forest" title="Frankfurt City Forest">Frankfurt City Forest</a> seen from <a href="/wiki/Goethe_Tower" title="Goethe Tower">Goethe Tower</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_Frankfurt" title="List of tallest buildings in Frankfurt">Frankfurt's skyline</a> in the background (2007)</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Deutsche_Bank_Taunusanlage.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Deutsche_Bank_Taunusanlage.jpg/220px-Deutsche_Bank_Taunusanlage.jpg" width="220" height="322" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Deutsche_Bank_Taunusanlage.jpg/330px-Deutsche_Bank_Taunusanlage.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Deutsche_Bank_Taunusanlage.jpg/440px-Deutsche_Bank_Taunusanlage.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3084" data-file-height="4517" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Deutsche_Bank_Taunusanlage.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Wallanlagen" title="Wallanlagen">Wallanlagen</a> with <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bank_Twin_Towers" title="Deutsche Bank Twin Towers">Deutsche Bank Twin Towers</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>With a large forest, many parks, the Main riverbanks and the two botanical gardens, Frankfurt is considered a "green city": More than 50 percent of the area within the city limits are protected green areas.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><b>Frankfurter Grüngürtel</b> – The Green Belt is a ring-shaped public green space around the city. With 8,000 <a href="/wiki/Hectare" title="Hectare">ha</a> it covers a third of the administrative area. It includes the Frankfurter Stadtwald (<i><a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_City_Forest" title="Frankfurt City Forest">Frankfurt City Forest</a></i>, Germany's largest forest within a city), the Schwanheimer Düne (<i><a href="/wiki/Schwanheim_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Schwanheim (Frankfurt am Main)">Schwanheim</a> <a href="/wiki/Dune" title="Dune">Dune</a></i>), the Niddatal (<i><a href="/wiki/Nidda_(river)" title="Nidda (river)">Nidda</a> <a href="/wiki/Valley" title="Valley">Valley</a></i>), the Niddapark, the Lohrberg (<i>Lohr Mountain</i>, Frankfurt's only <a href="/wiki/Vineyard" title="Vineyard">vineyard</a>), the Huthpark, the Enkheimer Ried (<i><a href="/wiki/Frankfurt-Bergen-Enkheim" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankfurt-Bergen-Enkheim">Enkheim</a> <a href="/wiki/Marsh" title="Marsh">Marsh</a></i>), the Seckbacher Ried (<i><a href="/wiki/Seckbach_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Seckbach (Frankfurt am Main)">Seckbach</a> <a href="/wiki/Marsh" title="Marsh">Marsh</a></i>) and the Fechenheimer Mainbogen (a S-shaped part of the <a href="/wiki/Main_(river)" title="Main (river)">Main</a> river in <a href="/wiki/Fechenheim_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" class="mw-redirect" title="Fechenheim (Frankfurt am Main)">Fechenheim</a>). The Green Belt is a <a href="/wiki/Protected_area" title="Protected area">protected area</a> which means that housing is not allowed. The Green Belt was formally created in 1991 with its own constitution.</li>
<li><b>Mainuferpark</b> – The Mainuferpark (<i>Main Riverbanks Park</i>) is the common term to describe the inner-city Main riverbanks. It is an auto-free zone with large green areas that is popular with strollers and tourists, especially in the summertime, when it can become crowded. The southern riverbank, which continues further to <a href="/wiki/Offenbach_am_Main" title="Offenbach am Main">Offenbach am Main</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hanau" title="Hanau">Hanau</a>, offers the best skyline views. The northern riverbank ends in the west at the former Westhafen (<i>West Harbour</i>, a residential housing area) and is growing to the east: A former industrial-used area between the future <a href="/wiki/Seat_of_the_European_Central_Bank" title="Seat of the European Central Bank">Seat of the European Central Bank</a> and the Osthafen (<i>East Harbour</i>) was to become a park named Hafenpark (<i>Harbour Park</i>).</li>
<li><b>Wallanlagen</b> – The <a href="/wiki/Wallanlagen" title="Wallanlagen">Wallanlagen</a> (former <i><a href="/wiki/Defensive_wall" title="Defensive wall">ramparts</a></i>) relate to the former ring-shaped <a href="/wiki/Defensive_wall" title="Defensive wall">city wall fortifications</a> around the <a href="/wiki/Altstadt_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Altstadt (Frankfurt am Main)">Altstadt</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Innenstadt_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Innenstadt (Frankfurt am Main)">Innenstadt</a> district (abolished 1804–1812), now a series of parks. Building is not allowed, with a few exceptions, the most famous being the <a href="/wiki/Alte_Oper" title="Alte Oper">Alte Oper</a> (built 1880) at the Opernplatz. The part between the northern Main riverbank and the Opernplatz, referred to officially as Taunusanlage and Gallusanlage, is locally known as "Central Park" (a reference to the <a href="/wiki/Central_Park" title="Central Park">famous park</a> in <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">Manhattan</a>), because of the skyscrapers which stand on both sides.</li>
<li><b>Nizza Park</b> – At the juncture of the northern Main riverbank and the Wallanlagen is a famous small park called Nizza. The name of the park recalls <a href="/wiki/Nice" title="Nice">Nice</a> in southern France, because it is one of the warmest areas with a nearly <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">mediterranean climate</a>. Numerous <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_flora" class="mw-redirect" title="Mediterranean flora">Mediterranean flora</a> grow there and can survive outside during the winter.</li>
<li><b>Garten des Himmlischen Friedens</b> – <i>Garden of Heavenly Peace</i>, named after the <a href="/wiki/Tiananmen_Square" title="Tiananmen Square">Tiananmen Gate</a> in Beijing, is a Chinese-styled park in the <a href="/wiki/Nordend_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Nordend (Frankfurt am Main)">Nordend</a> district and part of the larger Bethmannpark. It contains Chinese buildings, with building materials imported from China and built by Chinese workers in the 1980s. Hosts traditional Chinese plants and herbs.</li>
<li><b>Other parks</b> – The largest parks are the Niddapark (168 ha), the Ostpark (32 ha) and the <a href="/wiki/Gr%C3%BCneburgpark" title="Grüneburgpark">Grüneburgpark</a> (29 ha).</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums">Museums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Museums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FrankfurtM_Staedel.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/FrankfurtM_Staedel.jpg/220px-FrankfurtM_Staedel.jpg" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/FrankfurtM_Staedel.jpg/330px-FrankfurtM_Staedel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/FrankfurtM_Staedel.jpg/440px-FrankfurtM_Staedel.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1749" data-file-height="1251" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FrankfurtM_Staedel.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/St%C3%A4del" class="mw-redirect" title="Städel">Städel</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Schirn-ffm001.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Schirn-ffm001.jpg/220px-Schirn-ffm001.jpg" width="220" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Schirn-ffm001.jpg/330px-Schirn-ffm001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Schirn-ffm001.jpg/440px-Schirn-ffm001.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2740" data-file-height="2012" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Schirn-ffm001.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Schirn_Kunsthalle_Frankfurt" title="Schirn Kunsthalle Frankfurt">Schirn Art Gallery</a> from above</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Frankfurt_Am_Main-Senckenberg_Naturmuseum_von_Osten-20120325.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Frankfurt_Am_Main-Senckenberg_Naturmuseum_von_Osten-20120325.jpg/220px-Frankfurt_Am_Main-Senckenberg_Naturmuseum_von_Osten-20120325.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Frankfurt_Am_Main-Senckenberg_Naturmuseum_von_Osten-20120325.jpg/330px-Frankfurt_Am_Main-Senckenberg_Naturmuseum_von_Osten-20120325.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Frankfurt_Am_Main-Senckenberg_Naturmuseum_von_Osten-20120325.jpg/440px-Frankfurt_Am_Main-Senckenberg_Naturmuseum_von_Osten-20120325.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5000" data-file-height="3333" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Frankfurt_Am_Main-Senckenberg_Naturmuseum_von_Osten-20120325.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Naturmuseum_Senckenberg" title="Naturmuseum Senckenberg">Senckenberg Natural History Museum</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>With more than 30 museums, Frankfurt has one of the largest variety of museums in Europe. 20 museums are part of the <a href="/wiki/Museumsufer" title="Museumsufer">Museumsufer</a> (<i>Museums Riverbank</i>), located on the front row of both sides of the <a href="/wiki/Main_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Main River">Main</a> riverbank or nearby.</p>
<p>Ten museums are located on the southern riverbank in <a href="/wiki/Sachsenhausen_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Sachsenhausen (Frankfurt am Main)">Sachsenhausen</a> between the Eiserner Steg and the Friedensbrücke. The street itself, <a href="/wiki/Schaumainkai" title="Schaumainkai">Schaumainkai</a>, is partially closed to traffic on Saturdays for Frankfurt's largest <a href="/wiki/Flea_market" title="Flea market">flea market</a>.</p>
<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/German_Architecture_Museum" title="German Architecture Museum">Deutsches Architekturmuseum</a></b> (German Architecture Museum)</li>
<li><b>Deutsches Filmmuseum</b> (German Film Museum)</li>
<li><b>Frankfurter Ikonenmuseum</b> (Icon Museum Frankfurt)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Liebieghaus" title="Liebieghaus">Liebieghaus</a> (Museum of Municipal Sculptures)</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Museum_f%C3%BCr_Angewandte_Kunst" class="mw-redirect" title="Museum für Angewandte Kunst">Museum für Angewandte Kunst</a></b> (Museum of Applied Arts)</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Museum_Giersch" title="Museum Giersch">Museum Giersch</a></b> (Museum for Regional Art)</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Museum_f%C3%BCr_Kommunikation_Frankfurt" title="Museum für Kommunikation Frankfurt">Museum für Kommunikation</a></b> (Museum of Communications)</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Museum_der_Weltkulturen" title="Museum der Weltkulturen">Museum der Weltkulturen</a></b> (Museum of World Cultures)</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/St%C3%A4del" class="mw-redirect" title="Städel">Städel</a></b>, one of the most famous art museums in Germany</li>
<li><b>Bibelhaus Erlebnis Museum</b> (Bible House Experience Museum)</li>
</ul>
<p>Two museums are located on the northern riverbank:</p>
<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Jewish_Museum_Frankfurt" title="Jewish Museum Frankfurt">Jüdisches Museum Frankfurt</a></b> (Jewish Museum Frankfurt)</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Historical_museum,_Frankfurt" class="mw-redirect" title="Historical museum, Frankfurt">Historisches Museum Frankfurt</a></b> (Historical Museum Frankfurt)</li>
</ul>
<p>Not directly located on the northern riverbank in the <a href="/wiki/Altstadt_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Altstadt (Frankfurt am Main)">Altstadt</a> district are:</p>
<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Museum_f%C3%BCr_Moderne_Kunst" title="Museum für Moderne Kunst">Museum für Moderne Kunst</a></b> (Museum of Modern Art)</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Schirn_Kunsthalle_Frankfurt" title="Schirn Kunsthalle Frankfurt">Schirn Kunsthalle Frankfurt</a></b> (Schirn Art Gallery Frankfurt)</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Frankfurter_Kunstverein" title="Frankfurter Kunstverein">Frankfurter Kunstverein</a></b> (Art Association Frankfurt)</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Frankfurter_Judengasse" title="Frankfurter Judengasse">Museum Judengasse</a></b> (Jews' Alley Museum)</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Goethe_House" title="Goethe House">Goethe-Haus</a></b> (Goethe House)</li>
<li><b>Archäologisches Museum Frankfurt</b> (Archaeological Museum Frankfurt)</li>
<li><b>Caricatura Museum für Komische Kunst</b> (Caricatura Museum of Comical Art)</li>
<li><b>Dommuseum Frankfurt</b> (Frankfurt Cathedral Museum)</li>
</ul>
<p>Another important museum is located in the <a href="/wiki/Westend_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Westend (Frankfurt am Main)">Westend</a> district:</p>
<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Naturmuseum_Senckenberg" title="Naturmuseum Senckenberg">Naturmuseum Senckenberg</a></b> (Senckenberg Natural History Museum), the second largest <a href="/wiki/Natural_history" title="Natural history">natural history</a> museum in Germany</li>
</ul>
<p>Other museums are the <b>Dialogmuseum</b> (Dialogue Museum) in the <a href="/wiki/Ostend_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Ostend (Frankfurt am Main)">Ostend</a> district, <b><a href="/wiki/Eintracht_Frankfurt" title="Eintracht Frankfurt">Eintracht Frankfurt</a> Museum</b> at <a href="/wiki/Commerzbank-Arena" title="Commerzbank-Arena">Commerzbank-Arena</a>, <b>Explora Museum+Wissenschaft+Technik</b> (Explora Museum of Science and Engineering) in the <a href="/wiki/Nordend_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Nordend (Frankfurt am Main)">Nordend</a> district, the <b>Frankfurter Feldbahnmuseum e.V.</b> (Light Railway Museum Frankfurt) in the <a href="/wiki/Gallus_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Gallus (Frankfurt am Main)">Gallus</a> district, the <b>Verkehrsmuseum Frankfurt</b> (Transport Museum Frankfurt) in the <a href="/wiki/Schwanheim_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Schwanheim (Frankfurt am Main)">Schwanheim</a> district, the <b>Hammer Museum</b> in the <a href="/wiki/Bahnhofsviertel_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bahnhofsviertel (Frankfurt am Main)">Bahnhofsviertel</a> district and the <b>Geldmuseum der Deutschen Bundesbank</b> (Money Museum of the German Federal Bank) in the <a href="/wiki/Ginnheim_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ginnheim (Frankfurt am Main)">Ginnheim</a> district.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Performing_arts">Performing arts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Performing arts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Festhalle-Frankfurt-am-Main-2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Festhalle-Frankfurt-am-Main-2.jpg/220px-Festhalle-Frankfurt-am-Main-2.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Festhalle-Frankfurt-am-Main-2.jpg/330px-Festhalle-Frankfurt-am-Main-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Festhalle-Frankfurt-am-Main-2.jpg/440px-Festhalle-Frankfurt-am-Main-2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="763" data-file-height="510" /></a>
