<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Eurodance" title="Eurodance">Eurodance</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trance_music" title="Trance music">Trance music</a> originated in Frankfurt. In 1989 German producers Michael Münzing and Luca Anzilotti (under the pseudonyms Benito Benites and John "Virgo" Garrett III) formed the <a href="/wiki/Snap!" title="Snap!">Snap!</a> project. Snap! songs combined <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">Rap</a> and <a href="/wiki/Soul_music" title="Soul music">Soul</a> vocals adding rhythm by using computer technology and mixing electronic sounds, bass and drums. By doing so a new genre was born: Eurodance.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> In the early 1990s, DJs including <a href="/wiki/Sven_V%C3%A4th" title="Sven Väth">Sven Väth</a> and DJ DAG (of <a href="/wiki/Dance_2_Trance" title="Dance 2 Trance">Dance 2 Trance</a>) first played a harder, deeper style of <a href="/wiki/Acid_house" title="Acid house">acid house</a> that became popular worldwide over the next decade as Trance music. Some of the early and most influential Eurodance, Trance and <a href="/wiki/Techno_music" class="mw-redirect" title="Techno music">Techno</a> acts, e.g., <a href="/wiki/La_Bouche" title="La Bouche">La Bouche</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jam_and_Spoon" class="mw-redirect" title="Jam and Spoon">Jam and Spoon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Magic_Affair" title="Magic Affair">Magic Affair</a>, <a href="/wiki/Culture_Beat" title="Culture Beat">Culture Beat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Snap!" title="Snap!">Snap!</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dance_2_Trance" title="Dance 2 Trance">Dance 2 Trance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Lieb" title="Oliver Lieb">Oliver Lieb</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hardfloor" title="Hardfloor">Hardfloor</a>, and record labels such as <a href="/wiki/Harthouse" title="Harthouse">Harthouse</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eye_Q_(record_label)" title="Eye Q (record label)">Eye Q</a>, were based in the city in the early 1990s.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Venues">Venues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Venues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Opern-_und_Schauspielhaus_Frankfurt" title="Opern- und Schauspielhaus Frankfurt">Oper Frankfurt</a></b> – A leading Germany opera company and one of Europe's most important. It was elected <i><a href="/wiki/Opera_house_of_the_year" class="mw-redirect" title="Opera house of the year">Opera house of the year</a></i> (of Germany, Austria and German-speaking Switzerland) by German magazine <a href="/wiki/Opernwelt" title="Opernwelt">Opernwelt</a> in 1995, 1996 and 2003. It was also elected <i>Best opera house in Germany</i> in 2010 and 2011. Its orchestra was voted <i>Orchestra of the year</i> in 2009, 2010 and 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Opern-_und_Schauspielhaus_Frankfurt" title="Opern- und Schauspielhaus Frankfurt">Schauspiel Frankfurt</a></b> – Theatre at Willy-Brandt-Platz in the financial district, next to the Frankfurt Opera.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Radio_Symphony" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankfurt Radio Symphony">Frankfurt Radio Symphony</a></b> (<a href="/wiki/Hr-Sinfonieorchester" title="Hr-Sinfonieorchester">hr-Sinfonieorchester</a> in German) – one of the top symphony orchestras in the world</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Festhalle_Frankfurt" title="Festhalle Frankfurt">Festhalle Frankfurt</a></b> – Multi-purpose hall next to the <a href="/wiki/Messeturm" title="Messeturm">Messeturm</a> at the grounds of the <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Trade_Fair" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankfurt Trade Fair">Frankfurt Trade Fair</a>. It is mostly used for concerts, exhibitions or sport events and can accommodate up to 13,500.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Commerzbank-Arena" title="Commerzbank-Arena">Commerzbank-Arena</a></b> – Frankfurt's largest sports stadium and one of Germany's ten largest. It is located in the <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_City_Forest" title="Frankfurt City Forest">Frankfurt City Forest</a> near <a href="/wiki/Niederrad" title="Niederrad">Niederrad</a>. It is primarily used for soccer and concerts with a capacity up to 51,500. It opened in 1925 and underwent several major reconstructions. Locals still prefer to call the stadium by its traditional name, <b>Waldstadion</b> (<i>Forest Stadium</i>).</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Alte_Oper" title="Alte Oper">Alte Oper</a></b> – A major concert hall.</li>
<li><b>Jahrhunderthalle</b> – <i>Century Hall</i> is a large concert and exhibition hall in <a href="/wiki/Unterliederbach_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" class="mw-redirect" title="Unterliederbach (Frankfurt am Main)">Unterliederbach</a> district. Sometimes referred to as "Jahrhunderthalle Höchst", because it was built to celebrate the 100th anniversary of the chemical company <a href="/wiki/Hoechst_AG" title="Hoechst AG">Hoechst AG</a> in 1963.</li>
<li><b>The English Theatre</b> – Located on the ground floor of the <a href="/wiki/Gallileo_(skyscraper)" title="Gallileo (skyscraper)">Gallileo</a> high-rise building, this is the largest anglophone theatre in continental Europe. It was established in 1979.</li>
<li><b>Tigerpalast</b> – <i>Tiger Palace</i> is a <a href="/wiki/Variet%C3%A9" class="mw-redirect" title="Varieté">varieté</a> in the city centre near the Zeil. It was established in 1988 and houses the famous Tiger-Restaurant which was awarded a <a href="/wiki/Michelin_Guide" title="Michelin Guide">Michelin star</a>.</li>
<li><b>Künstlerhaus Mousonturm</b> – <i>House of Artists Mouson Tower</i> is a free theatre, which means that it has a smaller budget than traditional theatres and used more unconventional performing methods. It is located in an old factory in the <a href="/wiki/Ostend_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Ostend (Frankfurt am Main)">Ostend</a> district.</li>
<li><b>Die Schmiere</b> – <i>The Grease</i> is a <a href="/wiki/Cabaret" title="Cabaret">cabaret</a> and Frankfurt's oldest privately owned theatre. It is located in the Karmeliterkloster in the <a href="/wiki/Altstadt_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Altstadt (Frankfurt am Main)">Altstadt</a> district. According to its own advertising it is <i>the worst theatre in the world</i>.</li>
<li><b>Die Komödie</b> – <i>The Comedy</i> is a <a href="/wiki/Boulevard_theatre_(aesthetic)" title="Boulevard theatre (aesthetic)">boulevard theatre</a> in the city centre near Willy-Brandt-Platz.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Botanical_gardens">Botanical gardens</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Botanical gardens">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Palmengarten-ffm-Haus_Rosenbrunn-002.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Palmengarten-ffm-Haus_Rosenbrunn-002.jpg/220px-Palmengarten-ffm-Haus_Rosenbrunn-002.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Palmengarten-ffm-Haus_Rosenbrunn-002.jpg/330px-Palmengarten-ffm-Haus_Rosenbrunn-002.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Palmengarten-ffm-Haus_Rosenbrunn-002.jpg/440px-Palmengarten-ffm-Haus_Rosenbrunn-002.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2744" data-file-height="2052" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Palmengarten-ffm-Haus_Rosenbrunn-002.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Palmengarten</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Frankfurt is home to two major botanical gardens.</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Palmengarten" title="Palmengarten">Palmengarten</a> – Located in the <a href="/wiki/Westend_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Westend (Frankfurt am Main)">Westend</a> district, it is Hesse's largest botanical garden covering 22 <a href="/wiki/Hectare" title="Hectare">ha</a>. It opened to the public in 1871. The botanical exhibits are organized according to their origin in free-air or in greenhouses that host tropical and subtropical plants, hence the name "<a href="/wiki/Arecaceae" title="Arecaceae">Palm</a> Garden".</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Botanischer_Garten_der_Johann_Wolfgang_Goethe-Universit%C3%A4t_Frankfurt_am_Main" class="mw-redirect" title="Botanischer Garten der Johann Wolfgang Goethe-Universität Frankfurt am Main">Botanischer Garten der Goethe-Universität</a></b> – The university's botanical garden is also an <a href="/wiki/Arboretum" title="Arboretum">arboretum</a>. It contains about 5,000 <a href="/wiki/Species" title="Species">species</a>, with special collections of <i><a href="/wiki/Rubus" title="Rubus">Rubus</a></i> (45 <a href="/wiki/Species" title="Species">species</a>) and indigenous plants of central Europe. It is organized into two major areas: The <a href="/wiki/Geobotany" class="mw-redirect" title="Geobotany">geobotanical</a> area contains an <a href="/wiki/Alpine_garden" title="Alpine garden">alpine garden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arboretum" title="Arboretum">arboretum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Meadow" title="Meadow">meadows</a>, <a href="/wiki/Steppe" title="Steppe">steppes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marsh" title="Marsh">marsh</a>, and a pond, as well as collections of plants from the <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">Canary Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasus</a>, East Asia, <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean" class="mw-redirect" title="Mediterranean">Mediterranean</a>, and North America and the systematic and ecological collection includes crop plants, <a href="/wiki/Endangered_species" title="Endangered species">endangered species</a>, ornamental plants, <a href="/wiki/Rose" title="Rose">roses</a>, and the <i>Neuer Senckenbergischer Arzneipflanzengarten</i> (New Senckenberg Medicinal Plant Garden, 1200 m²). The Botanical Garden, the neighbouring Palmengarten and the neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Gr%C3%BCneburgpark" title="Grüneburgpark">Grüneburgpark</a> form the largest inner-city green area.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_culture">Foreign culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Foreign culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Instituto-cervantes-ffm003.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Instituto-cervantes-ffm003.jpg/220px-Instituto-cervantes-ffm003.jpg" width="220" height="134" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Instituto-cervantes-ffm003.jpg/330px-Instituto-cervantes-ffm003.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Instituto-cervantes-ffm003.jpg/440px-Instituto-cervantes-ffm003.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2829" data-file-height="1723" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Instituto-cervantes-ffm003.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Amerika-Haus Frankfurt</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Instituto_Cervantes" title="Instituto Cervantes">Instituto Cervantes</a></b> – Named after <a href="/wiki/Miguel_de_Cervantes" title="Miguel de Cervantes">Miguel de Cervantes</a>, one of the most important Spanish authors, this is the world's largest organization for promoting the study and teaching of Spanish language and culture. 54 such Centros Cervantes across the world offer Spanish language and history courses. The Frankfurt branch was officially opened in September 2008 by <a href="/wiki/Felipe_VI_of_Spain" title="Felipe VI of Spain">Felipe, Prince of Asturias</a> and his wife <a href="/wiki/Letizia_of_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Letizia of Spain">Letizia, Princess of Asturias</a>. It is located in the so-called <i>Amerika-Haus</i>.<a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://frankfurt.cervantes.es/">[2]</a></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Institut_Fran%C3%A7ais" title="Institut Français">Institut Français</a></b> – A French public industrial and commercial organization (EPIC), started in 1907 by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for promoting French, francophone as well as local cultures around the world. The French Institute works closely with the French cultural network abroad consisting of more than 150 branches and nearly 1000 branches of the <a href="/wiki/Alliance_fran%C3%A7aise" class="mw-redirect" title="Alliance française">Alliance française</a> around the world.<a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://frankfurt.institutfrancais.de/">[3]</a></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Istituto_Italiano_di_Cultura" title="Istituto Italiano di Cultura">Istituto Italiano di Cultura</a></b> – A worldwide non-profit organization created by the Italian government. It promotes Italian culture and is involved in the teaching of the Italian language; there are 83 Italian Cultural Institutes throughout major cities around the world.<a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.iic-frankfurt.de/">[4]</a></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Confucius_Institute" title="Confucius Institute">Confucius Institute</a></b> – A non-profit public educational organization affiliated with the Ministry of Education of the People's Republic of China,[2] whose aim is to promote Chinese language and culture, support local Chinese teaching internationally, and facilitate cultural exchanges. There are over 480 Confucius Institutes worldwide.<a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.konfuzius-institut-frankfurt.de/">[5]</a></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Central_and_Eastern_European_Online_Library" title="Central and Eastern European Online Library">Central and Eastern European Online Library</a></b> – CEEOL is an online archive providing access to full text articles from humanities and social science scholarly journals on Central, Eastern and South Eastern European topics. Subject areas include anthropology, culture and society, economy, gender studies, history, Judaic studies, fine arts, literature, linguistics, political sciences and social sciences, philosophy and religion. CEEOL is operated by Questa.Soft GmbH.<a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://www.ceeol.com/">[6]</a></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Festivals">Festivals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Festivals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Museumsuferfest_2005_-_Riesenrad.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Museumsuferfest_2005_-_Riesenrad.jpg/220px-Museumsuferfest_2005_-_Riesenrad.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Museumsuferfest_2005_-_Riesenrad.jpg/330px-Museumsuferfest_2005_-_Riesenrad.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Museumsuferfest_2005_-_Riesenrad.jpg/440px-Museumsuferfest_2005_-_Riesenrad.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1333" data-file-height="1000" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Museumsuferfest_2005_-_Riesenrad.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Museumsuferfest in 2005</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Frankfurt-Waeldchestag.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Frankfurt-Waeldchestag.jpg/220px-Frankfurt-Waeldchestag.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Frankfurt-Waeldchestag.jpg/330px-Frankfurt-Waeldchestag.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Frankfurt-Waeldchestag.jpg/440px-Frankfurt-Waeldchestag.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Frankfurt-Waeldchestag.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Wäldchestag in 2002</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Luminale_2012_-_OVO.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Luminale_2012_-_OVO.jpg/220px-Luminale_2012_-_OVO.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Luminale_2012_-_OVO.jpg/330px-Luminale_2012_-_OVO.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Luminale_2012_-_OVO.jpg/440px-Luminale_2012_-_OVO.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5342" data-file-height="3575" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Luminale_2012_-_OVO.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
"OVO" at Luminale 2012</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><b>Museumsuferfest</b> – <i>Museums Riverbank Festival</i> is one of Germany's biggest cultural festivals, attracting more than 3 million visitors over three days at the end of August along the <a href="/wiki/Main_(river)" title="Main (river)">Main</a> riverbank in the city centre. The 20 museums there open far into the night. It offers live music, dance shows, booths for crafts, jewellery, clothes and food stands from around the world.</li>
<li><b>Dippemess</b> – Frankfurt's oldest folk festival is the <i>Festival of Stoneware</i>, which takes place semi-annually around Easter and the end of September in the eastern area. "Dippe" is a regional <a href="/wiki/Hessian_dialects" title="Hessian dialects">Hessian dialect</a> word meaning "pot" or "jar" which would not be understood in most other German regions. Mentioned for the first time in the 14th century as an annual marketplace it is now more of an amusement park. The name of the festival derives from its original purpose, when it was a fair where traditionally crafted jars, pots and other stoneware were on offer.</li>
<li><b>Wäldchestag</b> – <i>Day of the forest</i> is known as a regional holiday because until the 1990s it was common that Frankfurt's shops were closed on this day. The festival takes place over four days after <a href="/wiki/Pentecost" title="Pentecost">Pentecost</a> with the formal Wäldchestag on Tuesday. Its unique location is in the <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_City_Forest" title="Frankfurt City Forest">Frankfurt City Forest</a>, south-west of the city centre in <a href="/wiki/Niederrad" title="Niederrad">Niederrad</a>. "Wäldches" is a regional dialect of the German word "Wäldchen", meaning "small forest".</li>
<li><b>Nacht der Museen</b> – <i>Night of the museums</i> takes place every year in April or May. 50 museums in Frankfurt and in the neighbouring city of <a href="/wiki/Offenbach_am_Main" title="Offenbach am Main">Offenbach am Main</a> are open until 2:00&#160;am surrounded by special music events, dance performances, readings and guided tours. A free shuttle operates between the museums. In 2010, approximately 40,000 visitors attended.</li>
<li><b>Nacht der Clubs</b> – <i>Night of the clubs</i> is an event similar to Nacht der Museen: On one night as many as 20 clubs can be visited with a single ticket for €12. Usually club-door-policies are loosened to attract new customers. A free shuttle runs between the clubs. 15,000 people participated in 2008.</li>
<li><b>Luminale</b> — The "festival of light" takes place biannually since 2000, parallel to the <i>Light + building</i> exhibition at the trade fair. Many buildings are specially lit for the event. In 2008, more than 220 light installations could be seen and attracted 100,000 visitors. The last Luminale was held in April 2012.</li>
<li><b>Wolkenkratzer Festival</b> — The <i>Skyscraper Festival</i> is unique in Germany. It takes place irregularly, lately in May 2013, and attracted around 1.2 million visitors. For two days most skyscrapers are open to the public. Sky-divers, base jumpers, fireworks and laser shows are extra attractions.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nightlife">Nightlife</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Nightlife">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CocoonClub_-_public_coccon.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/CocoonClub_-_public_coccon.jpg/220px-CocoonClub_-_public_coccon.jpg" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/CocoonClub_-_public_coccon.jpg/330px-CocoonClub_-_public_coccon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/CocoonClub_-_public_coccon.jpg/440px-CocoonClub_-_public_coccon.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2811" data-file-height="1932" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CocoonClub_-_public_coccon.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Cocoon Club</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Frankfurt_Main_Japan_Tower_6240a.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Frankfurt_Main_Japan_Tower_6240a.jpg/220px-Frankfurt_Main_Japan_Tower_6240a.jpg" width="220" height="390" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Frankfurt_Main_Japan_Tower_6240a.jpg/330px-Frankfurt_Main_Japan_Tower_6240a.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Frankfurt_Main_Japan_Tower_6240a.jpg/440px-Frankfurt_Main_Japan_Tower_6240a.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1674" data-file-height="2968" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Frankfurt_Main_Japan_Tower_6240a.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Japan Center, home of Club 101</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Frankfurt offers a variety of restaurants, bars, pubs and clubs. Clubs concentrate in and around the city centre and in the <a href="/wiki/Ostend_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Ostend (Frankfurt am Main)">Ostend</a> district, mainly close to Hanauer Landstraße. Restaurants, bars and pubs concentrate in <a href="/wiki/Sachsenhausen_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Sachsenhausen (Frankfurt am Main)">Sachsenhausen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nordend_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Nordend (Frankfurt am Main)">Nordend</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bornheim_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Bornheim (Frankfurt am Main)">Bornheim</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bockenheim_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Bockenheim (Frankfurt am Main)">Bockenheim</a>.</p>
<p>One of the main venues of the early <a href="/wiki/Trance_music" title="Trance music">Trance music</a> sound was the <a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Omen_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" class="extiw" title="de:Omen (Frankfurt am Main)">Omen nightclub</a> (closed 1998). Another popular disco club of the 1980-1990s and a hotspot for Techno/Trance music was the <a href="/wiki/Dorian_Gray_(club)" title="Dorian Gray (club)">Dorian Gray</a>, located within Terminal 1 at Frankfurt Airport. Because of the location at the airport the club had no restrictions regarding opening hours. The club had to close at the end of 2000 because of stricter <a href="/wiki/Fire_safety" title="Fire safety">fire safety</a> regulations. Also notable for its extraordinary design was <a href="/wiki/Cocoon_(club)" title="Cocoon (club)">Coocoon Club</a> in <a href="/wiki/Fechenheim_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" class="mw-redirect" title="Fechenheim (Frankfurt am Main)">Fechenheim</a> which opened in 2004 was and voted <i>best techno club of the year</i> by music magazines "Groove" and "Raveline" in 2004, 2005, 2006 and 2007. It closed in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/King_Kamehameha_Club" class="extiw" title="de:King Kamehameha Club"><b>King Kamehameha Club</b></a> – named after the <a href="/wiki/Kamehameha_I" title="Kamehameha I">first king of Hawaii</a> and a fictional Club in <a href="/wiki/Magnum,_P.I." title="Magnum, P.I.">Magnum, P.I.</a>, was a disco club at Hanauer Landstraße, known for live music. It opened in 1999 and expanded with a beach club in <a href="/wiki/Offenbach_am_Main" title="Offenbach am Main">Offenbach am Main</a> and a restaurant (King Kamehameha Suite) in the financial district. The club closed in 2013, although the King Kamehameha Suite is still open.</li>
<li><a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/U60311" class="extiw" title="de:U60311"><b>U60311</b></a> – Techno club in the city centre. "60311" is the <a href="/wiki/Postal_code" title="Postal code">postal code</a> of the area. It was voted <i>best club of the year</i> by music magazines "Groove" and "Raveline" multiple times. Its location was an underground former pedestrian underpass. It closed in 2012.</li>
<li><b>Living XXL</b> – Club/restaurant in the financial district, it was located on the ground floor of the <a href="/wiki/Eurotower_(Frankfurt)" class="mw-redirect" title="Eurotower (Frankfurt)">Eurotower</a> and closed in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></li>
<li><b>Club 101</b> — Located on the 24th floor of the <a href="/wiki/Japan_Center_(Frankfurt)" title="Japan Center (Frankfurt)">Japan Center</a>. It closed at the end of 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Batschkapp-2014-Gwinnerstrasse-Ffm-Seckbach-726-728.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Batschkapp-2014-Gwinnerstrasse-Ffm-Seckbach-726-728.jpg/220px-Batschkapp-2014-Gwinnerstrasse-Ffm-Seckbach-726-728.jpg" width="220" height="55" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Batschkapp-2014-Gwinnerstrasse-Ffm-Seckbach-726-728.jpg/330px-Batschkapp-2014-Gwinnerstrasse-Ffm-Seckbach-726-728.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Batschkapp-2014-Gwinnerstrasse-Ffm-Seckbach-726-728.jpg/440px-Batschkapp-2014-Gwinnerstrasse-Ffm-Seckbach-726-728.jpg 2x" data-file-width="9312" data-file-height="2344" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Batschkapp-2014-Gwinnerstrasse-Ffm-Seckbach-726-728.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Batschkapp, 2014</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Batschkapp" title="Batschkapp">Batschkapp</a></b> – Alternative rock club, located in Frankfurt-Seckbach. It opened in 1976 and attracts mostly people with a left-wing political attitude<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>. <a href="/wiki/Joschka_Fischer" title="Joschka Fischer">Joschka Fischer</a>, Germany's former Foreign Minister, was a regular guest in the 1980s.</li>
<li><b>Velvet Club</b> (<a href="/wiki/Innenstadt_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Innenstadt (Frankfurt am Main)">Innenstadt</a>)</li>
<li><b>Cooky's</b> (Innenstadt)</li>
<li><b>Nachtleben</b> (Innenstadt)</li>
<li><b>Silbergold</b> (Innenstadt)</li>
<li><a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sinkkasten_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" class="extiw" title="de:Sinkkasten (Frankfurt am Main)"><b>Sinkkasten Arts Club</b></a> (Innenstadt) – Closed in 2012, replaced by Zoom club.</li>
<li><b>Tanzhaus West</b> (<a href="/wiki/Gutleutviertel" title="Gutleutviertel">Gutleutviertel</a>)</li>
<li><b>Dora Brillant</b> (Gutleutviertel)</li>
<li><b>Odeon</b> (<a href="/wiki/Nordend,_Frankfurt" class="mw-redirect" title="Nordend, Frankfurt">Nordend</a>)</li>
<li><b>Monza</b> (Innenstadt) – Closed in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></li>
<li><b>Travolta</b> (Innenstadt)</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Domestic_culture">Domestic culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Domestic culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Frankfurter-kueche-vienna.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Frankfurter-kueche-vienna.JPG/170px-Frankfurter-kueche-vienna.JPG" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Frankfurter-kueche-vienna.JPG/255px-Frankfurter-kueche-vienna.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Frankfurter-kueche-vienna.JPG/340px-Frankfurter-kueche-vienna.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2112" data-file-height="2816" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Frankfurter-kueche-vienna.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A "Frankfurt kitchen" in the version of 1926 in an Austrian museum</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_kitchen" title="Frankfurt kitchen">Frankfurt kitchen</a> – Designed originally in 1926 for the <a href="/wiki/New_Frankfurt" title="New Frankfurt">New Frankfurt</a>-project and built in some 10,000 units, the kitchen became a milestone in domestic architecture, considered the forerunner of modern fitted kitchens.</li>
<li>Frankfurt cupboard – The Baroque Frankfurt-style cupboards were used to store the family linen, one of them by Goethe's father, who took one cupboard to Rome. The most luxurius versions have wave-shaped parts, some are made of solid cherry wood inlaid with plumwood.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Culinary_specialties">Culinary specialties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Culinary specialties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Hessian_cuisine" title="Hessian cuisine">Hessian cuisine</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Apfelwein_Geripptes_Bembel.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Apfelwein_Geripptes_Bembel.jpg/220px-Apfelwein_Geripptes_Bembel.jpg" width="220" height="206" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Apfelwein_Geripptes_Bembel.jpg/330px-Apfelwein_Geripptes_Bembel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Apfelwein_Geripptes_Bembel.jpg/440px-Apfelwein_Geripptes_Bembel.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2121" data-file-height="1983" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Apfelwein_Geripptes_Bembel.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
"Bembel" and "Geripptes"</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Frankfurter-rippchen-mit-kraut-kpl.001-1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Frankfurter-rippchen-mit-kraut-kpl.001-1.jpg/220px-Frankfurter-rippchen-mit-kraut-kpl.001-1.jpg" width="220" height="194" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Frankfurter-rippchen-mit-kraut-kpl.001-1.jpg/330px-Frankfurter-rippchen-mit-kraut-kpl.001-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Frankfurter-rippchen-mit-kraut-kpl.001-1.jpg/440px-Frankfurter-rippchen-mit-kraut-kpl.001-1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2268" data-file-height="1999" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Frankfurter-rippchen-mit-kraut-kpl.001-1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Frankfurter Rippchen</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Apfelwein" title="Apfelwein">Apfelwein</a></b> – <i>Apple wine</i> or <i>hard cider</i> is regionally known as "Ebbelwoi", "Äppler" or "Stöffsche". It has an alcohol content of 5.5%–7% and a tart, sour taste. It is traditionally served in a glass, typically decorated with lozenges, called "Geripptes", a full glass is then called "Schoppen". Apfelwein is also available in a stoneware jar locally known as "Bembel". A group normally orders a "Bembel" and shares the content. Apfelwein can be ordered as "sauergespritzer", which is apfelwein blended with 30% mineral water or as "süssgespritzer", which is Apfelwein blended with lemon soda, orange soda or fresh-pressed apple juice (lemon soda being the most common). Most of the pubs which serve Apfelwein are located in <a href="/wiki/Sachsenhausen_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Sachsenhausen (Frankfurt am Main)">Sachsenhausen</a>, which is therefore known as "Ebbelwoi district". Due to its national drink Frankfurt is sometimes called "Big Ebbel" (pronunciation with <a href="/wiki/Hessian_dialects" title="Hessian dialects">hessian dialect</a>), an homage to <a href="/wiki/Big_Apple" title="Big Apple">Big Apple</a>, the famous nickname of New York City.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Green_sauce#German_Gr.C3.BCne_So.C3.9Fe" title="Green sauce">Grüne Soße</a></b> – <i>Green sauce</i> is a sauce made with hard-boiled eggs, oil, vinegar, salt and generous amount of seven fresh herbs, namely borage, sorrel, garden cress, chervil, chives, parsley and salad burnet. Variants, often due to seasonal availability include dill, lovage, lemon balm and spinach. Original green sauce Frankfurt-style is made of herbs that were gathered only on fields within the city limits.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Frankfurter_W%C3%BCrstchen" title="Frankfurter Würstchen">Frankfurter Würstchen</a></b> – "short Frankfurter" is a small <a href="/wiki/Sausage" title="Sausage">sausage</a> made of smoked pork smoked. They are similar to <a href="/wiki/Hot_dog" title="Hot dog">Hot dogs</a>. The name Frankfurter Würstchen has been trademarked since 1860.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Frankfurter_Rindswurst" title="Frankfurter Rindswurst">Frankfurter Rindswurst</a></b> – Sausage made of pure beef.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Frankfurter_Rippchen" title="Frankfurter Rippchen">Frankfurter Rippchen</a></b> – Also known as Rippchen mit Kraut, this is a traditional dish which consists of cured pork cutlets, slowly heated in <a href="/wiki/Sauerkraut" title="Sauerkraut">sauerkraut</a> or meat broth, and usually served with sauerkraut, mashed potatoes and yellow mustard.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Handk%C3%A4se" title="Handkäse">Handkäs mit Musik</a></b> – German regional <a href="/wiki/Sour_milk_cheese" title="Sour milk cheese">sour milk cheese</a> (similar to <a href="/wiki/Harzer" title="Harzer">Harzer</a>) and a culinary specialty in the <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Rhine-Main" title="Frankfurt Rhine-Main">Rhine Main Region</a>. The traditional way producing it is by hand. When it is topped with chopped onions it becomes "Handkäs mit Musik" (with music) because the onions are supposed to stimulate flatulence.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Frankfurter_Kranz" title="Frankfurter Kranz">Frankfurter Kranz</a></b> – Cake speciality believed to originate from Frankfurt.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Bethm%C3%A4nnchen" title="Bethmännchen">Bethmännchen</a></b> – "A little Bethmann" is a pastry made from marzipan with almond, powdered sugar, rosewater, flour, and egg. It is usually baked for Christmas.</li>
</ul>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airports">Airports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Airports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:AirportFrankfurt_fromair_2010-09-19.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/AirportFrankfurt_fromair_2010-09-19.jpg/220px-AirportFrankfurt_fromair_2010-09-19.jpg" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/AirportFrankfurt_fromair_2010-09-19.jpg/330px-AirportFrankfurt_fromair_2010-09-19.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/AirportFrankfurt_fromair_2010-09-19.jpg/440px-AirportFrankfurt_fromair_2010-09-19.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1760" data-file-height="1206" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:AirportFrankfurt_fromair_2010-09-19.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Airport" title="Frankfurt Airport">Frankfurt Airport</a> (with the fourth runway under construction in 2010) and the <a href="/wiki/Frankfurter_Kreuz" title="Frankfurter Kreuz">Frankfurter Kreuz</a> (lower right corner)</div>
</div>
</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Frankfurt_Airport">Frankfurt Airport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Frankfurt Airport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The city can be accessed from around the world via <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Airport" title="Frankfurt Airport">Frankfurt Airport</a> (<i>Flughafen Frankfurt am Main</i>) located 12&#160;km (7&#160;mi) southwest of the city centre. The airport has four <a href="/wiki/Runway" title="Runway">runways</a> and serves 265 non-stop destinations. Run by transport company <a href="/wiki/Fraport" title="Fraport">Fraport</a> it ranks among the <a href="/wiki/World%27s_busiest_airports_by_passenger_traffic" class="mw-redirect" title="World's busiest airports by passenger traffic">world's busiest airports by passenger traffic</a> and is the <a href="/wiki/World%27s_busiest_airports_by_cargo_traffic" class="mw-redirect" title="World's busiest airports by cargo traffic">busiest airport by cargo traffic</a> in Europe. The airport also serves as a hub for <a href="/wiki/Condor_Flugdienst" title="Condor Flugdienst">Condor</a> and as the main hub for German <a href="/wiki/Flag_carrier" title="Flag carrier">flag carrier</a> <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa" title="Lufthansa">Lufthansa</a>. Depending upon whether total passengers or flights are used for calculations, it ranks third or second busiest in Europe alongside <a href="/wiki/London_Heathrow_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="London Heathrow Airport">London Heathrow Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport" title="Charles de Gaulle Airport">Paris Charles de Gaulle Airport</a>. Passenger traffic at Frankfurt Airport in 2012 was 57.5&#160;million. There are plans to expand the airport with a third passenger terminal to increase the capacity up to 88 million in 2020.</p>
<p>The airport can be reached by car or bus and has two railway stations, one for regional and one for long-distance traffic. The <a href="/wiki/S-Bahn" class="mw-redirect" title="S-Bahn">S-Bahn</a> lines S8 and S9 (direction <i>Offenbach Ost</i> or <i>Hanau Hbf</i>) departing at the <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Airport_regional_station" title="Frankfurt Airport regional station">regional station</a> take 10–15 minutes from the airport to <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Central_Station" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankfurt Central Station">Frankfurt Central Station</a> and onwards to the city centre (<a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Hauptwache_station" title="Frankfurt Hauptwache station">Hauptwache station</a>), the <a href="/wiki/InterCity" title="InterCity">IC</a> and <a href="/wiki/Intercity-Express" title="Intercity-Express">ICE</a> trains departing at the <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Airport_long-distance_station" title="Frankfurt Airport long-distance station">long-distance station</a> take 10 minutes to Frankfurt Central Station.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Frankfurt_Hahn_Airport">Frankfurt Hahn Airport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Frankfurt Hahn Airport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Despite the name, <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt%E2%80%93Hahn_Airport" title="Frankfurt–Hahn Airport">Frankfurt Hahn Airport</a> (<i>Flughafen Frankfurt-Hahn</i>) is situated approximately 120&#160;km (75&#160;mi) from the city in <a href="/wiki/Lautzenhausen" title="Lautzenhausen">Lautzenhausen</a> (<a href="/wiki/Rhineland-Palatinate" title="Rhineland-Palatinate">Rhineland-Palatinate</a>). Hahn Airport is a major base for <a href="/wiki/Low-cost_carrier" title="Low-cost carrier">low-cost carrier</a> <a href="/wiki/Ryanair" title="Ryanair">Ryanair</a>. This airport can only be reached by car or bus. An hourly bus service runs from <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Hauptbahnhof" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankfurt Hauptbahnhof">Frankfurt Central Station</a>, taking about 1-hour and 45 minutes. Passenger traffic at Hahn Airport in 2010 was 3.5&#160;million.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Frankfurt_Egelsbach_Airport">Frankfurt Egelsbach Airport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Frankfurt Egelsbach Airport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Egelsbach_Airport" title="Frankfurt Egelsbach Airport">Frankfurt Egelsbach Airport</a> (<i>Flugplatz Frankfurt-Egelsbach</i>) is a busy <a href="/wiki/General_aviation" title="General aviation">general aviation</a> airport located south-east of Frankfurt Airport, near <a href="/wiki/Egelsbach" title="Egelsbach">Egelsbach</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Roads">Roads</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Roads">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:A_3_Frankfurter_Kreuz,_2014.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/A_3_Frankfurter_Kreuz%2C_2014.JPG/220px-A_3_Frankfurter_Kreuz%2C_2014.JPG" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/A_3_Frankfurter_Kreuz%2C_2014.JPG/330px-A_3_Frankfurter_Kreuz%2C_2014.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/A_3_Frankfurter_Kreuz%2C_2014.JPG/440px-A_3_Frankfurter_Kreuz%2C_2014.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2657" data-file-height="1493" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:A_3_Frankfurter_Kreuz,_2014.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The western approach on the <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_3" title="Bundesautobahn 3">A3</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Frankfurter_Kreuz" title="Frankfurter Kreuz">Frankfurter Kreuz</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Frankfurt is a traffic hub for the German motorway (<i><a href="/wiki/Autobahn" title="Autobahn">Autobahn</a></i>) system. The <a href="/wiki/Frankfurter_Kreuz" title="Frankfurter Kreuz">Frankfurter Kreuz</a> is an Autobahn interchange close to the airport, where the <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_3" title="Bundesautobahn 3">Bundesautobahn 3</a> (A3), <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a> to <a href="/wiki/W%C3%BCrzburg" title="Würzburg">Würzburg</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_5" title="Bundesautobahn 5">Bundesautobahn 5</a> (A5), <a href="/wiki/Basel" title="Basel">Basel</a> to <a href="/wiki/Hannover" class="mw-redirect" title="Hannover">Hannover</a>, meet. With approximately 320,000 cars passing through it every day it is Europe's most heavily used interchange. The <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_66" title="Bundesautobahn 66">Bundesautobahn 66</a> (A66) connects Frankfurt with <a href="/wiki/Wiesbaden" title="Wiesbaden">Wiesbaden</a> in the west and <a href="/wiki/Fulda" title="Fulda">Fulda</a> in the east. The <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_661" title="Bundesautobahn 661">Bundesautobahn 661</a> (A661) is mainly a commuter motorway which starts in the south (Egelsbach), runs through the eastern part and ends in the north (<a href="/wiki/Oberursel" class="mw-redirect" title="Oberursel">Oberursel</a>). The <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_648" title="Bundesautobahn 648">Bundesautobahn 648</a> (A648) is a very short motorway in the western part which primarily serves as a fast connection between the A 66 and the <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Trade_Fair" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankfurt Trade Fair">Frankfurt Trade Fair</a>. The A5 in the west, the A3 in the south and the A661 in the north-east form a <a href="/wiki/Ring_road" title="Ring road">ring road</a> around the inner city districts and define a <a href="/wiki/Low-emission_zone" title="Low-emission zone">Low-emission zone</a> (<i>Umweltzone</i>; established in 2008), meaning that vehicles have to meet certain emission criteria to enter the zone.</p>
<p>The streets of central Frankfurt are usually congested with cars during <a href="/wiki/Rush_hour" title="Rush hour">rush hour</a>. Some areas, especially around the shopping streets Zeil, Goethestraße and Freßgass, are pedestrian-only streets. Car parks are located throughout the city and especially in the city centre.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Railway_stations">Railway stations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Railway stations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Frankfurt_Central_Station">Frankfurt Central Station</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Frankfurt Central Station">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_(Main)_Hauptbahnhof" title="Frankfurt (Main) Hauptbahnhof">Frankfurt Central Station</a> (<i>Frankfurt Hauptbahnhof</i>, often abbreviated as <i>Frankfurt (Main) Hbf</i> or <i>F-Hbf</i>) is the largest railway station in Germany by railway traffic. By daily passenger volume, it ranks second together with <a href="/wiki/M%C3%BCnchen_Hauptbahnhof" title="München Hauptbahnhof">Munich Central Station</a> (350,000 each) after <a href="/wiki/Hamburg_Hauptbahnhof" title="Hamburg Hauptbahnhof">Hamburg Central Station</a> (450,000). It is located between the <a href="/wiki/Gallus_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Gallus (Frankfurt am Main)">Gallus</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Gutleutviertel" title="Gutleutviertel">Gutleutviertel</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Bahnhofsviertel_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bahnhofsviertel (Frankfurt am Main)">Bahnhofsviertel</a> district, not far away from the trade fair and the financial district. It serves as a major hub for long-distance trains (<a href="/wiki/InterCity" title="InterCity">InterCity</a>, <a href="/wiki/InterCityExpress" class="mw-redirect" title="InterCityExpress">ICE</a>) and regional trains as well as for Frankfurt's public transport system. It is a stop for most of ICE high speed lines, making it Germany's most important ICE station. ICE Trains to London via the <a href="/wiki/Channel_Tunnel" title="Channel Tunnel">Channel Tunnel</a> were planned for 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> All <a href="/wiki/Rhine-Main_S-Bahn" title="Rhine-Main S-Bahn">Rhine-Main S-Bahn</a> lines, two <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_U-Bahn" title="Frankfurt U-Bahn">U-Bahn</a> lines (U4, U5), several tram and bus lines stop there. Regional and local trains are integrated in the Public transport system <a href="/wiki/Rhein-Main-Verkehrsverbund" title="Rhein-Main-Verkehrsverbund">Rhein-Main-Verkehrsverbund</a> (RMV), the second largest integrated public transport systems in the world, after <a href="/wiki/Verkehrsverbund_Berlin-Brandenburg" title="Verkehrsverbund Berlin-Brandenburg">Verkehrsverbund Berlin-Brandenburg</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Frankfurt_Airport_stations">Frankfurt Airport stations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Frankfurt Airport stations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Frankfurt Airport can be accessed by two railway stations: <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Airport_long-distance_station" title="Frankfurt Airport long-distance station">Frankfurt Airport long-distance station</a> (<i>Frankfurt Flughafen Fernbahnhof</i>) is only for long-distance traffic and connects the airport to the main rail network, with most of the <a href="/wiki/InterCityExpress" class="mw-redirect" title="InterCityExpress">ICE</a> services using the <a href="/wiki/Cologne-Frankfurt_high-speed_rail_line" class="mw-redirect" title="Cologne-Frankfurt high-speed rail line">Cologne-Frankfurt high-speed rail line</a>. The long-distance station is located outside the actual airport ground but has a connecting bridge for pedestrians to Terminal 1, concourse B. <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Airport_regional_station" title="Frankfurt Airport regional station">Frankfurt Airport regional station</a> (<i>Frankfurt Flughafen Regionalbahnhof</i>) is for local <a href="/wiki/Rhine-Main_S-Bahn" title="Rhine-Main S-Bahn">S-Bahn</a> trains (lines S8, S9) and regional trains. The regional station is located within Terminal 1, concourse B.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Frankfurt_South_station">Frankfurt South station</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Frankfurt South station">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Frankfurt's third long-distance station is <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_South_station" title="Frankfurt South station">Frankfurt South station</a> (<i>Frankfurt Südbahnhof</i>, often abbreviated as <i>Frankfurt (Main) Süd</i> or <i>F-Süd</i>), located in <a href="/wiki/Sachsenhausen_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Sachsenhausen (Frankfurt am Main)">Sachsenhausen</a>. It is an important destination for local trains and trams (lines 14 to 16, 19) and the terminal stop for four U-Bahn lines (U1, U2, U3, U8) and four S-Bahn lines (S3, S4, S5, S6).</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Messe_stations">Messe stations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Messe stations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Trade_Fair" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankfurt Trade Fair">Frankfurt Trade Fair</a> offers two railway stations: <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Messe_station" title="Frankfurt Messe station">Messe station</a> is for local <a href="/wiki/Rhine-Main_S-Bahn" title="Rhine-Main S-Bahn">S-Bahn</a> trains (lines S3-S6) and is located at the centre of the trade fair premises while Festhalle/Messe station is served by U-Bahn line U4 and is located at the north-east corner of the premises.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Konstablerwache_station_and_Hauptwache_station">Konstablerwache station and Hauptwache station</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Konstablerwache station and Hauptwache station">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Two other major railway stations in the city centre are Konstablerwache and Hauptwache, located on each end of the Zeil. They are the main stations to change from east-to-west-bound S-Bahn trains to north-to-south-bound U-Bahn trains. Konstablerwache station is the second-busiest railway station regarding daily passenger volume (191,000) after the central station. The third-busiest railway station is Hauptwache station (181,000).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_transport">Public transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Public transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
