<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Public_transport_in_Frankfurt_am_Main" title="Public transport in Frankfurt am Main">Public transport in Frankfurt am Main</a></div>
<p>The city has two <a href="/wiki/Rapid_transit" title="Rapid transit">rapid transit</a> systems: the U-Bahn and the S-Bahn, as well as an above-ground tram system. Information about the U- and S-Bahn can be found on the website of the <a href="/wiki/Rhein-Main-Verkehrsverbund" title="Rhein-Main-Verkehrsverbund">RMV</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="S-Bahn">S-Bahn</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: S-Bahn">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Nine <a href="/wiki/S-Bahn" class="mw-redirect" title="S-Bahn">S-Bahn</a> lines (S1 to S9) connect Frankfurt with the densely populated <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Rhein-Main_Region" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankfurt Rhein-Main Region">Rhine Main Region</a>. Most routes have at least 15-minute service during the day, either by one line running every 15 minutes, or by two lines servicing one route at a 30-minute interval. All lines, except line S7, run through the Frankfurt city tunnel and serve the stations <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Ostendstra%C3%9Fe_station" title="Frankfurt Ostendstraße station">Ostendstraße</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_(Main)_Konstablerwache_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankfurt (Main) Konstablerwache station">Konstablerwache</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_(Main)_Hauptwache_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankfurt (Main) Hauptwache station">Hauptwache</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taunusanlage_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Taunusanlage station">Taunusanlage</a> and <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Central_Station" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankfurt Central Station">Frankfurt Central Station</a>. When leaving the city the S-Bahn travels above ground. It provides access to the trade fair (S3, S4, S5, S6), the airport (S8, S9), the stadium (S7, S8, S9) and nearby cities such as <a href="/wiki/Wiesbaden" title="Wiesbaden">Wiesbaden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mainz" title="Mainz">Mainz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Darmstadt" title="Darmstadt">Darmstadt</a>, <a href="/wiki/R%C3%BCsselsheim" class="mw-redirect" title="Rüsselsheim">Rüsselsheim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hanau" title="Hanau">Hanau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Offenbach_am_Main" title="Offenbach am Main">Offenbach am Main</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oberursel" class="mw-redirect" title="Oberursel">Oberursel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bad_Homburg" class="mw-redirect" title="Bad Homburg">Bad Homburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kronberg" class="mw-redirect" title="Kronberg">Kronberg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Friedberg,_Hesse" title="Friedberg, Hesse">Friedberg</a> and smaller towns that are on the way. The S8/S9 runs 24/7.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="U-Bahn">U-Bahn</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: U-Bahn">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/U-Bahn" class="mw-redirect" title="U-Bahn">U-Bahn</a> has nine lines (U1 to U9) serving Frankfurt and the larger suburbs of Bad Homburg and Oberursel in the north. The trains that run on the line are in fact <a href="/wiki/Light_rail" title="Light rail">light rail</a> as many lines travel along a track in the middle of the street instead of underground further from the city centre. The minimum service interval is 2.5 minutes, although the usual pattern is that each line runs at 7.5 to 10-minute intervals, which produce between 3 and 5-minute intervals on city centre tracks shared by more than one line.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Tram">Tram</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Tram">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Frankfurt has ten <a href="/wiki/Trams_in_Frankfurt_am_Main" title="Trams in Frankfurt am Main">tram</a> lines (11, 12, 14 to 21), with trams arriving usually every 10 minutes. Many sections are served by two lines, combining to run at 5-minute intervals during rush-hour. The tram runs only above ground and serve more stops than the U-Bahn or the S-Bahn.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Bus">Bus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Bus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>A number of <a href="/wiki/Public_transport_in_Frankfurt_am_Main" title="Public transport in Frankfurt am Main">bus</a> lines complete the Frankfurt public transport system. Night buses replace U-Bahn and tram services between 1:30&#160;am and 3:30&#160;am.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> The central junction for the night bus service is Konstablerwache in the city centre, where all night bus lines start and end.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Taxis">Taxis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Taxis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Taxicab" title="Taxicab">Taxis</a> can usually be found outside the major S-Bahn and U-Bahn stations, at the central station, the south station, the airport, the trade fair and in the crowded inner-city shopping streets. The common way to obtain a taxi is to either call a taxi operator or to go to a taxi rank. However, although not the norm, one can hail a passing taxi on the street.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Uber_(company)" title="Uber (company)">Uber</a> ceased Frankfurt operations on 9 November 2015. It is unknown when services will resume.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bicycles">Bicycles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Bicycles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Frankfurt_Velotaxi.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Frankfurt_Velotaxi.jpg/220px-Frankfurt_Velotaxi.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Frankfurt_Velotaxi.jpg/330px-Frankfurt_Velotaxi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Frankfurt_Velotaxi.jpg/440px-Frankfurt_Velotaxi.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Frankfurt_Velotaxi.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Velotaxi at the Zeil</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bahn" title="Deutsche Bahn">Deutsche Bahn</a> makes bicycles available for hire through their <a href="/wiki/Call_a_Bike" title="Call a Bike">Call a Bike</a> service. The bicycles are stationed all over the city, including at selected railway stations. They can easily be spotted because of their eye-catching silver-red colour. To rent a specific bike, riders either call a service number to get an unlock code or reserve the bike via the smartphone application. To return the bike, the rider locks it within a designated return area (and calls the service number, if not booked via the app).<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Nextbike" title="Nextbike">Nextbike</a> also makes bicycles available for hire in Frankfurt. They are stationed all over the city. These can be spotted with their blue color scheme.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Cycle_rickshaw" title="Cycle rickshaw">Cycle rickshaws</a> (velotaxis), a type of <a href="/wiki/Tricycle" title="Tricycle">tricycle</a> designed to carry passengers in addition to the driver, are also available. These are allowed to operate in pedestrian-only areas and are therefore practical for sightseeing.</p>
<p>Frankfurt has a network of cycle routes. Many long-distance bike routes into the city have cycle tracks that are separate from motor vehicle traffic. A number of roads in the city centre are "bicycle streets" where the cyclist has the right of way and where motorised vehicles are only allowed access if they do not disrupt the cycle users. In addition, cyclists are allowed to ride many cramped one-way streets in both directions. As of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, 15 percent of citizens used bicycles.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy_and_business">Economy and business</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: Economy and business">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <small><i>(September 2015)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Frankfurt is one of the world's most important <a href="/wiki/Financial_centre" title="Financial centre">financial centres</a> and Germany's financial capital, followed by <a href="/wiki/Munich%27s_financial_community" title="Munich's financial community">Munich</a>. Frankfurt was ranked 8th at the <a href="/wiki/Financial_centre#International_Financial_Centers_Development_Index" title="Financial centre">International Financial Centers Development Index</a> (2013), 8th at the <a href="/wiki/Worldwide_Centres_of_Commerce_Index" class="mw-redirect" title="Worldwide Centres of Commerce Index">Worldwide Centres of Commerce Index</a> (2008), 9th at the <a href="/wiki/Global_Financial_Centres_Index" title="Global Financial Centres Index">Global Financial Centres Index</a> (September 2013),<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> 10th at the <a href="/wiki/Global_city#Global_Power_City_Index" title="Global city">Global Power City Index</a> (2011), 11th at the <a href="/wiki/Global_city#Global_City_Competitiveness_Index" title="Global city">Global City Competitiveness Index</a> (2012), 12th at the Innovation Cities Index (2011),<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> 14th at the <a href="/wiki/Global_city#World_City_Survey" title="Global city">World City Survey</a> (2011) and 23rd at the <a href="/wiki/Global_city#Global_Cities_Index" title="Global city">Global Cities Index</a> (2012).<sup id="cite_ref-Kearney.2C_Inc_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kearney.2C_Inc-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>The city's importance as a financial centre has risen since the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone_crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="Eurozone crisis">eurozone crisis</a>. Indications are the establishment of two institutions of the <a href="/wiki/European_System_of_Financial_Supervisors" class="mw-redirect" title="European System of Financial Supervisors">European System of Financial Supervisors</a> (<a href="/wiki/European_Insurance_and_Occupational_Pensions_Authority" title="European Insurance and Occupational Pensions Authority">European Insurance and Occupational Pensions Authority</a> and <a href="/wiki/European_Systemic_Risk_Board" title="European Systemic Risk Board">European Systemic Risk Board</a>) in 2011 and the <a href="/wiki/Single_Supervisory_Mechanism" title="Single Supervisory Mechanism">Single Supervisory Mechanism</a> by which the European Central Bank was to assume responsibility for specific supervisory tasks related to the financial stability of the biggest and most important <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">Eurozone</a> banks.</p>
<p>According to an annual study by <a href="/wiki/Cushman_%26_Wakefield" title="Cushman &amp; Wakefield">Cushman &amp; Wakefield</a>, the European Cities Monitor (2010), Frankfurt has been one of the top three cities for international companies in Europe, after London and Paris, since the survey started in 1990.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> It is the only German city considered to be an <a href="/wiki/Global_city#GaWC_study" title="Global city">alpha world city (category 3)</a> as listed by the <a href="/wiki/Loughborough_University" title="Loughborough University">Loughborough University</a> group's 2010 inventory,<sup id="cite_ref-Beaverstock_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beaverstock-57">[57]</a></sup> which was a promotion from the group's 2008 inventory when it was ranked as an alpha minus world city (category 4).<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>With over 922 jobs per 1,000 inhabitants, Frankfurt has the highest concentration of jobs in Germany. On work days and Saturdays one million people commute from all over the <a href="/wiki/Rhein-Main_Region" class="mw-redirect" title="Rhein-Main Region">Rhein-Main-Area</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Central_banks">Central banks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=57" title="Edit section: Central banks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:European_Central_Bank_-_building_under_construction_-_Frankfurt_-_Germany_-_14.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/European_Central_Bank_-_building_under_construction_-_Frankfurt_-_Germany_-_14.jpg/220px-European_Central_Bank_-_building_under_construction_-_Frankfurt_-_Germany_-_14.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/European_Central_Bank_-_building_under_construction_-_Frankfurt_-_Germany_-_14.jpg/330px-European_Central_Bank_-_building_under_construction_-_Frankfurt_-_Germany_-_14.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/European_Central_Bank_-_building_under_construction_-_Frankfurt_-_Germany_-_14.jpg/440px-European_Central_Bank_-_building_under_construction_-_Frankfurt_-_Germany_-_14.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6000" data-file-height="4004" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:European_Central_Bank_-_building_under_construction_-_Frankfurt_-_Germany_-_14.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The new headquarters of the European Central Bank in the Ostend district</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Frankfurt is home to two important <a href="/wiki/Central_bank" title="Central bank">central banks</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Central_Bank">European Central Bank</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=58" title="Edit section: European Central Bank">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The European Central Bank (<i>Europäische Zentralbank</i>) is one of the world's most important central banks. The ECB sets monetary policy for the Eurozone, consisting of 19 <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> <a href="/wiki/Member_state_of_the_European_Union" title="Member state of the European Union">member states</a> that have adopted the <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">Euro</a> (€) as their common currency. From 1998 the ECB Headquarters have been located in Frankfurt, first in the <a href="/wiki/Eurotower_(Frankfurt)" class="mw-redirect" title="Eurotower (Frankfurt)">Eurotower</a> at Willy-Brandt-Platz and in two other nearby high-rises. The new <a href="/wiki/Seat_of_the_European_Central_Bank" title="Seat of the European Central Bank">Seat of the European Central Bank</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Ostend_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Ostend (Frankfurt am Main)">Ostend</a> district, consisting of the former wholesale market hall (<i><a href="/wiki/Gro%C3%9Fmarkthalle" title="Großmarkthalle">Großmarkthalle</a></i>) and a newly built 185-metre skyscraper, was completed in late 2014. The new building complex was designed to accommodate up to 2,300 ECB personnel. The location is a few kilometres away from the city centre and borders an industrial area as well as the Osthafen (<i>East Harbour</i>), It was primarily chosen because of its large premises which allows the ECB to install security arrangements without high fences.</p>
<p>The city honours the importance of the ECB by officially using the slogan "The City of the Euro" since 1998.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="German_Federal_Bank">German Federal Bank</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=59" title="Edit section: German Federal Bank">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bundesbank" title="Deutsche Bundesbank">German Federal Bank</a> (<i>Deutsche Bundesbank</i>), located in <a href="/wiki/Bockenheim_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Bockenheim (Frankfurt am Main)">Ginnheim</a>, was established in 1957 as the central bank for the Federal Republic of Germany. Until the euro (€) was introduced in 1999, the Deutsche Bundesbank was responsible for the monetary policy of Germany and for the German currency, the <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Mark" title="Deutsche Mark">Deutsche Mark</a> (DM). The Bundesbank was greatly respected for its control of inflation through the second half of the 20th century. Today the Bundesbank is an integral part of the <a href="/wiki/European_System_of_Central_Banks" title="European System of Central Banks">European System of Central Banks</a> (ESCB) which is formed by all 27 European Union member states.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial_banks">Commercial banks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=60" title="Edit section: Commercial banks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Frankfurt_Deutsche_Bank.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Frankfurt_Deutsche_Bank.jpg/220px-Frankfurt_Deutsche_Bank.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Frankfurt_Deutsche_Bank.jpg/330px-Frankfurt_Deutsche_Bank.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Frankfurt_Deutsche_Bank.jpg/440px-Frankfurt_Deutsche_Bank.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Frankfurt_Deutsche_Bank.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bank_Twin_Towers" title="Deutsche Bank Twin Towers">Deutsche Bank Twin Towers</a> in the financial district</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Westendtower-5.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Westendtower-5.JPG/220px-Westendtower-5.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Westendtower-5.JPG/330px-Westendtower-5.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Westendtower-5.JPG/440px-Westendtower-5.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Westendtower-5.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Westend_Tower" class="mw-redirect" title="Westend Tower">Westend Tower</a>, also known as <i>Westendstraße 1</i> or <i>Crown Tower</i>, Headquarters of DZ Bank</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:OpernturmVoll.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/OpernturmVoll.jpg/220px-OpernturmVoll.jpg" width="220" height="316" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/OpernturmVoll.jpg/330px-OpernturmVoll.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/OpernturmVoll.jpg/440px-OpernturmVoll.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2500" data-file-height="3594" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:OpernturmVoll.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Opernturm" title="Opernturm">Opernturm</a>, Headquarters of UBS Germany, at the Opernplatz</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2010, 63 national and 152 international banks had a registered office, including the headquarters of the major German banks, as well as 41 offices of international banks.<sup id="cite_ref-Bundesbank:_Bankenplatz_Frankfurt_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bundesbank:_Bankenplatz_Frankfurt-7">[7]</a></sup> Frankfurt is therefore known as Bankenstadt ("City of the banks") and nicknamed "Mainhattan" (a <a href="/wiki/Portmanteau" title="Portmanteau">portmanteau</a> of the local <a href="/wiki/Main_(river)" title="Main (river)">Main</a> river and <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">Manhattan</a> in New York City) or "Bankfurt". 73,200 people were employed at banks in 2010.</p>
<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bank" title="Deutsche Bank">Deutsche Bank</a> —</b> Germany's largest <a href="/wiki/Commercial_bank" title="Commercial bank">commercial bank</a>. It had 15% share of private customers and total assets of €1,900&#160;billion in 2010. Deutsche Bank ranks among the 30 largest banks in the world and the ten largest banks in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> Deutsche Bank is listed on the <a href="/wiki/DAX" title="DAX">DAX</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Stock_market_index" title="Stock market index">stock market index</a> of the 30 largest German business companies at the Frankfurt Stock Exchange. In November 2010 Deutsche Bank bought the majority of shares of competitor <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Postbank" title="Deutsche Postbank">Postbank</a>. Its <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bank_Twin_Towers" title="Deutsche Bank Twin Towers">headquarters</a> are located at Taunusanlage in the financial district.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Commerzbank" title="Commerzbank">Commerzbank</a> —</b> Germany's second-largest commercial, bank with total assets of €754&#160;billion (2010). In 2009, Commerzbank merged with competitor <a href="/wiki/Dresdner_Bank" title="Dresdner Bank">Dresdner Bank</a>, then the third-largest German bank. Due to the merger and the higher credit risks, Commerzbank was partially <a href="/wiki/Nationalization" title="Nationalization">nationalized</a> (25 percent) during the <a href="/wiki/Late-2000s_financial_crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="Late-2000s financial crisis">financial crisis in 2009</a>. It is listed in the DAX. Its headquarters are at <a href="/wiki/Commerzbank_Tower" title="Commerzbank Tower">Commerzbank Tower</a> (259 metres), the <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_the_European_Union" title="List of tallest buildings in the European Union">2nd tallest building in the European Union</a>, at Kaiserplatz.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/KfW" title="KfW">KfW Bankengruppe</a></b> —Government-owned development bank formed in 1948 as part of the <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Plan" title="Marshall Plan">Marshall Plan</a>. KfW provides loans for approved purposes at lower rates than commercial banks, especially to medium-sized businesses. With total assets of €442&#160;billion (2010), it is Germany's third-largest bank. The KfW Headquarters are located in the <a href="/wiki/Westend_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Westend (Frankfurt am Main)">Westend</a> district at Bockenheimer Landstraße and Senckenberganlage.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/DZ_Bank" title="DZ Bank">DZ Bank</a> —</b> Central institution for more than 900 <a href="/wiki/Cooperative_banking" title="Cooperative banking">co-operative banks</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Bundesverband_der_Deutschen_Volksbanken_und_Raiffeisenbanken" title="Bundesverband der Deutschen Volksbanken und Raiffeisenbanken">Volksbanken und Raiffeisenbanken</a></i>) and their 12,000 branch offices in Germany and is a corporate and investment bank. It is Germany's fourth-largest bank (total assets: €383 billion). The DZ Bank Group defines itself primarily as a service provider for the local Volksbanken and Raiffeisenbanken and their 30 million clients. The DZ Bank headquarters are the <a href="/wiki/Westend_Tower" class="mw-redirect" title="Westend Tower">Westend Tower</a> and the <a href="/wiki/City-Haus" title="City-Haus">City-Haus</a> at Platz der Republik. The DZ Bank Group includes <a href="/wiki/Union_Investment" title="Union Investment">Union Investment</a>, DVB Bank and Reisebank, which are also headquartered in Frankfurt.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Helaba" title="Helaba">Landesbank Hessen-Thüringen</a></b> – Landesbank Hessen-Thüringen, or short <b>Helaba</b>, is the central federal bank (<i><a href="/wiki/Landesbank" title="Landesbank">Landesbank</a></i>) for the federal states of <a href="/wiki/Hesse" title="Hesse">Hesse</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thuringia" title="Thuringia">Thuringia</a>. As such, it is state-owned and defined as a service provider for the local <a href="/wiki/German_public_bank" title="German public bank">German public banks</a> (<i>Sparkassen</i>). Helaba is one of nine <i>Landesbanken</i> and is the fifth-largest in Germany. It is located in the 200-metre-tall <a href="/wiki/Main_Tower" title="Main Tower">Main Tower</a> in the financial district, the only skyscraper with an observation desk open to the public.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/DekaBank" class="mw-redirect" title="DekaBank">DekaBank</a></b> – DekaBank is the central asset manager of the <i>Sparkassen</i> in Germany. The headquarters of DekaBank are located at the <a href="/wiki/Trianon_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Trianon (Frankfurt am Main)">Trianon</a> skyscraper at Mainzer Landstraße.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/ING_Group" title="ING Group">ING Diba</a> Germany</b> – Germany's largest <a href="/wiki/Direct_bank" title="Direct bank">direct bank</a>, headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Bockenheim_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Bockenheim (Frankfurt am Main)">Bockenheim</a>.</li>
</ul>
<p>Other major German banks include Frankfurter Volksbank, the second-largest <i>Volksbank</i> in Germany, Frankfurter Sparkasse and old-established private banks such as <a href="/wiki/Metzler_Bank" title="Metzler Bank">Bankhaus Metzler</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hauck_%26_Aufh%C3%A4user" title="Hauck &amp; Aufhäuser">Hauck &amp; Aufhäuser</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bethmann_bank" class="mw-redirect" title="Bethmann bank">Delbrück Bethmann Maffei</a>.</p>
<p>Many international banks have a registered or a representative office, e.g., <a href="/wiki/Credit_Suisse" title="Credit Suisse">Credit Suisse</a>, <a href="/wiki/UBS" title="UBS">UBS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_America" title="Bank of America">Bank of America</a>, <a href="/wiki/Morgan_Stanley" title="Morgan Stanley">Morgan Stanley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Goldman_Sachs" title="Goldman Sachs">Goldman Sachs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Merrill_Lynch" title="Merrill Lynch">Merrill Lynch</a>, <a href="/wiki/JPMorgan_Chase_%26_Co." class="mw-redirect" title="JPMorgan Chase &amp; Co.">JPMorgan Chase &amp; Co.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_China" title="Bank of China">Bank of China</a>, <a href="/wiki/Banco_do_Brasil" title="Banco do Brasil">Banco do Brasil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ita%C3%BA_Unibanco" title="Itaú Unibanco">Itaú Unibanco</a> <a href="/wiki/Soci%C3%A9t%C3%A9_G%C3%A9n%C3%A9rale" title="Société Générale">Société Générale</a>, <a href="/wiki/BNP_Paribas" title="BNP Paribas">BNP Paribas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Skandinaviska_Enskilda_Banken" class="mw-redirect" title="Skandinaviska Enskilda Banken">SEB</a>, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Bank_of_Scotland" title="Royal Bank of Scotland">Royal Bank of Scotland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barclays" title="Barclays">Barclays</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Frankfurt_Stock_Exchange">Frankfurt Stock Exchange</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=61" title="Edit section: Frankfurt Stock Exchange">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bulle_und_B%C3%A4r_Frankfurt.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Bulle_und_B%C3%A4r_Frankfurt.jpg/220px-Bulle_und_B%C3%A4r_Frankfurt.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Bulle_und_B%C3%A4r_Frankfurt.jpg/330px-Bulle_und_B%C3%A4r_Frankfurt.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Bulle_und_B%C3%A4r_Frankfurt.jpg/440px-Bulle_und_B%C3%A4r_Frankfurt.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bulle_und_B%C3%A4r_Frankfurt.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Market_trend" title="Market trend">Bull and bear</a> in front of the Frankfurt Stock Exchange</div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Stock_Exchange" title="Frankfurt Stock Exchange">Frankfurt Stock Exchange</a></div>
<p>The Frankfurt Stock Exchange (<i>Frankfurter Wertpapierbörse</i>) began in the 9th century. By the 16th century Frankfurt had developed into an important European hub for trade fairs and financial services. Today the Frankfurt Stock Exchange is by far the largest in Germany, with a turnover of more than 90 percent of the German <a href="/wiki/Stock_market" title="Stock market">stock market</a> and is the third-largest in Europe after the <a href="/wiki/London_Stock_Exchange" title="London Stock Exchange">London Stock Exchange</a> and the European branch of the <a href="/wiki/NYSE_Euronext" title="NYSE Euronext">NYSE Euronext</a>. The most important <a href="/wiki/Stock_market_index" title="Stock market index">stock market index</a> is the <a href="/wiki/DAX" title="DAX">DAX</a>, the index of the 30 largest German business companies listed at the stock exchange. The stock exchange is owned and operated by <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_B%C3%B6rse" title="Deutsche Börse">Deutsche Börse</a>, which is itself listed in the DAX. Deutsche Börse also owns the European <a href="/wiki/Futures_exchange" title="Futures exchange">futures exchange</a> <a href="/wiki/Eurex" class="mw-redirect" title="Eurex">Eurex</a> and clearing company <a href="/wiki/Clearstream" title="Clearstream">Clearstream</a>. Trading takes place exclusively via the <a href="/wiki/Xetra_(trading_system)" title="Xetra (trading system)">Xetra trading system</a>, with redundant floor brokers taking on the role of market-makers on the new platform.</p>
<p>On 1 February 2012 European Commission blocked the proposed merger of Deutsche Börse and <a href="/wiki/New_York_Stock_Exchange" title="New York Stock Exchange">NYSE Euronext</a>. "The merger between Deutsche Börse and NYSE Euronext would have led to a near-monopoly in European financial derivatives worldwide. These markets are at the heart of the financial system and it is crucial for the whole European economy that they remain competitive. We tried to find a solution, but the remedies offered fell far short of resolving the concerns."<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> European competition commissioner, <a href="/wiki/Joaqu%C3%ADn_Almunia" title="Joaquín Almunia">Joaquín Almunia</a>, said.</p>
<p>It is located in the city centre at the Börsenplatz. Deutsche Börse's headquarters are formally registered in Frankfurt but it moved most of its employees a high-rise called "The Cube" in <a href="/wiki/Eschborn" title="Eschborn">Eschborn</a> in 2010, primarily due to significantly lower local <a href="/wiki/Corporate_tax" title="Corporate tax">corporate taxes</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Frankfurt_Trade_Fair">Frankfurt Trade Fair</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=62" title="Edit section: Frankfurt Trade Fair">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Messefrankfurt-messeturm-und-messebesucher.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Messefrankfurt-messeturm-und-messebesucher.jpg/220px-Messefrankfurt-messeturm-und-messebesucher.jpg" width="220" height="279" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Messefrankfurt-messeturm-und-messebesucher.jpg/330px-Messefrankfurt-messeturm-und-messebesucher.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Messefrankfurt-messeturm-und-messebesucher.jpg/440px-Messefrankfurt-messeturm-und-messebesucher.jpg 2x" data-file-width="551" data-file-height="700" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Messefrankfurt-messeturm-und-messebesucher.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Messeturm" title="Messeturm">Messeturm</a> seen from the trade fair premises</div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Trade_Fair" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankfurt Trade Fair">Frankfurt Trade Fair</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Trade_Fair" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankfurt Trade Fair">Frankfurt Trade Fair</a> (<i>Messe Frankfurt</i>) has the third-largest exhibition site in the world with a total of 578,000 square metres (6,221,540 square feet). The trade fair premises are located in the western part between <a href="/wiki/Bockenheim_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Bockenheim (Frankfurt am Main)">Bockenheim</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Westend_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Westend (Frankfurt am Main)">Westend</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Gallus_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Gallus (Frankfurt am Main)">Gallus</a> district. It houses ten exhibition halls with a total of 321,754 square meters (3,463,331 square feet) of space and 96,078 square metres (1,034,175 square feet) of outdoor space.</p>
<p>Hosted in Frankfurt are the <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Motor_Show" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankfurt Motor Show">Frankfurt Motor Show</a> (<i>Internationale Automobil-Ausstellung – IAA</i>), the world's largest <a href="/wiki/Auto_show" title="Auto show">auto show</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Book_Fair" title="Frankfurt Book Fair">Frankfurt Book Fair</a> (<i>Frankfurter Buchmesse</i>), the world's largest book fair, the Ambiente Frankfurt, the world's largest <a href="/wiki/Final_good" title="Final good">consumer goods</a> fair, the Achema, the world's largest plant engineering fair, and many more like Paperworld, Christmasworld, Beautyworld, Tendence Lifestyle or Light+Building.</p>
<p>Messe Frankfurt GmbH, the owner and operator company, organized 87 exhibitions in 2010, 51 thereof in foreign countries. It is one of the largest trade fair companies with commercial activities in over 150 countries.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Messeturm">Messeturm</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=63" title="Edit section: Messeturm">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>A landmark building of the trade fair (and of the whole city) is the <a href="/wiki/Messeturm" title="Messeturm">Messeturm</a> (the name translates as <i>Fair Trade Tower</i>), which was the <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_Europe" title="List of tallest buildings in Europe">tallest building in Europe</a> from 1991 to 1997. It is located on the north-east corner of the trade fair premises at the so-called city entrance. Despite the name it is not used for exhibition but serves as an office tower.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Aviation">Aviation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=64" title="Edit section: Aviation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2010-07-21_A380_LH_D-AIMB_EDDF_06.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/2010-07-21_A380_LH_D-AIMB_EDDF_06.jpg/220px-2010-07-21_A380_LH_D-AIMB_EDDF_06.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/2010-07-21_A380_LH_D-AIMB_EDDF_06.jpg/330px-2010-07-21_A380_LH_D-AIMB_EDDF_06.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/2010-07-21_A380_LH_D-AIMB_EDDF_06.jpg/440px-2010-07-21_A380_LH_D-AIMB_EDDF_06.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2000" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2010-07-21_A380_LH_D-AIMB_EDDF_06.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Two Lufthansa Airbus A380s at <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Airport" title="Frankfurt Airport">Frankfurt Airport</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Airport" title="Frankfurt Airport">Frankfurt Airport</a> is one of the busiest airports in the world and is also the single largest place of work in Germany with over 500 companies which employ 71,500 people (2010).<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Lufthansa">Lufthansa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=65" title="Edit section: Lufthansa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The largest employer at Frankfurt Airport is Lufthansa, Germany's <a href="/wiki/Flag_carrier" title="Flag carrier">flag carrier</a> and Europe's largest airline. Lufthansa employs 35,000 people in Frankfurt.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> The Lufthansa Aviation Center (LAC) is the main operation base of Lufthansa at Frankfurt Airport. The airport serves as Lufthansa's primary <a href="/wiki/Airline_hub" title="Airline hub">hub</a> with 157 worldwide destinations (compared to 110 destinations at <a href="/wiki/Munich_Airport" title="Munich Airport">Munich Airport</a>, Lufthansa's second-largest hub). <b><a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_Cargo" title="Lufthansa Cargo">Lufthansa Cargo</a></b> is based in Frankfurt and operates its largest cargo center (LCC) at Frankfurt Airport. <b><a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_Flight_Training" title="Lufthansa Flight Training">Lufthansa Flight Training</a></b> is also based here.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Fraport">Fraport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=66" title="Edit section: Fraport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Fraport" title="Fraport">Fraport</a> is the owner and operator of Frankfurt Airport. It is the airport's second-largest employer (19,800 workers in 2010).<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> Fraport also operates other airports worldwide, e.g., <a href="/wiki/King_Abdulaziz_International_Airport" title="King Abdulaziz International Airport">King Abdulaziz International Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Jeddah" title="Jeddah">Jeddah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Ch%C3%A1vez_International_Airport" title="Jorge Chávez International Airport">Jorge Chávez International Airport</a> in Lima and <a href="/wiki/Antalya_Airport" title="Antalya Airport">Antalya Airport</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Condor">Condor</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=67" title="Edit section: Condor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Condor_Flugdienst" title="Condor Flugdienst">Condor</a> is a German airline and part of <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Cook_Group" title="Thomas Cook Group">Thomas Cook Group</a>, based at Frankfurt Airport.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_industries">Other industries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=68" title="Edit section: Other industries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Accountancy_and_professional_services">Accountancy and professional services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=69" title="Edit section: Accountancy and professional services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Three of the four largest international <a href="/wiki/Accountancy" class="mw-redirect" title="Accountancy">accountancy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Professional_services" title="Professional services">professional services</a> firms <i>(<a href="/wiki/Big_Four_(audit_firms)" class="mw-redirect" title="Big Four (audit firms)">Big Four</a>)</i> are present.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/PricewaterhouseCoopers" title="PricewaterhouseCoopers">PricewaterhouseCoopers</a> (PwC) German headquarters are located at <a href="/wiki/Tower_185" title="Tower 185">Tower 185</a>. <a href="/wiki/KPMG" title="KPMG">KPMG</a> moved its European Headquarters (<a href="/wiki/KPMG#Recent_history" title="KPMG">KPMG Europe LLP</a>) to <a href="/wiki/The_Squaire" title="The Squaire">The Squaire</a>. <a href="/wiki/Deloitte_Touche_Tohmatsu" class="mw-redirect" title="Deloitte Touche Tohmatsu">Deloitte Touche Tohmatsu</a> are present, while <a href="/wiki/Ernst_%26_Young" title="Ernst &amp; Young">Ernst &amp; Young</a> is located in <a href="/wiki/Eschborn" title="Eschborn">Eschborn</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Credit_rating_agencies">Credit rating agencies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=70" title="Edit section: Credit rating agencies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The three major international <a href="/wiki/Credit_rating_agency" title="Credit rating agency">credit rating agencies</a> – <a href="/wiki/Standard_%26_Poor%27s" title="Standard &amp; Poor's">Standard &amp; Poor's</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moody%27s" class="mw-redirect" title="Moody's">Moody's</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fitch_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Fitch Group">Fitch Ratings</a> – have their German headquarters in Frankfurt.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Investment_trust_companies">Investment trust companies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=71" title="Edit section: Investment trust companies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>DWS Investments is the largest <a href="/wiki/Investment_trust" title="Investment trust">investment trust</a> company in Germany and manages €288&#160;billion fund assets. It is one of the 10 largest investment trust companies in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> Other large investment trust companies are Allianz Global Investors Europe (a division of <a href="/wiki/Allianz_SE" class="mw-redirect" title="Allianz SE">Allianz SE</a>, and a top-five global active investment manager with €1,933&#160;billion assets under management globally), <a href="/wiki/Union_Investment" title="Union Investment">Union Investment</a> and Deka Investmentfonds.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Management_consultancies">Management consultancies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=72" title="Edit section: Management consultancies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Many of the largest international <a href="/wiki/Management_consulting" title="Management consulting">management consultancies</a> are represented, including <a href="/wiki/Arthur_D._Little" title="Arthur D. Little">Arthur D. Little</a>, <a href="/wiki/McKinsey_%26_Company" title="McKinsey &amp; Company">McKinsey &amp; Company</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boston_Consulting_Group" title="Boston Consulting Group">Boston Consulting Group</a>, <a href="/wiki/Booz_%26_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Booz &amp; Company">Booz &amp; Company</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Wyman" title="Oliver Wyman">Oliver Wyman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bearing_Point" class="mw-redirect" title="Bearing Point">Bearing Point</a>, <a href="/wiki/Capgemini" title="Capgemini">Capgemini</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bain_%26_Company" title="Bain &amp; Company">Bain &amp; Company</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roland_Berger_Strategy_Consultants" class="mw-redirect" title="Roland Berger Strategy Consultants">Roland Berger Strategy Consultants</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Real_estate_services_companies">Real estate services companies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=73" title="Edit section: Real estate services companies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Located in Frankfurt are the German headquarters of <a href="/wiki/Jones_Lang_LaSalle" class="mw-redirect" title="Jones Lang LaSalle">Jones Lang LaSalle</a> and <a href="/wiki/BNP_Paribas_Real_Estate" class="mw-redirect" title="BNP Paribas Real Estate">BNP Paribas Real Estate</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Law_firms">Law firms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=74" title="Edit section: Law firms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Frankfurt has the highest concentration of lawyers in Germany, with one lawyer per 97 inhabitants (followed by <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="Düsseldorf">Düsseldorf</a> with a ratio of 1/117 and <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a> with 1/124) in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p>Most of the large international <a href="/wiki/Law_firms" class="mw-redirect" title="Law firms">law firms</a> maintain offices, among them <a href="/wiki/Allen_%26_Overy" title="Allen &amp; Overy">Allen &amp; Overy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baker_%26_McKenzie" class="mw-redirect" title="Baker &amp; McKenzie">Baker &amp; McKenzie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bird_%26_Bird" title="Bird &amp; Bird">Bird &amp; Bird</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clifford_Chance" title="Clifford Chance">Clifford Chance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cleary_Gottlieb_Steen_%26_Hamilton" title="Cleary Gottlieb Steen &amp; Hamilton">Cleary Gottlieb Steen &amp; Hamilton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Debevoise_%26_Plimpton" title="Debevoise &amp; Plimpton">Debevoise &amp; Plimpton</a>, <a href="/wiki/DLA_Piper" title="DLA Piper">DLA Piper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Freshfields_Bruckhaus_Deringer" title="Freshfields Bruckhaus Deringer">Freshfields Bruckhaus Deringer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hogan_Lovells" title="Hogan Lovells">Hogan Lovells</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jones_Day" title="Jones Day">Jones Day</a>, <a href="/wiki/Latham_%26_Watkins" title="Latham &amp; Watkins">Latham &amp; Watkins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Linklaters" title="Linklaters">Linklaters</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mayer_Brown" title="Mayer Brown">Mayer Brown</a>, <a href="/wiki/Milbank,_Tweed,_Hadley_%26_McCloy" title="Milbank, Tweed, Hadley &amp; McCloy">Milbank, Tweed, Hadley &amp; McCloy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norton_Rose" class="mw-redirect" title="Norton Rose">Norton Rose</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shearman_%26_Sterling" title="Shearman &amp; Sterling">Shearman &amp; Sterling</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sidley_Austin" title="Sidley Austin">Sidley Austin</a>, <a href="/wiki/SJ_Berwin" title="SJ Berwin">SJ Berwin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Skadden,_Arps,_Slate,_Meagher_%26_Flom" title="Skadden, Arps, Slate, Meagher &amp; Flom">Skadden, Arps, Slate, Meagher &amp; Flom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sullivan_%26_Cromwell" title="Sullivan &amp; Cromwell">Sullivan &amp; Cromwell</a>, <a href="/wiki/K%26L_Gates" title="K&amp;L Gates">K&amp;L Gates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taylor_Wessing" title="Taylor Wessing">Taylor Wessing</a> and <a href="/wiki/White_%26_Case" title="White &amp; Case">White &amp; Case</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Advertising_agencies">Advertising agencies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=75" title="Edit section: Advertising agencies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Although it is best known for its banks and financial institutions, Frankfurt is also a centre for media companies. Around 570 companies of the advertising industry and 270 <a href="/wiki/Public_relations" title="Public relations">public relations</a> companies are there.</p>
<p>According to a ranking of German <a href="/wiki/Focus_(German_magazine)" title="Focus (German magazine)">FOCUS magazine</a> (November 2007) seven of the 48 largest <a href="/wiki/Advertising_agency" title="Advertising agency">advertising agencies</a> in Germany are based in Frankfurt, including <a href="/wiki/McCann-Erickson" class="mw-redirect" title="McCann-Erickson">McCann-Erickson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saatchi_%26_Saatchi" title="Saatchi &amp; Saatchi">Saatchi &amp; Saatchi</a>, <a href="/wiki/J._Walter_Thompson" title="J. Walter Thompson">JWT</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Publicis" title="Publicis">Publicis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Food">Food</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=76" title="Edit section: Food">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Frankfurt is home to the German headquarters of <a href="/wiki/Nestl%C3%A9" title="Nestlé">Nestlé</a>, the world's largest <a href="/wiki/Food_industry" title="Food industry">food company</a>, located in <a href="/wiki/Niederrad_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" class="mw-redirect" title="Niederrad (Frankfurt am Main)">Niederrad</a>. Other important food companies are <a href="/wiki/Ferrero_SpA" title="Ferrero SpA">Ferrero SpA</a> (German headquarters) and Radeberger Gruppe KG, the largest private brewery group in Germany.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Automotive">Automotive</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=77" title="Edit section: Automotive">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The South-Korean <a href="/wiki/Automotive_industry" title="Automotive industry">automobile manufacturer</a> <a href="/wiki/Kia_Motors" title="Kia Motors">Kia Motors</a> moved its European headquarters to Frankfurt in 2007. In the same year Italian manufacturer <a href="/wiki/Fiat" class="mw-redirect" title="Fiat">Fiat</a> opened its new German headquarters. The automotive supplier <a href="/wiki/Continental_AG" title="Continental AG">Continental AG</a> has the headquarters and a major manufacturing plant of its Chassis &amp; Safety division (formerly ITT Automotive) located in Frankfurt Rödelheim.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Construction">Construction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=78" title="Edit section: Construction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Some of the largest German construction companies have offices, e.g., <a href="/wiki/Bilfinger_Berger" class="mw-redirect" title="Bilfinger Berger">Bilfinger Berger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hochtief" title="Hochtief">Hochtief</a>, Züblin and BAM Deutschland.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Property_and_real_estate">Property and real estate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=79" title="Edit section: Property and real estate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Frankfurt has Germany's highest concentration of homeowners. This is partly attributed to the financial sector, but also to its cosmopolitan nature, with expatriates and immigrants representing one fourth of its population. For this reason Frankfurt's property market often operates differently than the rest of the country where the prices are generally flatter.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other">Other</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=80" title="Edit section: Other">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Industriepark_H%C3%B6chst,_Leunabr%C3%BCcke.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Industriepark_H%C3%B6chst%2C_Leunabr%C3%BCcke.jpg/220px-Industriepark_H%C3%B6chst%2C_Leunabr%C3%BCcke.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Industriepark_H%C3%B6chst%2C_Leunabr%C3%BCcke.jpg/330px-Industriepark_H%C3%B6chst%2C_Leunabr%C3%BCcke.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Industriepark_H%C3%B6chst%2C_Leunabr%C3%BCcke.jpg/440px-Industriepark_H%C3%B6chst%2C_Leunabr%C3%BCcke.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920" /></a>

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mainova_-_M%C3%BCllheizkraftwerk_Nordweststadt_-_Frankfurt_am_Main.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Mainova_-_M%C3%BCllheizkraftwerk_Nordweststadt_-_Frankfurt_am_Main.jpg/220px-Mainova_-_M%C3%BCllheizkraftwerk_Nordweststadt_-_Frankfurt_am_Main.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Mainova_-_M%C3%BCllheizkraftwerk_Nordweststadt_-_Frankfurt_am_Main.jpg/330px-Mainova_-_M%C3%BCllheizkraftwerk_Nordweststadt_-_Frankfurt_am_Main.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Mainova_-_M%C3%BCllheizkraftwerk_Nordweststadt_-_Frankfurt_am_Main.jpg/440px-Mainova_-_M%C3%BCllheizkraftwerk_Nordweststadt_-_Frankfurt_am_Main.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5616" data-file-height="3744" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mainova_-_M%C3%BCllheizkraftwerk_Nordweststadt_-_Frankfurt_am_Main.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Mainova" title="Mainova">Mainova</a> heating plant</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Frankfurt is home to companies from the chemical, the transportation, the telecommunication and the energy industry. Some of the larger companies are:</p>
<ul>
<li><b>Industriepark Höchst</b> — An <a href="/wiki/Industrial_park" title="Industrial park">industrial park</a> in <a href="/wiki/H%C3%B6chst_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Höchst (Frankfurt am Main)">Höchst</a>. It is one of Germany's largest with over 90 companies from the <a href="/wiki/Pharmaceutical_industry" title="Pharmaceutical industry">pharmaceutical</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Chemical_industry" title="Chemical industry">chemical</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Biotechnology" title="Biotechnology">biotechnology</a> industry, including <a href="/wiki/Celanese" title="Celanese">Celanese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clariant" title="Clariant">Clariant</a>, <a href="/wiki/BASF" title="BASF">BASF</a>, <a href="/wiki/Merck_KGaA" class="mw-redirect" title="Merck KGaA">Merck KGaA</a> and <a href="/wiki/Siemens" title="Siemens">Siemens</a>. It was founded by chemical company <a href="/wiki/Hoechst_AG" title="Hoechst AG">Hoechst AG</a> in 1874. At the beginning of the 1980s Hoechst AG was the largest pharmaceutical corporation and Industriepark Höchst was known as "the pharmacy of the world". Hoechst AG merged with <a href="/wiki/Rh%C3%B4ne-Poulenc" title="Rhône-Poulenc">Rhône-Poulenc</a> to become <a href="/wiki/Aventis" class="mw-redirect" title="Aventis">Aventis</a> in 1999 and in 2004 Aventis merged with <a href="/wiki/Sanofi-Synth%C3%A9labo" class="mw-redirect" title="Sanofi-Synthélabo">Sanofi-Synthélabo</a> to become <a href="/wiki/Sanofi-Aventis" class="mw-redirect" title="Sanofi-Aventis">Sanofi-Aventis</a>. In 2005, around 22,000 people worked at Industriepark Höchst. In 2011, <a href="/wiki/Ticona" class="mw-redirect" title="Ticona">Ticona</a> now part of <a href="/wiki/Celanese" title="Celanese">Celanese</a>, an international manufacturer of engineering <a href="/wiki/Polymer" title="Polymer">polymers</a>, moved to Industriepark Höchst.</li>
<li><b>Deutsche Bahn</b> – Deutsche Bahn subsidiaries <a href="/wiki/DB_Fernverkehr" title="DB Fernverkehr">DB Fernverkehr</a>, <a href="/wiki/DB_Regio" title="DB Regio">DB Regio</a>, <a href="/wiki/DB_Stadtverkehr" class="mw-redirect" title="DB Stadtverkehr">DB Stadtverkehr</a>, <a href="/wiki/DB_Netz" title="DB Netz">DB Netz</a>, <a href="/wiki/DB_Schenker" title="DB Schenker">DB Schenker</a> and the corporate development department of Deutsche Bahn are Frankfurt-based.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Telekom" title="Deutsche Telekom">Deutsche Telekom</a></b> – Deutsche Telekom's subsidiary <a href="/wiki/T-Systems" title="T-Systems">T-Systems</a> is Frankfurt-based.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/COLT_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="COLT Group">COLT</a></b> – Telecommunications company with Frankfurt-based German headquarters.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Level_3_Communications" title="Level 3 Communications">Level 3 Communications</a> —</b> <a href="/wiki/Internet_service_provider" title="Internet service provider">internet service provider</a> with German headquarters in Frankfurt.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/DE-CIX" class="mw-redirect" title="DE-CIX">DE-CIX</a></b> – Frankfurt is an important location for <a href="/wiki/Electronic_communication" class="mw-redirect" title="Electronic communication">electronic communication</a>, especially the Internet. It is home to <a href="/wiki/DE-CIX" class="mw-redirect" title="DE-CIX">DE-CIX</a>, the world's largest <a href="/wiki/Internet_exchange_point" title="Internet exchange point">internet exchange point</a>, and also the place where <a href="/wiki/Domain_name" title="Domain name">domain names</a> are registered for top-level-domain "<a href="/wiki/.de" title=".de">.de</a>".</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Mainova" title="Mainova">Mainova</a></b> – The largest regional <a href="/wiki/Energy_supply" title="Energy supply">energy supplier</a> in Germany with about one million customers in <a href="/wiki/Hesse" title="Hesse">Hesse</a>. It provides electricity, gas, heat and water. Its headquarters are Frankfurt-based.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span id="Urban_area_(suburban)_businesses"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Urban_area_.28suburban.29_businesses">Urban area (suburban) businesses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=81" title="Edit section: Urban area (suburban) businesses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Within Frankfurt's urban area are several important companies.</p>
<p>The business centre of Eschborn is located right at Frankfurt's city limits in the west and attracts businesses with significantly lower <a href="/wiki/Corporate_tax" title="Corporate tax">corporate taxes</a> compared to Frankfurt. Major companies in Eschborn include <a href="/wiki/Ernst_%26_Young" title="Ernst &amp; Young">Ernst &amp; Young</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vodafone_Germany" title="Vodafone Germany">Vodafone Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Randstad_Holding" title="Randstad Holding">Randstad Holding</a> and VR Leasing. <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_B%C3%B6rse" title="Deutsche Börse">Deutsche Börse</a> moved most of its employees to Eschborn in 2010.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/R%C3%BCsselsheim" class="mw-redirect" title="Rüsselsheim">Rüsselsheim</a> is internationally known for its <a href="/wiki/Automotive_industry" title="Automotive industry">automobile manufacturer</a> <a href="/wiki/Opel" title="Opel">Opel</a>, one of the biggest automobile manufacturers in Germany. With 20,000 employees in 2003, Opel was one of the five largest employers in <a href="/wiki/Hesse" title="Hesse">Hesse</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Offenbach_am_Main" title="Offenbach am Main">Offenbach am Main</a> is home to the European headquarters of automobile manufacturer <a href="/wiki/Hyundai_Motor_Company" title="Hyundai Motor Company">Hyundai Motor Company</a>, to the German headquarters of automobile manufacturer <a href="/wiki/Honda" title="Honda">Honda</a>, to <a href="/wiki/Honeywell" title="Honeywell">Honeywell Germany</a> and to <a href="/wiki/Deutscher_Wetterdienst" title="Deutscher Wetterdienst">Deutscher Wetterdienst</a>, the central scientific agency that monitors weather and <a href="/wiki/Meteorology" title="Meteorology">meteorological</a> conditions over Germany.</p>
<p>Two <a href="/wiki/DAX" title="DAX">DAX</a> companies are located in <a href="/wiki/Bad_Homburg_vor_der_H%C3%B6he" title="Bad Homburg vor der Höhe">Bad Homburg vor der Höhe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fresenius_(company)" title="Fresenius (company)">Fresenius SE &amp; Co. KGaA</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fresenius_Medical_Care" title="Fresenius Medical Care">Fresenius Medical Care</a>. Other major companies are <a href="/wiki/Hewlett-Packard" title="Hewlett-Packard">Hewlett-Packard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bridgestone" title="Bridgestone">Bridgestone</a>, Deutsche Leasing and Basler Versicherungen.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Kronberg_im_Taunus" title="Kronberg im Taunus">Kronberg im Taunus</a> is home of the German headquarters of automobile manufacturer <a href="/wiki/Jaguar_Cars" title="Jaguar Cars">Jaguar Cars</a> as well as the German headquarters of <a href="/wiki/Accenture" title="Accenture">Accenture</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_Systems" title="Lufthansa Systems">Lufthansa Systems</a>, a subsidiary of <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa" title="Lufthansa">Lufthansa</a>, is located in <a href="/wiki/Kelsterbach" title="Kelsterbach">Kelsterbach</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/LSG_Sky_Chefs" title="LSG Sky Chefs">LSG Sky Chefs</a>, another subsidiary of <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa" title="Lufthansa">Lufthansa</a>, is located in <a href="/wiki/Neu-Isenburg" title="Neu-Isenburg">Neu-Isenburg</a>.</p>
<p>The German headquarters of <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Cook_Group" title="Thomas Cook Group">Thomas Cook Group</a> are based in <a href="/wiki/Oberursel_(Taunus)" title="Oberursel (Taunus)">Oberursel</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Langen,_Hesse" title="Langen, Hesse">Langen</a> is home to <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Flugsicherung" title="Deutsche Flugsicherung">Deutsche Flugsicherung</a>, the German <a href="/wiki/Air_traffic_control" title="Air traffic control">air traffic control</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Quality_of_life">Quality of life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=82" title="Edit section: Quality of life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:A5_with_Frankfurt_airport_on_the_horizon_-_Autobahn_A5_mit_Flughafen_Frankfurt_am_Horizont_-_02.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Rush hour on Autobahn 5</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>According to a ranking list (2001) produced by the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Liverpool" title="University of Liverpool">University of Liverpool</a>, Frankfurt is the richest city in Europe by <a href="/wiki/GDP_per_capita" class="mw-redirect" title="GDP per capita">GDP per capita</a>, followed by <a href="/wiki/Karlsruhe" title="Karlsruhe">Karlsruhe</a>, Paris and <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<p>Frankfurt was voted the 7th in the <a href="/wiki/World%27s_most_livable_cities" class="mw-redirect" title="World's most livable cities">Mercer Quality of Living Survey</a> by the Mercer Quality of Living Survey (2012),<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> seventh in the Mercer Quality of Living Survey (2010) and 18th at the <a href="/wiki/Economist_Intelligence_Unit" title="Economist Intelligence Unit">Economist's</a> World's Most Liveable Cities Survey (2011).<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> According to an annual citizen survey (2010), arranged by the city council, 66 percent inhabitants are satisfied or highly satisfied with the city, while only 6 percent said that they are dissatisfied. Compared to the 1993's survey the number of satisfied inhabitants has grown about 22 percent while the number of dissatisfied inhabitants was reduced by 8 percent. 84 percent of the inhabitants like to live in Frankfurt, 13 percent would rather choose to live somewhere else. 37 percent are satisfied with the public safety (1993: only 9 percent), 22 percent are dissatisfied (1993: 64 percent).<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<p>Frankfurt consistently has the highest levels of crime per 100,000 inhabitants in Germany (15.976 crimes per annum in 2008) and is therefore dubbed the German "crime capital".<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> However, this statistic is often criticized<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> because it ignores major factors: It is calculated based on the administrative 680,000-inhabitant figure while the urban area has 2.5 M inhabitants and on weekdays adds another million people<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> (not counting the 53 million passengers passing through the airport each year). The rate for personal safety-relevant crimes such as murder, manslaughter, rape or bodily harm, is 3.4 percent, placing Frankfurt twelfth in the ranking (related to the official 680,000-inhabitant figure) or number 21 (related to the one-million-figure).<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Governmental_institutions">Governmental institutions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=83" title="Edit section: Governmental institutions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Insurance_and_Occupational_Pensions_Authority">European Insurance and Occupational Pensions Authority</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=84" title="Edit section: European Insurance and Occupational Pensions Authority">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/European_Insurance_and_Occupational_Pensions_Authority" title="European Insurance and Occupational Pensions Authority">European Insurance and Occupational Pensions Authority</a> (EIOPA) is an institution of the European Union and part of the <a href="/wiki/European_System_of_Financial_Supervisors" class="mw-redirect" title="European System of Financial Supervisors">European System of Financial Supervisors</a> that was created in response to the <a href="/wiki/Late-2000s_financial_crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="Late-2000s financial crisis">financial crisis</a>. It was established on 1 January 2011.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Federal_Financial_Supervisory_Authority">Federal Financial Supervisory Authority</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=85" title="Edit section: Federal Financial Supervisory Authority">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Frankfurt is one of two locations of the German <a href="/wiki/Federal_Financial_Supervisory_Authority" title="Federal Financial Supervisory Authority">Federal Financial Supervisory Authority</a> (<i>Bundesanstalt für Finanzdienstleistungsaufsicht</i>, short: <i>BaFin</i>). The BaFin is an independent federal institution and acts as Germany's <a href="/wiki/Financial_regulation" title="Financial regulation">financial regulatory</a> authority.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_Finance_Corporation">International Finance Corporation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=86" title="Edit section: International Finance Corporation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Frankfurt is home to the German office of the <a href="/wiki/International_Finance_Corporation" title="International Finance Corporation">International Finance Corporation</a> (IFC), which is part of the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> Group. The IFC promotes sustainable private sector investment in <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">developing countries</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="German_National_Library">German National Library</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=87" title="Edit section: German National Library">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Frankfurt is one of two sites of the <a href="/wiki/German_National_Library" title="German National Library">German National Library</a> (<i>Deutsche Nationalbibliothek</i>), the other being <a href="/wiki/Leipzig" title="Leipzig">Leipzig</a>. The Deutsche Nationalbibliothek is the largest <a href="/wiki/Universal_library" title="Universal library">universal library</a> in Germany. Its task, unique in Germany, is to collect, permanently archive, comprehensively document and record bibliographically all German and German-language publications from 1913 on, foreign publications about Germany, translations of German works and the works of German-speaking emigrants published abroad between 1933 and 1945, and to make them available to the public.</p>

Main Forum, home to <a href="/wiki/IG_Metall" title="IG Metall">IG Metall</a></div>

<p>Frankfurt is home to multiple trade unions and associations, including:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/IG_Metall" title="IG Metall">IG Metall</a>, Germany's largest <a href="/wiki/Metalworking" title="Metalworking">metalworkers</a> trade union, based at the Main Forum high-rise building in the <a href="/wiki/Gutleutviertel_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" class="mw-redirect" title="Gutleutviertel (Frankfurt am Main)">Gutleutviertel</a> district</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/IG_Bauen-Agrar-Umwelt" title="IG Bauen-Agrar-Umwelt">IG Bauen-Agrar-Umwelt</a>, a union for <a href="/wiki/Construction_worker" title="Construction worker">construction</a> and engineering workers,</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Education_and_Science_Workers%27_Union_(Germany)" title="Education and Science Workers' Union (Germany)">Gewerkschaft Erziehung und Wissenschaft</a>, a union for teachers</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gewerkschaft_Deutscher_Lokomotivf%C3%BChrer" title="Gewerkschaft Deutscher Lokomotivführer">Gewerkschaft Deutscher Lokomotivführer</a>, a union for <a href="/wiki/Railroad_engineer" title="Railroad engineer">train drivers</a></li>
</ul>
<p><a href="/wiki/Trade_association" title="Trade association">trade associations</a> include:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Verband_der_Elektrotechnik,_Elektronik_und_Informationstechnik" title="Verband der Elektrotechnik, Elektronik und Informationstechnik">Verband der Elektrotechnik, Elektronik und Informationstechnik</a> (Electrotechnical, Electronic and Information Technology Association)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/DECHEMA" title="DECHEMA">DECHEMA Gesellschaft für Chemische Technik und Biotechnologie</a> (Applied Chemistry and Biotechnology Association)</li>
<li>Börsenverein des Deutschen Buchhandels (German Booksellers Association), which organises the <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Book_Fair" title="Frankfurt Book Fair">Frankfurt Book Fair</a></li>
<li>Bundesverband des Deutschen Versandhandels (German Catalogue Selling Association)</li>
<li>Verband der Chemischen Industrie (Chemical Industry Association)</li>
<li>Verband der Photoindustrie (Photography Industry Association)</li>
<li>Verband Deutscher Maschinen- und Anlagenbau (German Machine and Equipment Building Association)</li>
<li>Verband der Köche Deutschlands (German Cooks Association)</li>
</ul>

<p>Frankfurt is one of Germany's leading tourist destinations. In addition to its infrastructure and economy, its diversity supports a vibrant cultural scene. This blend of attractions led 4.3&#160;million tourists (2012) to visit Frankfurt.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> The Hotels in central Frankfurt offer 34,000 beds in 228 hotels, of which 13 are luxury hotels and 46 are first-class hotels.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>

<p>Besides the tourist attractions in central Frankfurt many internationally famous sites are within 80&#160;km (50&#160;mi) of the city, such as:</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="North">North</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=92" title="Edit section: North">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Taunus" title="Taunus">Taunus mountain range</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Saalburg" title="Saalburg">Roman Empire Army Camp Saalburg</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Limes" title="Limes">Limes</a> (former northern border of the Roman Empire)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bad_Homburg_vor_der_H%C3%B6he" title="Bad Homburg vor der Höhe">Bad Homburg vor der Höhe</a> with its famous <a href="/wiki/Casino" title="Casino">casino</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bad_Nauheim" title="Bad Nauheim">Bad Nauheim</a> <a href="/wiki/Elvis_Presley" title="Elvis Presley">Elvis Presley</a> memorial</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hessenpark" title="Hessenpark">Hessenpark</a></li>
</ul>
