<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Frankfurt,_Zeppelinallee_43,_griechisches_Generalkonsulat.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Frankfurt%2C_Zeppelinallee_43%2C_griechisches_Generalkonsulat.JPG/220px-Frankfurt%2C_Zeppelinallee_43%2C_griechisches_Generalkonsulat.JPG" width="220" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Frankfurt%2C_Zeppelinallee_43%2C_griechisches_Generalkonsulat.JPG/330px-Frankfurt%2C_Zeppelinallee_43%2C_griechisches_Generalkonsulat.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Frankfurt%2C_Zeppelinallee_43%2C_griechisches_Generalkonsulat.JPG/440px-Frankfurt%2C_Zeppelinallee_43%2C_griechisches_Generalkonsulat.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2505" data-file-height="1812" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Frankfurt,_Zeppelinallee_43,_griechisches_Generalkonsulat.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Greek consulate</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As a profoundly international city, Frankfurt hosts 92 diplomatic missions (consulates and <a href="/wiki/Consulate-_general" class="mw-redirect" title="Consulate- general">consulates-general</a>). Worldwide, only New York City and <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a> are non-capital cities with more foreign representation. The <a href="/wiki/Consulate_General_of_the_United_States_in_Frankfurt" class="mw-redirect" title="Consulate General of the United States in Frankfurt">Consulate General of the United States</a> in <a href="/wiki/Eckenheim_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" class="mw-redirect" title="Eckenheim (Frankfurt am Main)">Eckenheim</a> is the largest American consulate in the world.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Courts">Courts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=97" title="Edit section: Courts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Several courts are located in Frankfurt, including:</p>
<ul>
<li><b>Hessisches Landesarbeitsgericht</b> (Hessian State Employment Court)<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></li>
<li><b>Oberlandesgericht Frankfurt</b> (Higher Regional Court Frankfurt)<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></li>
<li><b>Landgericht Frankfurt</b> (Regional Court Frankfurt)<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></li>
<li><b>Amtsgericht Frankfurt</b> (Local Court Frankfurt)<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></li>
<li><b>Sozialgericht Frankfurt</b> (Social Court Frankfurt)<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></li>
<li><b>Arbeitsgericht Frankfurt</b> (Employment Court Frankfurt)<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></li>
<li><b>Verwaltungsgericht Frankfurt</b> (Administration Court Frankfurt)<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=98" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Newspapers">Newspapers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=99" title="Edit section: Newspapers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Two important daily newspapers are published. The conservative <i><a href="/wiki/Frankfurter_Allgemeine_Zeitung" title="Frankfurter Allgemeine Zeitung">Frankfurter Allgemeine Zeitung</a></i>, also known as <i>FAZ</i>, was founded in 1949 and is the German newspaper with the widest circulation outside of Germany, with its editors claiming to deliver the newspaper to 148 countries every day. The FAZ has a circulation of over 380,000 copies daily. The other important newspaper, the <i><a href="/wiki/Frankfurter_Rundschau" title="Frankfurter Rundschau">Frankfurter Rundschau</a></i>, was first published in 1945 and has a daily circulation of over 181,000.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Magazines">Magazines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=100" title="Edit section: Magazines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Several magazines also originate from Frankfurt. The local <i>Journal Frankfurt</i> is the best-known magazine for events, parties, and "insider tips". <i>Öko-Test</i> is a consumer-oriented magazine that focuses on ecological topics. <a href="/wiki/Titanic_(magazine)" title="Titanic (magazine)"><i>Titanic</i></a> is a well-known and often criticized <a href="/wiki/Satire" title="Satire">satirical</a> magazine with a circulation of approximately 100,000.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Radio_and_TV">Radio and TV</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=101" title="Edit section: Radio and TV">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Frankfurt's first radio station was the Südwestdeutsche Rundfunkdienst AG (Southwest German Broadcast Service), founded in 1924. Its successor service is the public broadcaster <a href="/wiki/Hessischer_Rundfunk" title="Hessischer Rundfunk">Hessischer Rundfunk</a> (Hessian Broadcast Service). It is located at the "Funkhaus am Dornbusch" in the <a href="/wiki/Dornbusch_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Dornbusch (Frankfurt am Main)">Dornbusch</a> district and is one of the most important radio and television <a href="/wiki/Broadcasting" title="Broadcasting">broadcasters</a> in Hesse, with additional studios in <a href="/wiki/Kassel" title="Kassel">Kassel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Darmstadt" title="Darmstadt">Darmstadt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fulda" title="Fulda">Fulda</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Bloomberg_TV" class="mw-redirect" title="Bloomberg TV">Bloomberg TV</a> and <a href="/wiki/RTL_Television" title="RTL Television">RTL Television</a> have regional studios.</p>
<p>Other radio broadcasters include Main FM and Radio X.</p>
<p>From August 1945 to October 2004, the <a href="/wiki/American_Forces_Network" title="American Forces Network">American Forces Network</a> (AFN) had broadcast from Frankfurt. Due to troop reductions the AFN's location has been closed with AFN now broadcasting from <a href="/wiki/Mannheim" title="Mannheim">Mannheim</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="News_agency">News agency</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=102" title="Edit section: News agency">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Frankfurt is home to the German office of <a href="/wiki/Reuters" title="Reuters">Reuters</a>, the global <a href="/wiki/News_agency" title="News agency">news agency</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education_and_research">Education and research</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=103" title="Edit section: Education and research">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Frankfurt hosts two universities and several specialist schools. The two business schools are <a href="/wiki/Goethe_University_Frankfurt" title="Goethe University Frankfurt">Goethe University Frankfurt</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Goethe_Business_School" title="Goethe Business School">Goethe Business School</a> and <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_School_of_Finance_%26_Management" title="Frankfurt School of Finance &amp; Management">Frankfurt School of Finance &amp; Management</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Johann_Wolfgang_Goethe_University">Johann Wolfgang Goethe University</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=104" title="Edit section: Johann Wolfgang Goethe University">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The oldest and best-known university is the <a href="/wiki/Johann_Wolfgang_Goethe_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Johann Wolfgang Goethe University">Johann Wolfgang Goethe University</a>, with locations in Bockenheim, Westend, and Riedberg, and the university hospital in Niederrad. <a href="/wiki/Goethe_Business_School" title="Goethe Business School">Goethe Business School</a> is part of the University's <a href="/wiki/House_of_Finance" title="House of Finance">House of Finance</a> at Campus Westend. The Business School's Full Time MBA program has over 70% international students.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Frankfurt_University_of_Applied_Sciences">Frankfurt University of Applied Sciences</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=105" title="Edit section: Frankfurt University of Applied Sciences">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_University_of_Applied_Sciences" title="Frankfurt University of Applied Sciences">Frankfurt University of Applied Sciences</a> was created out of several older organisations in 1971, and offers over 38 study areas, in the arts, sciences, engineering and law. Some of the most important research projects: Planet Earth Simulator, <a href="/wiki/FraLine" title="FraLine">FraLine</a>-IT-School-Service, quantitative analysis of <a href="/wiki/Methane" title="Methane">methane</a> in human corpses with the help of a mass spectrometer, software engineering (e.g., fraDesk), analysis of qualitative and quantitative gas in human lungs, long-term studies on <a href="/wiki/Photovoltaic" class="mw-redirect" title="Photovoltaic">photovoltaic</a> modules (to name only a few).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Frankfurt_School_of_Finance_and_Management">Frankfurt School of Finance and Management</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=106" title="Edit section: Frankfurt School of Finance and Management">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Alongside the university is the banking academy <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_School_of_Finance_%26_Management" title="Frankfurt School of Finance &amp; Management">Frankfurt School of Finance &amp; Management</a>, formerly known as the <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Hochschule für Bankwirtschaft</span></i> (Institution of Higher Learning for Banking Economics), with its new campus near Deutsche Nationalbibliothek U-Bahn stop (recently moving from its previous location in the Ostend (Eastend) neighbourhood). In 2001, it became a specialist institution for Economics and Management, or FOM.</p>
<h3><span id="Städelschule"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="St.C3.A4delschule">Städelschule</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=107" title="Edit section: Städelschule">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Frankfurt has the State Institution of Higher Learning for Artistic Education known as the <a href="/wiki/St%C3%A4delschule" title="Städelschule">Städelschule</a>, founded in 1817 by Johann Friedrich <a href="/wiki/St%C3%A4del" class="mw-redirect" title="Städel">Städel</a>. It was taken over by the city in 1942 and turned into a state art school.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_schools_and_conservatory">Music schools and conservatory</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=108" title="Edit section: Music schools and conservatory">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Music institutions are the <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_University_of_Music_and_Performing_Arts" title="Frankfurt University of Music and Performing Arts">Frankfurt University of Music and Performing Arts</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Hoch_Conservatory" title="Hoch Conservatory">Hoch Conservatory</a> (Dr. Hoch's Konservatorium) which was founded in 1878. The International <a href="/wiki/Ensemble_Modern" title="Ensemble Modern">Ensemble Modern</a> Academy is a significant institution for the study of contemporary music.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_notable_schools">Other notable schools</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=109" title="Edit section: Other notable schools">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">

<td class="mbox-image">

<p>The <a href="/wiki/Sankt_Georgen_Graduate_School_of_Philosophy_and_Theology" title="Sankt Georgen Graduate School of Philosophy and Theology">Sankt Georgen Graduate School of Philosophy and Theology</a> (German:<i>Philosophisch-Theologische Hochschule Sankt Georgen</i>), a private institution with membership in the German Jesuit Association, has been located in <a href="/wiki/Sachsenhausen_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Sachsenhausen (Frankfurt am Main)">Sachsenhausen</a> since 1950.</p>
<p>The city is home to three <a href="/wiki/Max_Planck_Society" title="Max Planck Society">Max Planck Society</a> institutes: the <a href="/wiki/Max_Planck_Institute_for_European_History_of_Law" class="mw-redirect" title="Max Planck Institute for European History of Law">Max Planck Institute for European History of Law</a> (MPIeR), <a href="/wiki/Max_Planck_Institute_for_Biophysics" class="mw-redirect" title="Max Planck Institute for Biophysics">Max Planck Institute for Biophysics</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Max_Planck_Institute_for_Brain_Research" title="Max Planck Institute for Brain Research">Max Planck Institute for Brain Research</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Institute_for_Advanced_Studies" title="Frankfurt Institute for Advanced Studies">Frankfurt Institute for Advanced Studies</a>, sponsored by several institutional and private sources, is involved in theoretical research in physics, chemistry, neuroscience, and computer science.</p>
<p>Frankfurt is host to the <i>Römisch-Germanische-Kommission</i> (RGK), the <a href="/wiki/German_Archaeological_Institute" title="German Archaeological Institute">German Archaeological Institute</a> branch for <a href="/wiki/Prehistory" title="Prehistory">prehistoric archaeology</a> in Germany and Europe. The RGK is involved in a variety of research projects. Its library, with over 130,000 volumes, is one of the largest specialised archaeological libraries in the world.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Education_and_media">Education and media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=110" title="Edit section: Education and media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>

<p>Frankfurt schools rank among the best equipped schools nationwide for availability of PCs and other media facilities. In order to assure maintenance and support of the school PCs, the city in cooperation with the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Applied_Sciences_Giessen-Friedberg" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Applied Sciences Giessen-Friedberg">University of Applied Sciences</a> launched the project <a href="/wiki/Fraline" class="mw-redirect" title="Fraline">Fraline</a> – IT-Schul-Service, an initiative employing students to provide basic school IT-support.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=111" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div>

<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. </table>
<p>Frankfurt is home to several professional sports teams. Some of them have won German Championships. E.g. the <a href="/wiki/Skyliners_Frankfurt" title="Skyliners Frankfurt">Skyliners Frankfurt</a> won the <a href="/wiki/German_Basketball_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="German Basketball Championship">German Basketball Championship</a> in 2004 and the <a href="/wiki/German_Basketball_Cup" title="German Basketball Cup">German Cup</a> in 2000. Women's side <a href="/wiki/1._FFC_Frankfurt" title="1. FFC Frankfurt">1. FFC Frankfurt</a> are Germany's record title holders; <a href="/wiki/Eintracht_Frankfurt" title="Eintracht Frankfurt">Eintracht Frankfurt</a> are one-time German champions, four-times winners of the <a href="/wiki/DFB-Pokal" title="DFB-Pokal">DFB-Pokal</a>, and winners of the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="UEFA Cup">UEFA Cup</a> in 1980. Frankfurt hosts the following sports teams or clubs:</p>
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 22em; -webkit-column-width: 22em; column-width: 22em;">
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/1._FFC_Frankfurt" title="1. FFC Frankfurt">1. FFC Frankfurt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> (women)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Eintracht_Frankfurt" title="Eintracht Frankfurt">Eintracht Frankfurt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> (men)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/FSV_Frankfurt" title="FSV Frankfurt">FSV Frankfurt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> (men)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rot-Weiss_Frankfurt" title="Rot-Weiss Frankfurt">Rot-Weiss Frankfurt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Frankfurter_FC_Germania_1894" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankfurter FC Germania 1894">Frankfurter FC Germania 1894</a>, <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Skyliners_Frankfurt" title="Skyliners Frankfurt">Skyliners Frankfurt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">Basketball</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Galaxy" title="Frankfurt Galaxy">Frankfurt Galaxy</a> (1991–2007), <a href="/wiki/WLAF" title="WLAF">American football</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Universe" title="Frankfurt Universe">Frankfurt Universe</a>, <a href="/wiki/GFL" class="mw-redirect" title="GFL">American football</a></li>
<li>Frankfurt Pirates, <a href="/wiki/GFL" class="mw-redirect" title="GFL">American football</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Sarsfields_GAA" title="Frankfurt Sarsfields GAA">Frankfurt Sarsfields GAA</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gaelic_football" title="Gaelic football">Gaelic football</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Lions" title="Frankfurt Lions">Frankfurt Lions</a> (until 2010), <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">Ice hockey</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/L%C3%B6wen_Frankfurt" title="Löwen Frankfurt">Löwen Frankfurt</a> (since 2010), <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">Ice hockey</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/SC_1880_Frankfurt" title="SC 1880 Frankfurt">SC 1880 Frankfurt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">Rugby union</a></li>
</ul>
</div>
<p>Frankfurt is host to the <a href="/wiki/Classic_cycle_races" title="Classic cycle races">classic cycle</a> race <a href="/wiki/Eschborn-Frankfurt_City_Loop" class="mw-redirect" title="Eschborn-Frankfurt City Loop">Eschborn-Frankfurt City Loop</a> (known as <i>Rund um den Henninger-Turm</i> from 1961 to 2008). The city hosts also the annual <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Marathon" title="Frankfurt Marathon">Frankfurt Marathon</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ironman_Germany" title="Ironman Germany">Ironman Germany</a>. In addition to the former, it is one of 13 global host locations to the J.P. Morgan Corporate Challenge <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://www.jpmorganchasecc.com/city/frankfurt">[7]</a>, Germany's biggest corporate sports event.</p>
